Current Commentary

The Russo-Japanese Situation After the Transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway 32

According to a Reuters dispatch from Tokyo the day before yesterday, the issue of the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway, which had been under negotiation between Japan and the puppet state in Tokyo for a year and seven months, finally reached a final agreement in principle between the two parties on the morning of the 22nd of this month after 40 rounds of prolonged negotiations. The date for a formal resolution is imminent, so its success is already a confirmed fact. Today, as we recall the course of these sales negotiations, the interactions between the two sides have been sometimes tense and sometimes relaxed, demonstrating the utmost in confusing maneuvers, making it truly impossible for people to discern the superiority of their tactics or who would ultimately prevail. However, judging from the terms of the agreement that have now been reached, Japan and the puppet state cannot immediately regard it as an absolute victory. Although the puppet state must pay a price of 140 million yen, the Russian side receives no more than 50 million yen in cash. Superficially, it seems that Russia is not coming out ahead. However, it is also manifestly clear that the Chinese Eastern Railway today no longer possesses the economic value it once did. Therefore, we cannot judge the reason for the final agreement of this negotiation solely in terms of the interests of the Chinese Eastern Railway itself, but rather we must seek its significance in the impact it will have on the international diplomatic stage.

Since the Chinese Eastern Railway has been jointly operated by Russia and our country, disputes have arisen from time to time. However, in terms of the past relationship between China and Russia regarding the railway, it was originally jointly owned. Now, Russia has suddenly made this transaction with Japan and the puppet state. From the perspective of our country's position, we naturally cannot agree to this kind of sale, and we must solemnly express this to maintain our consistent policy of "non-recognition." However, the land of the four northeastern provinces has already been forcibly occupied, so what leisure do we have to inquire about the transfer of this mere railway right? Empty arguments will not remedy the reality. Therefore, what we must clearly recognize today regarding this issue is the significance of the establishment of this negotiation for the overall situation of peace in the Far East.

I have often discussed that Russia and Japan are originally places where the forces of the two countries come into contact in the Northeast. Since the September 18th Incident has already occurred, Japan's economic power has been expanding daily, and Russia cannot but relinquish its interests in the Chinese Eastern Railway. However, will Russia also be willing to concede its other military plans along with it? Does Japan have other further hopes beyond the economic benefits of the Chinese Eastern Railway? This is truly the most important question. Yesterday, the Russian Pravda commented on the Japanese government's efforts to resolve outstanding issues between Japan and Russia, saying, "It is astonishing that the Japanese Foreign Minister actually believes that Soviet Russia intends to relax its Far Eastern border defenses. It would be absurd to regard the Russian government's plans in the Far East as offensive rather than defensive." It can be seen that the hearts of both parties are still filled with suspicion regarding various military and political matters and have not shown the slightest sign of being dispelled. Moreover, according to recent telegrams, puppet troops from Heilongjiang suddenly clashed with Russian troops from Outer Mongolia again. A Hualian News Agency dispatch stated that Russian troops from Outer Mongolia occupied fishing grounds near Lake Baikal and also occupied the triangular area where the three rivers north of the lake converge, resulting in a clash with Japanese and puppet troops. The puppet troops suffered heavy casualties. Now, Japanese and puppet reinforcements have arrived and are engaged in fierce fighting. However, the Russian side's explanation is not yet clear. According to Reuters' speculation, it is questionable whether this matter will develop seriously. If Outer Mongolia sends troops to assist, the Japanese army will inevitably intervene, and the scope may not be guaranteed not to expand. Therefore, it is very difficult to predict the future of this conflict between Japan and the puppet state and Russian troops. The transaction between Japan and the puppet state and Russia for the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway has only been completed for three or four days. The general public all believe that the relationship between Japan and Russia may gradually improve from now on. However, the conflict over the fishing pond occurred immediately afterward. Although it may only be a minor incident on the border, and the authorities on both sides may not be willing to expand it, it can also be seen that disputes can arise between Japan and Russia at any time, and spark a war at any time. Therefore, it may not be a profound understanding of the Far Eastern situation to say that just based on the agreement on the Chinese Eastern Railway, it is beneficial to the overall situation of peace in the Far East.

Death of Kubyshev, Deputy Chairman of the Russian People's Committee 46

Another Leader of the Government Weakened

Issuing Obituary 47

(Moscow) Upon Kubyshev's death, Stalin, Molotov, Voroshilov, Kaganovich, Kalinin, Ordzhonikidze, and other party and government leaders issued the following obituary: "Today, one of the most important leaders in the party, our outstanding comrade and close friend, has passed away. The party has suffered a great loss. Kubyshev worked tirelessly, analyzed meticulously, and dedicated his entire life to the proletarian revolution. Kubyshev was truly an outstanding Bolshevik politician. Kubyshev served as Chairman of the Central Control Commission and Chairman of the Workers' and Peasants' Inspection Commission, which was reorganized in accordance with Lenin's instructions. He carried out his struggle with steadfast and indomitable spirit against all incorrect tendencies that deviated from the party's general line. When he served as Deputy Chairman of the Soviet People's Committee, his rich experience in organizing economic work and his national vision were particularly evident. Kubyshev fought hard while he still had a breath, and now he has died on his front line. Kubyshev's life and his entire person have worked for the benefit of the working class and our heroic people." (Moscow) The government has established a committee to prepare for Kubyshev's funeral, with Kubaev, Yenukidze, Antipov, and Filatov as members. Kubyshev's remains are temporarily placed in the Trade Union Hall today, allowing the public to pay their last respects. The remains will be cremated early tomorrow morning, and the ashes will be placed in the Trade Union Hall on the 27th of this month. The funeral will be held in Red Square that afternoon. (25th Tass Dispatch)

Kubyshev's brief history Kubyshev was born in Omsk in 1888. In 1904, he joined the Bolshevik Party. He actively participated in party and revolutionary work in various towns in Siberia. He later went to St. Petersburg and was arrested and exiled four times. During the February Revolution in 1917, he was being exiled in a village in Siberia. Later, Kubyshev led the October Revolution in Samara and fought against Kolchak on the Eastern and Turkestan Fronts as a member of the Revolutionary Military Committee. At the 11th Party Congress in 1922, Kubyshev was elected as a member of the Central Control Commission of the Party. From 1922 to 1923, he served as one of the secretaries of the Central Committee. After 1926, he served as Chairman of the Supreme Economic Council and member of the Political Bureau of the Central Committee. From 1930, he served as Chairman of the State Planning Commission, Deputy Chairman of the Soviet People's Committee, and Deputy Chairman of the Labor and Defense Council. After the 17th Party Congress in 1934, he served as Chairman of the Soviet Supervisory Committee, Deputy Chairman of the People's Committee, and Deputy Chairman of the Labor and Defense Committee. Kubyshev was the most active participant in organizing and participating in the October Revolution and the Civil War, the most important organizer of planned economy, and a leader in the socialist construction of the Soviet Union. (Tass)

Meeting of the International Labor Organization Governing Body 49

Scheduled to Be Convened on the 29th of This Month

The United States Sends Wilson as Representative

(Geneva) The Governing Body of the International Labor Office is scheduled to meet on January 29 to re-elect the eight most industrialized countries to serve as permanent members of the Governing Body. The current eight major countries that serve as permanent members of the International Labor Office are, in alphabetical order: Germany, Belgium, Canada, France, Great Britain, India, Italy, and Japan. However, the United States and the Soviet Union are both major industrial countries and have recently joined the International Labor Office, so the list of the eight major industrial countries serving as permanent members must be revised.

(Geneva) Wilson, the US Consul in Geneva, recently notified the Director of the International Labor Office that the United States has accepted the dispatch of representatives to attend the meeting of the Governing Body of the International Labor Office on January 29, and has appointed Rubin, a statistician from the US Department of Labor, as the US representative. The Rome Agreement Between France and Italy Signed: 51

｜Laval Reports to the House Committee｜

The Colonial Problem of Africa Resolved

Promoting Peace and Cooperation Between the Two Countries

Naval Issues Not Involved

(Paris) Foreign Minister Laval reported today at a joint meeting of the House Foreign Affairs, Navy, and Colonies Committees on the contents of the Franco-Italian Rome Agreement and the process of its signing. He stated that Italian nationals in the French protectorate of Tunisia in Africa have enjoyed special privileges for 39 years, and fortunately, this problem has been resolved. This could not have been achieved without face-to-face meetings with Italian leader Mussolini and sincere communication. Although Italy is allowed to purchase some shares in the railway from French Djibouti to the capital of Abyssinia, France still holds the majority of the shares, and its management rights belong to France, so there is no problem. Italy's request to change the borders of its African territories was based on the 1915 Treaty of London. Now France has fulfilled its promise to incorporate part of the French territory south of Libya into Italian territory, which has been recognized by Italy, and this case can be concluded. As for the land along the coast of French Somaliland that is assigned to Italy, it faces the island of Doumeira, and it is far from the sea route from Europe to the Far East. Therefore, the Habelman-Dibout Strait in between can be opened and become a waterway. Now that the colonial problems between France and Italy have been satisfactorily resolved, France and Italy can cooperate closely to jointly seek peace, which is gratifying. Finally, Laval declared that naval issues were not mentioned in the Rome negotiations, because an atmosphere of mutual trust must first be created before new issues can be raised. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

(Paris) The Senate Foreign Affairs Committee unanimously re-elected Bérenger as Chairman of the Committee. Bérenger delivered a speech, emphasizing that the main tendency of the Senate Foreign Affairs Committee is based on the spirit of vigorous and appropriate French foreign policy, and is based on seeking peace in security. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

Excavating an Undersea Tunnel Under the Strait of Gibraltar 53

A Vast Project to Connect Europe and Africa

Spanish Government Actively Planning

Madrid - The Spanish government has decided to excavate an undersea tunnel under the Strait of Gibraltar to connect Europe and Africa. The excavation of this tunnel has become the most notable issue of the time. Construction of a new type of compressed air box is now underway, equipped with various instruments necessary for undersea exploration, to be used to explore the seabed at a depth of 300 meters. This method can test the seabed for leaks, so that no serious dangers will occur during the excavation of the tunnel. The Strait of Gibraltar tunnel is 32 kilometers long and passes through a depth of 400 meters below the sea surface, so its excavation is very vast. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

Czech German Engineer Assassinated by National Socialist Party 54

New Radio Invention Leaked to the Outside

Germany Determined to Put Him to Death

Prague, Czech Republic - German engineer Follmi, residing here, was assassinated yesterday. The murderer has not been apprehended. According to the investigation, the murderer was originally German and fled to Germany after the assassination. Therefore, the general public believes that it was done by the German National Socialist Party. Today, newspapers are commenting on the case, all expressing indignation, saying that this act is undermining the right to protection that German expatriates should enjoy abroad, and that the incident of German philosophy professor, a Jew named Lesen, who took refuge in Czechoslovakia in August 1933 and was assassinated by the National Socialist Party, has now reoccurred. Some newspapers say that Follmi was the director of the Stuttgart radio station in Germany and recently invented a method of using radio waves to stop the engines of airplanes in the sky. This invention is related to Germany's national defense secrets and is extremely important. Therefore, since Follmi has taken refuge abroad, the National Socialist Party is determined to get him. Others say that Follmi privately set up a radio station in Czechoslovakia and broadcast to Germany, which was known to the German government, so he was put to death. After Follmi was assassinated, the police seized a radio transmitter with a wavelength of 50 meters in his room. The Czechoslovak Post and Telecommunications Department had already discovered the transmitter on November 23 last year and had been searching for it everywhere, but it was only now that it was discovered. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

Central Bank Faction's First Defeat in the US Congress 56

Public Debt Bill Passed by the House of Representatives

Amendment Rejected

(Washington) The inflation faction suffered its first defeat in Congress today. Several amendments to the government bond bill proposed by them have been rejected by the House of Representatives. However, silver faction congressmen are not disappointed by today's developments, because the rejected amendments have no direct relationship with the silver issue. After the House rejected the inflation bill amendments, it passed the public debt bill by a vote of 152 to 30. The proposer was Doughton, Chairman of the Ways and Means Committee. The bill amended the second free public debt bill and authorized the Treasury Department to issue new public debts of $1,525,000,000. The first blow suffered by the inflation faction was the House's rejection of the Taussig amendment by a vote of 90 to 54. The amendment limited the Treasury Department to having collateral equal to three times the currency in circulation. Since the Treasury Department has to issue huge amounts of new public debt to enable the government to get through next year, if the Taussig bill were passed, it would have a very large inflationary effect. (National Telegram, 25th)

US Silver Purchase Statistics 57

(Washington) The Department of Commerce announced statistics today that the amount of silver imported by the United States in the week before January 18 increased sharply compared to the previous week. The silver imported this time was worth $5,097,710, while the previous week it was only worth $1,725,000. In the week before January 11, Hong Kong was the main supplier, but this time there was no supply from Hong Kong. Most of the silver came from the United Kingdom. The silver imported from the United Kingdom this time was worth $4,146,299. Mexico only supplied $132,701 this time, while the previous week it was worth $1,087,000. Observers attach importance to the silver of $348,344 imported from Soviet Russia. Most of the silver is ore and raw silver, which shows that the United States has recognized Soviet Russia as a silver-producing country. According to the figures released by the Department of Commerce, the gold imported this time was worth $11,271,401, while the previous week it was worth $6,293,769. (National Telegram, 25th)

French House of Representatives Passes Bill to Increase New Treasury Bonds 58

Imitating the British to Create a Short-Term Financial Market

Maintaining a Balanced Fiscal Policy

(Paris) The French government will submit a bill to Congress next week to relieve unemployment. According to Premier Flandin in the House of Representatives tonight, the main point of the bill is to provide special unemployment benefits to manufacturers who employ workers, and to advocate reducing working hours. The House of Representatives passed tonight the government's bill to increase the limit for issuing short-term treasury bonds from 100 billion francs to 150 billion francs, allowing the government to issue 50 billion francs of treasury bonds in 1935. When the vote was taken, 450 voted in favor and 122 voted against. According to Premier Flandin, the bill is a great experiment aimed at creating a short-term financial market and imitating the British approach. Flandin strongly criticized those who advocate lowering the value of the currency, saying that the French government intends to maintain its balanced policy. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

American Ship "Mohawk" Sunk by Collision 59

Carrying 163 Passengers

At Least 47 People Killed

Another Tragedy After the Loss of the Morro Castle

(New York) After the Ward Line ship "Mohawk" was sunk by a railroad tug off the coast of New Jersey on Thursday, a total of 116 people were rescued, 31 bodies were recovered, and 16 people are missing. The ship had a total of 163 passengers and crew, so the number of deaths should be 47. Including this one, there have been four accidents involving Ward Line ships recently. The first was the "Morro Castle," which was lost last September, killing more than 100 people. After arriving in New York, the railroad tug "announced that the Mohawk" was operated carelessly, resulting in this disaster. A crew member of the "Mohawk" also said that the ship's engine was out of order and could not be salvaged, resulting in the collision. According to a passenger, after the collision, the crew drove the passengers to gather on deck and distributed life jackets. The ship sank very quickly, so the lifeboats were immediately lowered. The captain stayed on the ship and sank with it. All the rescued people were attacked by severe cold, resulting in several people being frostbitten. Many people jumped into the sea, some of whom were rescued and some of whom drowned. Professor Kellerland led six students on the ship to investigate the relics of Malay culture in Central America, but unfortunately encountered disaster on the way. Kellerland and one student are now among the missing. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

American Cold Wave Gradually Killing, British Gales Howling 60

(London) Scotland and the Midlands were hit by gales today, while the cold wave in the United States has begun to end. Gales are howling throughout the United Kingdom, with speeds reaching 80 miles per hour. The large plane between Paris and London was forced to turn back after taking off, so all flights were suspended for the day. The sun shone through the snow clouds in New York, and the temperature has risen from 27 degrees below freezing to 16 degrees below freezing. However, other places are still suffering from severe cold. Several hundred people in the Mississippi district climbed to the tops of trees due to flooding. They were still perched on them at dawn today, and despite efforts to rescue them, they were unsuccessful. Several telephone poles in the United Kingdom were broken by the wind, causing telephone traffic to be blocked. The British oil tanker Fulfuota, which was damaged by fire in its engine room on Tuesday, is still stranded in the Atlantic Ocean. The weather is still bad and there is no sign of improvement. Vessel inspection stations and mooring points will be set up in the five counties of Fu'an and Ningde to strictly inspect ships, cut off the bandits' waterway transportation, and order people from Eastern Fujian living elsewhere to return home to enrich the countryside and prosper the locality. (26th Special Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) The commencement ceremony for dredging the rivers of the provincial capital was held yesterday at the Water Department. Coastal Pirates of Fujian and Guangdong Rob Merchant Ships 110

The Suzhou Suffered Thousands of Dollars in Losses

Many Crew and Passengers Were Kidnapped

Shantou Correspondence: Recently, coastal pirates have been rampant in Fujian and Guangdong, with merchant ships being robbed more than once. The pirates all land at the junction of Raoping and Zhao'an, gather in the Huanggang, Zhelin, and Dongjie areas, and harass everywhere. Last year, the Suzhou was robbed en route from Huanggang to Shantou, losing over 10,000 yuan. The pirate Mai Hongji, hiding in a small boat in Jingzhou, was captured by the Shantou Public Security Bureau's detective team, escorted to Shantou, and executed by firing squad. On the 16th of this month, the Suzhou, departing from Huanggang and Zhelin for Shantou, was robbed by pirates for the second time and sailed towards the Zhao'an sea area. The Hechang Company, the ship's agent in Shantou, immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau, requesting strict investigation of the pirates to facilitate navigation. The original report stated that on the 16th, the Suzhou departed from Huanggang, passing through Zhelin and Jingzhou, carrying 665 bags of brown sugar and four pieces of tin foil, with a total of over 20 cargo owners and passengers, sailing back to Shantou. At 2:00 PM, when sailing to the Fengshanwei sea area, suddenly six bandits disguised in military uniforms rushed into the wheelhouse, threatening the helmsman to steer the ship towards Zhao'an. They then confined the crew and passengers in the cabin. At around 6:00 PM in the evening, after arriving at the Xia'antou area under the jurisdiction of Zhao'an, several sailboats carrying dozens of bandits, each holding Browning pistols and machine guns, climbed onto the ship to search and rob, transporting the goods to each sailboat. A total of over 200 bags of brown sugar, worth approximately over 3,000 yuan, four pieces of tin foil, worth 500 to 600 yuan, and silver goods and clothes of the crew and passengers were robbed. Seven or eight cargo owners and passengers were kidnapped. The bandits set sail and left at night. This information is specially reported, requesting an order to strictly investigate the stolen goods in order to quell the bandit atmosphere. (22nd)

Page 10

Details of the Japanese and Puppet Troops' Incursion into Eastern Chahar 111

Presenting Unreasonable Demands and Suddenly Starting a War

Bombing Dongzhaizi and Pressing Towards Dushikou

Beijing Correspondence: After months of military deployment, the Japanese and puppet troops in western Rehe first presented unreasonable demands, followed by military action, using airplanes and artillery to bomb Dongzhaizi and pressing towards Guyuan and Dushikou. The detailed situation is recorded as follows:

Japanese Army's Intentions: Young officers in the Japanese army, seeing that the international situation is becoming increasingly dangerous, are actively preparing to realize their ambitions. They are dissatisfied with the gradual approach of the diplomatic faction in their policy towards China, and have criticized it. They convened a so-called leaders' meeting in Dalian, advocating a radical approach. Furthermore, in light of the Soviet Union's increasing troops and arms in Kulun, they believe that the areas east and north of Chahar leading to Kulun are strategically important places that they must compete for. They believe that it is not enough to ensure victory unless they seize these areas and make advance arrangements. For two months, they have been actively preparing in areas such as Dage, Datan, and Duolun in western Rehe in order to intrude. Most recently, they made unreasonable demands privately and informally, but to no avail. In the middle of this month, they again used the pretext that areas such as Changliang, Wuni River, and the North and South Stone Pillars belong to Fengning County in Rehe, declaring that they would not hesitate to take military action, with the intention of seizing important towns outside the Great Wall of Chahar Province as military strongholds. Their aim is that if it can be achieved peacefully, there will be no problem. Otherwise, they will not hesitate to resort to force. All kinds of steps have been planned and are now being gradually implemented.

Details of the Incursion: Since the conflict between the Japanese and puppet troops and local militias in the Changliang area, the situation has suddenly become tense. In order to avoid causing trouble, our representatives Qin Dechun and Yue Kaixian negotiated with Matsui, the Japanese liaison officer stationed in Zhangjiakou, based on reason. However, while the two sides were consulting, the Japanese and puppet troops in western Rehe suddenly intruded into eastern Chahar. The Japanese and puppet troops in the Datan area began to concentrate and move on the evening of the 22nd. Nagami, the commander of the 25th Regiment of the Japanese army stationed in Gubeikou, was ordered to lead about 1,500 infantry and cavalry, carrying artillery and machine guns, to Datan. At dusk, they moved forward, using the highway to transport them extremely quickly. At around 10:00 PM that night, they began firing machine guns at areas such as Longtan Temple and Dongqiaozi, carrying out provocations. Gunfire continued unabated all night on the 22nd. At 4:00 AM on the 23rd, 400 to 500 Japanese infantry and cavalry, carrying four heavy artillery pieces and more than 20 machine guns, launched a fierce attack on Longtan Temple and Dongzhaizi. At 10:30 AM, they fired more than 40 heavy artillery shells at Dongzhaizi and used airplanes to drop bombs. Only local militias were stationed there. As a result of the bombing by airplanes and artillery, more than 40 residents and militiamen were killed or injured, and the houses and villages were reduced to ashes. At noon, the vanguard of the Japanese army attacked the Great Wall line in the Dushikou area. At around 1:00 PM, four Japanese aircraft continuously dropped more than 10 bombs on the Great Wall line in that area. Japanese aircraft were also found reconnaissance over the Great Wall line in Longmensuo and Heihe, but did not drop bombs. Several Japanese aircraft reconnoitered over Zhangyuan City on the morning of the 23rd, but the infantry did not move. Outside Dushikou, the Japanese and puppet troops attacked continuously until 7:00 PM, when they stopped. The front was quiet on the night of the 23rd. At 10:00 AM this morning (the 24th), Japanese aircraft flew to Dushikou again to drop bombs, and the infantry continued to advance. At the same time, Guyuan was also alarmed. The situation at the front is serious. The headquarters of the Japanese and puppet troops attacking Dushikou are located in Datan. In the Dage Town area, there are more than 2,000 troops from the 7th Division of the Japanese army. In addition to artillery and aircraft, the Japanese and puppet troops originally had 20 tanks, and another 20 arrived today (the 24th). In addition to the puppet army of Li Shouxin, there are also more than 1,000 troops from the 7th Division of the Japanese army in the Guyuan area. The Japanese army has launched a war without cause. Our army is still defending the original defense line and has not moved out, maintaining a calm attitude in the hope that the Japanese side will realize their mistake.

Details of the Negotiations: After the Japanese side made unreasonable demands privately and informally regarding the Chahar incident but to no avail, they remained silent for several days. Since the conflict between the Japanese and puppet troops and the militias in the Changliang area, both sides believed that local negotiations should be held. They dispatched personnel to investigate. At the same time, Takahashi, the military attache of the Japanese embassy, telegraphed the Japanese army stationed in Rehe, stopping the Japanese and puppet troops from advancing. At the same time, Qin Dechun and Bing Kaixian began to contact Matsui, the Japanese liaison officer stationed in Zhangjiakou, in Zhangjiakou. Matsui, carrying the orders of the Japanese army, proposed that the two sides send representatives to Datan to negotiate. Since the Japanese army launched military operations the day before yesterday, the squadron has repeatedly received telegrams from Zhangjiakou. Yesterday's military branch meeting once raised it for discussion. This morning (the 24th) at 10:00 AM, Song Zheyuan again visited He Yingqin to ask for instructions. Relevant parties have telegraphed the central government to report. Currently, negotiations between the two sides have not been interrupted. The primary goal is to stop the military operations at the front. It is difficult to predict how the future will unfold.

Song Zheyuan's Statement: According to Chahar Chairman Song Zheyuan this morning, yesterday (the 23rd), the Japanese army attacked Dongzhaizi outside Dushikou, stopping at 7:00 PM. According to the investigation, the Japanese army dropped bombs on Dongzhaizi and fired more than 40 artillery shells. More than 40 militiamen and residents were killed or injured. We had no troops stationed in that area and there was no contact. The Japanese side had made unreasonable demands, and I am arguing based on reason. I will stay in Peiping, and the date of returning to Chahar is uncertain.

Takahashi's Statement: This afternoon at 4:00 PM, Takahashi, the military attache of the Japanese embassy, held a tea party for Chinese and foreign reporters. He said that the conflict in eastern Chahar is a local issue and will not affect the overall situation in North China. Negotiations are underway and will be resolved within a few days. (January 24th)

Fang Zhimin and Luo Binghui's Bandit Gang Completely Eliminated 112

Fang et al. Leading Hundreds of Confidants

Disguised Themselves and Fled into the Deep Mountains

Hangzhou Correspondence: The bandit gangs of Fang Zhimin and Luo Binghui, since joining forces and roaming the border areas of Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Anhui, have organized themselves into the 7th and 10th Army Groups, which are divided into the 19th, 20th, and 21st Divisions, with more than 7,000 people and a full array of guns. Chiang Kai-shek telegraphed Yu Jishi, director of the Zhejiang Provincial Security Office, to be responsible for suppression and ordered Wu Chengren's division and the groups of Wang Yaowu and Li Wenbin to be placed under Yu's command. Yu personally led seven regiments and two battalions of the Zhejiang Security Corps to encircle and fiercely attack them. On December 14th of last year, in Taiping County on the Anhui border, they killed Xun Weizhou, the commander of the pseudo 7th Army Group. His body was found in Maolin Village in Jing County, and his head was cut off and displayed in Tunxi. The bandit side suffered heavy losses, and their morale was shattered, determined to flee. After various units pursued them relentlessly, the bandits circled around, passing through southern Anhui and returning to Jiangxi Province. They were repeatedly intercepted and pursued at Fangcun, Jiangcun Liukou, Yicun, Xikou, Dalongshan, and Xujiacun. When they reached the Jiangxi border, the remaining bandits numbered only 2,000. In addition to Xun's death, Luo Shaohua, the military and political commissioner, and Liu Ying, the director of the political department, were both seriously injured. Wang Yizhi, the commander of the pseudo 20th Division, was killed in the Battle of Dalongshan. Wang Ruchun, the commander of the pseudo new 19th Division, was killed in the Battle of Xujiacun. The bandits' corpses have all been found. The bandit suppression forces then surrounded the bandit troops in the eastern territory of Dexing. After days of separate pursuit and interception, the bandits were beheaded, captured, and scattered in greater numbers at Gangtou, Fenshuiguan, Yinzhuang, Huaiyu Mountain, and Baji. Zhou Qun, the director of the protection bureau of the pseudo army group, was captured alive by Wu's division, and thousands of bandits were captured. According to the confession of Zhou Qun, the captured director of the protection bureau of the pseudo army group, the two bandit leaders, Fang and Luo, returned from southern Anhui and planned to pass through western Zhejiang to northern Fujian to contact the red bandits in eastern and northern Fujian, hoping to reorganize. However, they were fiercely attacked head-on by the Zhejiang Security Corps in Xingkou City and Xujiacun and could not flee south to Changshan. They then turned towards the eastern territory of Dexing and fled. Furthermore, because the various armies were pursuing closely, they climbed over the Nanhua Mountain and fled overnight, abandoning many horses and baggage. They were again blocked and attacked by Wu's division and Li's brigade at Gangtou and Fenshuiguan, and Wang's brigade pursued them in Yinzhuang. The military morale was panicked, and the internal collapse led to an irreparable situation. In particular, the two forces in Xingkou and Xujiacun were the key to breaking the bandits' southward escape. Yu himself is still searching for the remaining bandits at the front. The gangs of Fang and Luo have now been completely eliminated. The people in the border areas of Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Anhui can finally rest easy. (25th)

Shanghai Gentlemen Come to Songjiang to Shelter Refugees 113

In the Wangdian and Xiashi areas of Jiahe, Zhejiang Province, there have been years of famine, and farmers have been displaced, flocking to Songjiang to beg for food. The joint establishment of a shelter by Mr. Zhou, a native of the county, and the Shanghai gentlemen, is a unique highlight for the Zhejiang refugees.

A Tragic Murder Occurs in Ganyao Town 116

Zhang Kecai, a resident of Hedongdai in Ganyao Town, from Zhenjiang, runs the Deda bamboo shop, and his life is still considered good. His wife, Chen, is 36 years old, also from Zhenjiang, and has a son. However, she suddenly went missing after dinner the day before yesterday. The next morning, the local police officer A Si suddenly found a female corpse in the field near the Tingzi Bridge, lying in a pool of blood, in an extremely tragic state. The corpse had five or six knife wounds on the head, the nose was cut off, the eyes were gouged out, and all the teeth were knocked out. All the fingers of both hands and both breasts were cut off, and there were deep knife stab wounds in the heart. There were three knife marks on the face, and the flesh was blurred. After the local police reported to Zhang Kecai, he went to inspect and recognized that it was indeed his wife. A loan ticket and five pawn tickets were found on the deceased's body.

Special Report

Enemy or Friend? (Continued) Xu Daolin 117

丨A Review of Sino-Japanese Relations丨

4. China's Mistakes and Miscalculations

Although China cannot bear the same responsibility as Japan for creating such a major incident, looking back from before and after the September 18th Incident to the present day, China cannot be said to be completely without errors in understanding or action that have led to such an intractable stalemate. These errors belong to the government, to the people, and are errors that the government and the people should both acknowledge. They are summarized as follows:

(1) The Error of Missing Opportunities: Before 1930, we heard that the National Government had a tendency to resolve the issue of commercial lease rights. At that time, Japan had not yet signed the customs treaty, and all county cases were still pending. Later, it was said that the issue of commercial lease rights was shelved due to disagreements within the National Government. Originally, Japan was full of doubts and obstacles regarding the National Revolution, and it was no wonder that the Chinese Kuomintang did not arouse favorable feelings towards Japan. However, in international relations, are friends and enemies ever defined by rigid standards? If it benefits the country, one should put aside grievances and do it. Unfortunately, the authorities lacked this courage and missed a good opportunity. Otherwise, the Japanese military faction had not yet risen, and the prestige of political parties had not diminished. The relationship between the two countries might have improved, and the inducement for the September 18th Incident might not have occurred. After the September 18th Incident, public opinion in China was extraordinarily excited, but some people also recognized the crisis and advocated for an early resolution at the right time. For example, Mr. Hu Shih and others advocated resolutely engaging in direct negotiations based on the five principles proposed by Japan, regardless of the cost. However, the authorities ultimately hesitated and insisted on the principle of no negotiations without the withdrawal of troops, which prevented the rise of the Japanese moderate faction and increased the momentum of the military, making the problem more and more rigid. Even when Shenyang had fallen but had not yet invaded Shanhaiguan, there was still a possibility of stopping Japan at Jinzhou to gradually transform the situation. Unfortunately, every step was missed, resulting in an irreparable situation. This cannot but be attributed to the authorities' lack of determination and irresponsibility.

(2) The Error of Not Thoroughly Implementing Revolutionary Strategies: Some people may think that the above statement is too harsh in retrospect. China's hatred towards Japan has deep and widespread roots. Furthermore, with such a sudden and major stimulus, how could the authorities suppress the people's resentment and avoid internal unrest, even if they wanted to compromise for the sake of the country? However, what we are saying is based on the expectation of the Chinese Kuomintang, which has taken on the responsibility of saving the country through revolution. The difference between revolutionary diplomacy and ordinary diplomacy lies in being proactive rather than passive, adaptable rather than rigid, being firm when necessary, flexible when necessary, expanding when possible, and yielding when appropriate, fully implementing unchangeable goals with changing strategies. Historical examples are readily available. Have you not heard of Lenin overcoming public opinion and making peace with Germany? Instead, they were caught in a dilemma, unable to be strong or weak. Looking back at the events since September 18th, even if we do not say that the authorities had no intention of reversing the crisis, we cannot help but believe that they lacked the courage to make decisive decisions. Therefore, we increasingly believe that when the country is in distress, it especially needs great politicians. Now, the Chinese Kuomintang authorities lack both sincerity and wisdom, and the result is that they are trapped in a stalemate where they cannot advance or retreat. Even if we do not call it a betrayal of the country and the people, how can we avoid it?

(3) The Error of Judging the Opponent: After the September 18th Incident, there were many errors in the Chinese people's judgment of the situation in Japan. At that time, the general view was that although China's military strength was not as good as Japan's, the boycott movement could be used as a substitute weapon, so there must be no compromise with Japan. As long as the boycott movement lasted for a year or so, there would be major economic and political disturbances in Japan, and they would have no choice but to abandon the Northeast. However, China would have to expend great effort and endure great pain to consolidate its boycott movement front. At the same time, it did not clearly see the duration of Japan's ability to sustain, as well as the national psychology under its militarist control. This was a major mistake. Furthermore, after September 18th, China still thought that although Japan had caused this great disaster, it still had to consider international resentment and could not completely abandon its responsibility to international treaties. How could it know that Japan, driven by its ambition to dominate the Pacific and unify East Asia, had long regarded international treaties as mere formalities and considered various treaties as chains that restricted the development of its ambitions. It could not be treated as an ordinary country that abides by contracts and keeps its promises. At that time, some people in China even thought that the occupation of the Northeast was only the idea of Japanese warlords, and the enlightened public opinion of the people would be able to restrain the arrogance of the military. Therefore, at that time, Chinese public opinion was still speculating on the rise and fall of the Minseitō and Seiyukai party powers as a standard for response. How could they know that Japan was not an ordinary political party country or a constitutional country, but a special country controlled by a special class of military warlords? This error was completely proven later when Japan withdrew from the League of Nations and Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi was assassinated on May 15th, but it was very popular at the time.

(4) The Error of Examining Self-Reliance: At that time, China not only did not know the enemy's reality, but also did not know its own. It either exaggerated its own strength too much or relied on it too much. It only judged the enemy's weaknesses, and had no time to reflect on or admit its own weaknesses. The general public, aroused by righteous indignation, even believed that short knives could defeat airplanes and that the army, relying solely on non-modern equipment, could participate in modern warfare, shouting for war and urging the dispatch of troops, making it impossible for the government to explain and difficult to respond. This kind of arrogant shout exposed its own weakness of being outwardly strong but inwardly weak, which only strengthened the momentum of the Japanese military. It is regrettable, but in fact, it was not only the people who observed incorrectly, but also the government's judgment of the situation of the enemy and ourselves was contradictory and erroneous. At that time, in the military aspect, when Japan launched an invasion of Rehe, it over-believed that the Northeast Army had considerable defensive strength by taking advantage of the dangerous terrain, believing that Japan would not dare to invade Rehe unless it transported more than six divisions of troops from other countries. It did not know that the spirit and strength of the Northeast Army stationed in Rehe had declined to this point. This was an error in examining self-reliance.

(5) The Error of Observing Third Parties: At that time, China not only lacked a true understanding of both sides, but also could not fully grasp the reality of third parties. At that time, from the government to the people, China always believed that the League of Nations Covenant existed, and Japan was one of the covenant countries. If it blatantly disregarded it, the League would be able to implement economic sanctions in accordance with the covenant. At the same time, it also believed that if friendly mediation by Britain, the United States, or other countries was ineffective, they would also be able to protect the dignity of the covenant or protect world peace and rise up to take forceful intervention. It did not know that Britain and the United States each had their own difficulties, and the Soviet Union was burying itself in preparing for diplomatic and domestic affairs, and obviously could not take positive action. In the autumn of world economic depression, countries became more and more uneasy about the breakdown of peace, and Japan became more and more unscrupulous. Afterwards, the intervention of Britain and the United States was not seen in reality, and the League of Nations made no indication except for a few resolutions, and had no power except for so-called moral sympathy. At that time, this error of judgment has been proven today, three years later.

(6) The Error of Internal Disorder: At that time, China, on the one hand, could not hide its weaknesses due to arrogance, and on the other hand, could not maintain the secrecy of diplomacy. Often, before the government had made a decision, the people had already made a lot of noise, and every move was seen by the world. It was impossible to strengthen its strength in an instant, and there were various restraints on its face, making it impossible to weaken. The more China showed its arrogance, the stronger the momentum of the Japanese warlords became. China was ashamed and resentful of Japan's gradual advance, and could only appeal to the world's justice. The Japanese authorities then used the fact that China trusted the League of Nations and expected Britain and the United States to shout to the Japanese people, "China is using the policy of using barbarians to control barbarians" to stimulate the feelings of the Japanese people, making the views of the enlightened faction more and more declining, and the expansion of the incident was endless. At that time, the Chinese authorities and the people were not consistent internally, the various factions of the people could not be consistent, the Chinese Kuomintang and those outside the party could not be consistent, and even within the Chinese Kuomintang, divisions were revealed due to diplomatic propositions at this time. Therefore, internal turmoil and foreign troubles became more serious. When we look back on the past, we really feel unbearable to finish speaking.

(7) The Error of Acting on Emotions: Many of the various errors in understanding, judgment, and measures mentioned above have become past events, and some are still being followed. There is no need to pursue the various errors that have caused the past situation. What is important is whether we can stop following the mistakes of the past in observing things without careful consideration and making decisions without courage from now on. When we silently observe the country, this can only be regarded as a kind of expectation, and it is still difficult to affirm at present. The author has clearly stated in the previous article that the Sino-Japanese stalemate must be broken. We know that the initiative in the Sino-Japanese issue is entirely in Japan. The first step to break the stalemate must be that Japan has the sincerity of awareness and the expression of giving up the occupation. However, if Japan expresses its desire to start negotiations, China may still have those who cannot agree to direct negotiations. China has suffered unprecedented humiliation and insults, and the excitement of emotions is a matter of course. However, we believe that the method of "mutual destruction" is definitely not a solution. If Japan acts recklessly to the end, China should naturally exert its best efforts to seek struggle. All nationals feel the same way, but "seeking survival in death" is ultimately a method when there is no other way. If it is possible to "seek survival in life," we should suppress emotions and value reason, and plan for the long-term for the country and the nation. If this concept is not liberated, I am afraid that the Sino-Japanese stalemate will still leave some obstacles and cannot be thoroughly broken. If this continues, blindly following and holding on to the stalemate will ultimately not be a blessing for the country and the nation.

5. Japan's Mistakes (1)

...... The Direct Error in Understanding China

When it comes to the reasons for the incident and the inability to break the stalemate to this day, Japan's mistakes are certainly more than China's. Japan's understanding of China first fell into fundamental errors. Based on this fundamental error of understanding, judgments were made and plans were made, resulting in various errors in consideration. At the same time, because of being lost after the incident, the measures taken to respond to the international community also fell into errors. Now, let's first talk about Japan's error in understanding China:

(1) The Error in Understanding China's Current National Situation: I said in my previous article that Japan has no way to eliminate China's existence. The most important reason is that China is currently in a period of revolution. A country in the period of unfinished revolution is completely different from a country that already has a strong and well-defined organization. Japanese people view China, which is in the midst of revolution, as an ordinary country, and Chinese people view Japan, which is a special country under military control, as an ordinary country. Their errors are equal. In an ordinary country with a solid organizational structure, everyone knows that its elements are "land, people, and sovereignty (or government)." However, the historical examples of modern revolutions have shown us that a country in the revolutionary period is completely different from an ordinary country. Its elements are "ideology, leader, and masses." As for the masses, China has a large population, and the urgency of foreign aggression has created many patriotic people with a strong national consciousness. As for ideology, the Three Principles of the People have become a national consensus in China in the past seven or eight years. Chinese people may be dissatisfied with the measures of the Kuomintang authorities, but few oppose the Three Principles of the People. The Chinese intellectual class now generally recognizes that only by urging the Kuomintang to work hard to love itself can China be able to deal with foreign countries. Since September 18th, in fact, China has created a party and its de facto leader that can lead the national people. Therefore, as long as the ideology is widespread and deeply rooted, the leader exists in good health, and the masses support them unanimously, the success or failure of the temporary government or the gain or loss of land becomes a secondary issue. The Chinese National Government now claims to be a temporary revolutionary government, not a government after the completion of the revolution. Therefore, I said in the previous article that occupying the capital of China cannot control China's fate. If it cannot eliminate its leader, then the location of the leader is the location of the Chinese government and the center of national power. The Japanese think that if military actions continue and the territory shrinks, China will not be able to survive. How can they know that a country in the revolutionary period cannot be viewed as an ordinary country? The Chinese Kuomintang once encouraged the people to "consider the lost four northeastern provinces as Siberia before 1920 of Russia." I am not a party member and do not want to judge this statement, but the fact that China is still a country in the revolutionary period is an indisputable fact. From this, if the leader still exists, the Japanese will have no grasp of completely eliminating China. It is only a pity that Japanese China experts are unusually meticulous and thorough in their daily investigations and observations of Chinese affairs, but they neglect this important point.

(2) The Error in Understanding Chinese History and the Times: The Japanese claim to be able to understand Chinese history, believing that China, which is dominated by the Han people, could be destroyed by the Mongols more than 600 years ago, and by the Manchus 300 years ago. Why can't it be ruled by the Japanese today? This is another kind of observational error. Because in the late Song or late Ming Dynasties, Chinese people, except for a few Confucians, almost did not know that there was a change of dynasties, or that a minority ethnic group entered China to rule. However, when the Qing Dynasty was overthrown more than 20 years ago, not only did the revolutionary pioneers rise up and run around, but also a majority of the people participated. The overthrow of the Qing Dynasty was called for by the four slogans of the Tongmenghui: "Expel the Tartars, restore China, establish the Republic, and equalize land rights." The Xinhai Revolution marked a clear period in Chinese history, which was completely different from the previous changes of surnames and generations. Since then, at least the people have understood the meaning of nationalism. As for today, 12 million students in large, medium, and small schools across the country have a deep-rooted national consciousness. In addition, since the late Qing Dynasty, all literate adult nationals, calculated as 10% of the total population, also have 48 million people who know what it means to lose their country. Taking Japan's annexation of Taiwan and Korea as an example, 30 or 40 years ago, perhaps the majority of Chinese nationals did not know what relationship Taiwan and Korea had with China, and therefore did not feel any pain. Today, in many places, even farmers and old people know the fact that the four northeastern provinces have been occupied. This is not any power, this is the result of the changing times. Even if we talk about 60 million people, their number is close to the total population of Japan. Although Japan's military force is strong, it cannot eliminate all 60 million nationals who have a full national consciousness and make all of China obedient to Japan as submissive people. Therefore, inferring today's China by taking the historical examples of the loss of the Song and Ming Dynasties is another kind of error. Furthermore, when the Japanese observe Chinese history, they often only look for China's shortcomings from the bad aspects, and do not study the characteristics of the Chinese nation from the good aspects. The reason why China has been able to rise repeatedly and not be controlled by foreign tribes in the past dynasties is because China has a national spirit of entrusting life in times of crisis and the so-called righteousness between heaven and earth that has been passed down for generations. This spirit and righteousness are often expressed through the moving behavior of loyal ministers and people with lofty ideals in times of crisis and doom, and generations of teachers and Confucian scholars and surviving people write books and advocate, spreading them in songs and dramas, and becoming the main social education of China. This kind of education that is passed down from generation to generation has an unusually deep foundation. Almost Chinese people innately have some of this educational influence in their blood. Even in the main figures of modern China, there are still often quotes from Zhuge Wuhou's "Do your best and die, success or failure, profit or loss, do not look forward to the opposite" and "Cannot be subdued by force, cannot be moved by poverty and humbleness" and other sayings, as maxims for grinding determination. Therefore, the Japanese should not only see the situation when the Song and Ming Dynasties were destroyed, but not see the situation when the Chinese nation rose again in the late Yuan and late Qing Dynasties. They should not only see Qin Hui and Zhang Bangchang of the Song Dynasty, but not see Yue Wumu and Wen Wenshan. They should not only see Hong Chengchou and Wu Sangui of the late Ming Dynasty, but not see Shi Kefa and Zheng Chenggong. In the recent 20 years of the Republic of China era, Japanese general up-and-coming China experts should not only see the actions of warlords such as Yuan Shikai who were imperialistic and selfish, but ignore the sacrificial spirit of revolutionary salvation of Mr. Sun Yat-sen and others. We must know that this spirit and righteousness has always been permeated among the Chinese nation, and with the infusion of modern nationalism, this spirit has been entrusted and developed even greater, so when observing the Chinese nation, we must not represent it with a few shameless warlords and bureaucrats, but believe that it can all be threatened and lured. This level of meaning is really not understood by the Japanese new "China experts," but among the existing teachers and old Confucian scholars in Japan, there are still many old people who know the history of the East and understand the Chinese nation. If you ask them about this meaning, they will definitely allow the author's words to be correct.

(3) The Error in Observing the Chinese Kuomintang: The Japanese side also has two kinds of erroneous views. One is that the Chinese Kuomintang is the center of launching anti-Japanese forces, and the other is that the Sino-Japanese problem cannot be solved unless the Chinese Kuomintang is overthrown, and Japan cannot sleep peacefully. This is another fundamental error. I have explained at the beginning of this article: In China, the most thorough one who talks about the reason that China and Japan are interdependent is Sun Yat-sen, the president of the Kuomintang. In theory, when the National Revolution developed, Japan was the best opportunity to settle the unhappy relations between the two countries in the past and thoroughly renew the national relations. The Kuomintang after 1927 clearly abandoned the policy of tolerating communism, and there was no reason to make Japan afraid. From the analysis of the history of the Kuomintang and its characters, we really cannot see the existence of anti-Japanese elements. To be fair, a party with more than one million members cannot have absolutely consistent actions of its individual members, I am afraid that this is the case in all countries in the world. Accompanied by the deterioration of Sino-Japanese feelings, Kuomintang party members and the general public have the same resentment towards Japan, which is inevitable. However, among the Kuomintang cadres, from Sun Yat-sen to the Japanese ministers, there are not a few who have friendly exchanges and intellectual exchanges. Therefore, in China, the Kuomintang's theory is relatively clear about understanding the key to the survival of East Asia, understanding Japan, and understanding that China and Japan should be equal and work together and should not turn against each other and lose both. Taking recent events as an example, if Japan tries to read the amount of export trade to China before 1931, and then check the amount of trade to China in the years after 1932, and look at the number of their rise and fall, it can be seen that the number of Japanese trade to China shows a gradual recovery trend (the number of Japanese goods exported to China can only be fully expressed from customs statistics), which is a reflection of the policy of the Kuomintang authorities not wanting the relations between the two countries to become more tense. There is now a part of the Chinese people who are deeply dissatisfied with this kind of easing policy of the Kuomintang. I dare to say that if the National Government allows the people to be anti-Japanese, the relations between the two countries will become more tense, not to mention that Japan's economic losses will be incalculable. Therefore, if Japan thinks that the Kuomintang is the center of planning the anti-Japanese movement, it is definitely an error. Secondly, the deterioration of the Chinese people's feelings towards Japan has been caused by Japan itself step by step, and it is by no means the result of the Kuomintang's propaganda and encouragement. If Japan does not automatically improve its policy towards China, but only takes the elimination of the Kuomintang as a means to eliminate the anti-Japanese sentiment, then I dare to represent the general public who are not members of the Chinese Kuomintang and directly recognize that Japan's observation is a fallacy. I don't know if Japan's recent intentions are really like what it says on the surface to eliminate the anti-Japanese and to overthrow the Kuomintang? Or is it determined that the Kuomintang is an obstacle to Japan's absolute domination of China and wants to overthrow the Kuomintang? No matter from which aspect, the Chinese Kuomintang cannot be overthrown by any force within these ten years. Looking at the past, before September 18th, there were still many voices in China against the Kuomintang and Chiang Kai-shek, but since Japan occupied the Northeast, foreign aggression has become deeper and deeper, and the foundation of the Kuomintang has become more and more solid. Now, the remarks and actions against the Kuomintang and Chiang Kai-shek have become less and less. Although the dismemberment and division within the Kuomintang are still deep, the people have expressed their sympathy and love because Japan has tried its best to attack the Kuomintang. Isn't this a very clear example? Moreover, the Chinese Kuomintang can exist in China, and it has its inevitable reasons. In other words, the basis for its existence is not entirely in itself, but rather in the objective situation. It is undeniable that the Kuomintang's internal situation is a mess, and there are many places where its organization and spirit violate the modern style. Even if they compete for their own opinions and harm each other, the internal contradictions are really too numerous to count, but outsiders want to judge their fate by superficial observation, which is not in line with the facts. Looking at the past, since the second year of the Republic of China, the northern warlords have repeatedly borrowed the strongest foreign power to eliminate the Kuomintang, and they have done everything they can. However, the result of each oppression has turned to make the power of the Kuomintang more and more expanded. Even the most sinister third international communist party cannot achieve the goal of eliminating the Kuomintang. After March of the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, Soviet Russia's Borodin even said that he did not see that there was such a strong personality in the Kuomintang. As for today, it cannot be overthrown by any external force. Because the reason why the Kuomintang can still exist today is based on three factors: one is the historical mission, with China's history like this, there must be a Chinese Kuomintang. The second is the mission of the times. In today's world and era, there must be a Kuomintang in China that assumes the mission of the times. The third is the psychology of the people. Because China is in such a situation, national consciousness naturally requires a leading central force and organization. Therefore, the Kuomintang can never be overthrown. Even if it is overthrown, there must be an organization in China that leads the nation to deal with foreign countries. No matter what the Kuomintang's leaders cannot be eliminated. Even if they are eliminated, there must be second and third or even stronger leaders who will rise up in succession. From this inference, if Japan still has this kind of misunderstanding, thinking that it only needs to overthrow the Chinese Kuomintang or attack its leaders to make it decline, then China will have no central force to deal with foreign countries. This is actually the opposite of cause and effect. That is, according to the Japanese, the rule of the Chinese Kuomintang will not be able to withstand the oppression of external forces and collapse. However, the Kuomintang's current predicament is that a revolutionary organization is facing the national crisis head-on and is subject to the political responsibility constraints and restraints, so it reveals its exhaustion and contradiction everywhere. Once it is not in the government position and all the taboos are empty and the actions are free, its external force must be greater than when it is in the government position. Japan must be able to clearly understand what kind of force is spying behind the Chinese Kuomintang, what kind of influence the rise of this kind of force will have on East Asia, and after the Kuomintang is in the opposition position, its more than one million party members and the military force it can control are forced to take any means, and Japan is not difficult to imagine the result. Therefore, if Japan really wants to think about its own interests, this fallacy should be fundamentally corrected. (To be continued)

Selecting Antiquities to Ship to England 122

Currently Inspecting and Verifying as Part of the Handover Procedures from the Previous Administration

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, Chinese antiquities will be exhibited at the Chinese Art Exhibition in London. Since the government approved the British request, a preparatory committee was specially organized to oversee the matter with great care. It was also designated that the antiquities stored in Shanghai at the former Palace Museum serve as the standard for selecting items for exhibition in England. According to Mr. Shu Chushi, a specialist in overseeing the antiquities, the situation is as follows:

Inspection and Selection: The inspection and selection of antiquities are fundamentally two different matters. Recent reports that selection has already taken place are incorrect. The inspection of antiquities is because, since the change of leadership at the Palace Museum, the antiquities have not been handed over to the new director (Ma Heng). The simultaneous inspection in Beijing and Shanghai is the handover inspection. The selection of antiquities is the responsibility of the preparatory committee for the Chinese Art International Exhibition. The selection responsibility should be taken over by the preparatory committee in Shanghai. However, the antiquities we are currently inspecting at the Antiquities Museum are part of the antiquities that will be selected for shipment to England in the future. As there are many antiquities, without a target, it is difficult to start. Therefore, the selection is still based on the inventory list from today's inspection.

Detailed Inspection: Regarding the inspection of antiquities, there are four departments storing antiquities in Shanghai: 1) the Antiquities Museum, 2) the Documents Museum, 3) the Library, and 4) the Secretariat. The current inspection is of the Antiquities Museum. The Antiquities Museum stores over 2,000 boxes of antiquities in Shanghai, of which 581 boxes have been inspected. Approximately 20 boxes can be inspected each day. Although the antiquities have been inspected in the past, it was too careless, leading to theft incidents. To prevent future fraud, we are carefully registering and recording details, such as variety, dynasty, size, weight, pattern, and color, regardless of the inconvenience. The inventory list of the former Qing Dynasty Aftermath Committee is far less detailed than the current records. The current inspection inventory list is divided into ten copies: one for the Executive Yuan, one for the Ministry of Education, one for the Antiquities Preservation Committee, five for the Palace Museum, and the remainder for the inspectors themselves.

Selection Standards: The government ordered the Palace Museum Council to decide on the standards for selecting antiquities to be shipped to England. It was decided to use the antiquities from the Antiquities Museum for participation. The antiquities from the Antiquities Museum include bronzes, lacquerware, porcelain, jade, embroidery, calligraphy, and painting. Selection will be made from each of the above categories. However, there must be two of the same item, or a photo on file. During the current inspection, items with photos on file will not be re-photographed, while those without photos will be photographed. To expedite the inspection work, Beijing has recently sent ten more people to Shanghai to assist. The preparatory committee can send personnel to Shanghai next month to be responsible for presiding over the selection.

The Miscellaneous Grain Association Discusses Limiting the Purchase of Foreign Rice Yesterday 123

Resolved to Report to the Social Affairs Bureau for Handling

And Advising Colleagues to Pay Close Attention

The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain Industry Association held a temporary meeting of all executive and supervisory committee members at the Miscellaneous Grain Market on Min Guo Road at 4:00 PM yesterday to discuss methods to restrict the purchase of foreign rice by fellow traders. Gu Xinyi, Cai Yukun, Zhu Zixiang,

Tomorrow is the Third Anniversary of the "January 28th" Incident 124

｜Notice from the First Special District Municipal Federation｜

Shops and Citizens Fly Flags at Half-Mast for One Day

Visit the Miaohang to Pay Tribute to the Fallen Soldiers

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation issued a special notice to the member stores under the district branches yesterday, stating that tomorrow is the anniversary of the "January 28th" national humiliation: "Dear Sirs, as the anniversary of the January 28th national humiliation approaches, all members of our Chinese nation feel the pain of remembrance. It is hoped that your district branch will notify the member stores and citizens under your jurisdiction to fly flags at half-mast for one day on that day and observe three minutes of silence at 1:28 PM to commemorate the compatriots and soldiers who suffered in the Shanghai Incident. Please also ask the committee members of each district branch to lead citizens to Miaohang at 10:00 AM to pay tribute to the fallen soldiers. This is especially hoped for. Accordingly, this letter is sent to you, and it is hoped that you will check and handle it accordingly."

More than 20 people, including She Bingwen, Zhou Yuting, Wu Zisheng, Xu Shili, Fu Changyu, and He Quansheng, were present, with Gu Xinyi chairing.

Reporting on the Process: Chairman Gu Xinyi first reported, stating briefly that due to the severe drought last summer, the fields were cracked, and the autumn harvest was poor. Therefore, fellow traders and the banking industry in Shanghai ordered foreign rice from Saigon and other places to regulate the people's food supply. By the time of the autumn harvest, all the rice was on the market. Although the harvest in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, and other provinces was less than in previous years, the total amount of rice shortage was estimated at about 3 million shi. It has now been found that fellow traders and non-traders from both Shanghai and other places have ordered foreign rice. According to reports from various foreign firms, it has exceeded 6 million bags. The demand exceeds the supply, which will inevitably lead to a drop in the market price of domestic rice, affecting the rural areas. The association fears that it will cause economic risks to fellow traders. In order to reduce this phenomenon, the association convened a general meeting to discuss appropriate methods. The association hopes that all the committee members present will express their opinions.

Total Amount of Foreign Rice: The foreign firms that undertook the agency for ordering foreign rice include Da Yuan, Shun Jinlong, Yuanli, Fujia, Jiecheng, Jinfu, Guangjilong, Yali, Heyi, Baolong, Xiangmao, Dafu, Jinlong, Yongda, Dafeng, Taihe, Hengfeng, and 17 other companies. The total amount of foreign rice ordered is as follows: 1) Shanghai: A. Those that have already arrived amount to 150,400 tons. B. Those that have been loaded and are en route to Shanghai amount to 53,700 tons. C. Those that have been ordered but have not yet been shipped amount to 315,300 tons, totaling 549,500 tons. 2) Ningbo: 125,200 tons, totaling 674,700 tons, which is 6,747,000 bags at ten bags per ton.

Resolutions: After each executive and supervisory committee member expressed their opinions on the foreign rice issue, they began to discuss it. Some committee members advocated that the association should stop registration and implement restrictions from today, and stipulate penalties. Some committee members believed that business is free, and if the association implements restrictions, it will inevitably cause a backlash from fellow traders. If there is no forced prohibition, it will lose the credibility of the association. It was then resolved to report the total amount of foreign rice investigated by each foreign firm to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for handling, and to issue a notice of a persuasive nature, hoping that fellow traders would pay close attention. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

It is rumored that Mr. Zhang's mission in Shanghai will soon be completed, and he will return to Shandong tomorrow to report back.

A Steam Pipe on the Japanese Warship Izumo Bursts 127

Burning Three Japanese Soldiers

The Ship Sails as Scheduled

According to the Japanese-language Daily News, the Third Fleet, led by Commander Hyakutake, was about to leave the harbor at 1:30 PM on the 25th to cruise to various places along the South China coast and Taiwan when, unexpectedly, the steam pipe water tank of the flagship Izumo suddenly burst. Three soldiers in the engine room were burned by the fire, one of whom was scalded by hot water all over his body and was in critical condition. The injured soldiers were immediately sent to the Marine Corps hospital for treatment. The fleet still sailed as scheduled.

Formulating a Work Outline

The Shanghai Cooperative Enterprise Committee held its 18th regular meeting at the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge at 3:00 PM yesterday (the 25th). Resolved: 1) Designate Yinhang District as the rural cooperative experimental zone in Shanghai. 2) Request the Social Affairs Bureau to send personnel to investigate the rural economic situation in the district. 3) Establish a rural cooperative experimental zone promotion committee in the district, with the local primary school principal, municipal committee member, agricultural association representative, and local impartial persons who are enthusiastic about the peasant movement as committee members, with a number of five to seven people, and the Social Affairs Bureau sending personnel to guide them at any time. B. The Ministry of Industry will convene a national cooperative enterprise discussion meeting in May this year. Resolved: Send letters to each committee member to solicit proposals and opinions. C. The establishment of consumer cooperatives in factories in Shanghai is of great importance. Resolved: Request the Social Affairs Bureau to send personnel to each factory as soon as possible in accordance with the original plan. D. The internal organization of the committee is not very complete. Resolved: 1) Expand the number of committee members, with the Social Affairs Bureau adding one person, the Education Bureau adding two representatives, three expert committee members being hired, one representative from the Shanghai Cooperative Enterprise Promotion Association, and one person from the Shanghai industrial sector. 2) Hire a secretary to assist with the daily affairs of the committee. E. The committee has no definite funding, making it difficult to operate. Resolved: Request the Social Affairs Bureau to determine the amount of funding for the committee. F. Whether to promote consumer cooperatives in schools in Shanghai. Resolved: Reserve the matter for discussion at the next meeting. G. Motions. 1) Request the Social Affairs Bureau to forward a request to the municipal government to approve the appointment of rural cooperative enterprise instructors in Shanghai. Resolved: Passed. 2) Formulate a work outline for the committee. Resolved: Appoint Wang Gang, Hang Dingan, and Wang Shuji to draft the outline and submit it for discussion at the next meeting.

Reduced Parcel Rates for Xi'an and Other Places 129

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1199 states that the Longhai Railway has now been extended to Chang'an. All places along the line, such as Lingkou, Xinfeng Town, Lintong, Xiekou, Baqiao Town, and Chang'an (Xi'an), are allowed to be changed to wheel-and-rail transportation bureaus. The parcel rates to these bureaus can be paid according to the Tongguan Bureau rate, that is, those posted at the wheel-and-rail transportation bureaus in this postal district should be reduced to one single fee, and those posted at the non-wheel-and-rail bureaus should be reduced to two single fees. This is hereby notified for general knowledge.
