The Benevolent Childhood Association Held Its Sixth Annual Meeting Yesterday 132

Passed New Work Plans for This Year

Elected the President and Committee Members for This Term

According to the Central News Agency, the Chinese Benevolent Childhood Association held its sixth annual meeting yesterday at 3:00 PM in the grand hall of the New Asia Restaurant on North Sichuan Road. More than seventy people, including Kong Xiangxi, attended to discuss the work outline and budget for the 24th year (1935) and to amend the association's constitution. Xiong Xiling, Cai Yuanpei, and others also attended and gave speeches. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Those who attended yesterday included President Kong Xiangxi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, President of the Academia Sinica Cai Yuanpei, Legislative Yuan representative Sun Zhidong, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Yu Zuoting, Municipal Party Headquarters representative Mao Yun, Municipal Social Affairs Bureau representative Chen Lengseng, as well as Xiong Xiling, Lin Kanghou, Ding Shujing, Ding Fubao, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jianping, Zhao Jinqing, Li Tingan, Du Yuesheng, Wu Weide, Yan Fuqing, Zhu Shaoping, Yang Dunfu, and more than seventy others.

Proceedings: After 3:00 PM, the meeting was called to order with a bell. President Kong Xiangxi presided over the meeting and, after performing the formalities, reported the purpose of the meeting. Xu Jianping reported on the general situation of the work in the 23rd year (1934), and Lin Kanghou reported on the economic situation in the 23rd year. President Kong left the meeting due to other business and was replaced by Wang Xiaolai, who invited Xiong Xiling, Cai Yuanpei, and Chu Minyi to deliver speeches successively. Then, Lin Kanghou proposed a discussion on the budget for the 24th year, Zhao Jinqing proposed a discussion on amending the constitution, and He Weide proposed a discussion on the work plan for the 24th year. All were approved in order. Finally, representatives of party and government organizations delivered speeches before the meeting was adjourned.

President's Report: President Kong Xiangxi reported that today is the sixth annual meeting of the association. In the past year, thanks to the enthusiastic guidance of people from all walks of life and the efforts of the association's colleagues, the association's work has made much progress. The convocation of the National Benevolent Childhood Leaders Conference last year was of great significance. The issues raised for discussion and the various resolutions passed at the conference were very satisfactory. Benevolent childhood undertakings are extremely important to the country and society. Today's children are the future leaders of society. In this time of national crisis, we want to rescue this crisis, and we rely on each individual to be loyal to the country and society. If we want to cultivate talents who can fully serve the country and society, the education and upbringing of children cannot be ignored. If the education and upbringing of children are inadequate, how can we expect them to be fully effective when serving the country and society? Conversely, if children can be given excellent education and upbringing, they will surely serve the country and be loyal to the nation in the future, and they will achieve very satisfactory results. The ancients said, "Respect the elderly of my family and extend it to the elderly of other families; love the young of my family and extend it to the young of other families." The so-called loving the young of my family and extending it to the young of other families means that parents should pay attention to the education and upbringing of their own children, and also hope for the education and upbringing of children in general. Since its establishment, the association has had a history of six years. In these six years, although some aspects have not been achieved due to environmental factors, it has indeed achieved considerable results so far. Due to my other duties and busyness, I have not been able to devote myself to the benevolent childhood undertaking. Fortunately, colleagues and people from all walks of life have devoted themselves to the guidance and efforts of the benevolent childhood undertaking, and we have achieved today's results. I would like to express my deep gratitude here. I sincerely hope that people from all walks of life and colleagues can continue their efforts with a spirit of continuous encouragement. The revival of the nation and the strength of the country depend on this, which is by no means superficial. Let us encourage each other.

Mr. Xiong's Speech: Xiong Xiling continued with a speech, briefly stating that the association has made remarkable progress in its work and has achieved excellent results recently, which I greatly admire. Everyone is able to participate enthusiastically in today's conference, and I believe that the future of the benevolent childhood undertaking will be bright. I have two thoughts here: 1) In this transitional period, there may be those who do not understand the benevolent childhood undertaking, or those who understand it but not deeply. The former are generally old-fashioned and even oppose the methods of benevolent childhood, believing that China has not had so-called new methods of education and upbringing in the past, and children have still grown up and become outstanding talents. The latter are people of the new era, but they have not paid close attention to the care of children. Today, parents who receive higher education often specialize in a certain field of study and do not have time to study the education and upbringing of children, so they only know to send their children to nurseries or kindergartens and no longer inquire. However, children must never survive independently of their families. If there is no good education and upbringing in the family, the impact will be significant. The development of transportation, the easy spread of various infectious diseases, and the increase in the stimulation received by children are all factors that cannot be ignored. Judging from the current situation in China, families in urban areas may think that children enjoy better conditions than those in poor rural areas, but this is a great misconception in practice. When we look at families in urban areas, their furnishings may be exquisite, but they completely disregard the happiness of their children, often entrusting their children to nannies or caregivers without asking how poorly the nannies or caregivers live and dress, so their children are often affected by the nannies or caregivers and cannot be healthy. Therefore, we must make parents use scientific new methods for the education of their children. 2) Regarding the past childhood education and upbringing institutions, such as nurseries and kindergartens, they manage the children they receive entirely with school management methods. As a result, children can make considerable progress in their studies, but they feel weak in their ability to cope with the environment and various other activities. The Xiangshan Benevolent Childhood Institute, which I run, has been seeking to improve these shortcomings in recent years. In the past, each teacher managed dozens of children, which made the teachers unable to focus and made it difficult for the children to benefit. Now, the institute has set up a family department, where each teacher manages only ten children, so they can be in close contact with them at any time and place. The results of this method are much better than before. Therefore, my second thought is that teachers should be like parents.

Mr. Cai's Speech: Cai Yuanpei spoke, briefly stating that the ancients paid great attention to respecting the elderly and loving the young. The so-called "comfort the old and cherish the young." Our association takes the promotion of benevolent childhood as its mission. Some may think that benevolent childhood is more important than respecting the elderly, or that other relationships are more important, but let's put that aside for now. Life can be divided into three stages: the first is childhood, the second is adulthood, and the third is old age. The elderly have fulfilled their obligations to society for many years and can rest. Adults are working hard for social undertakings, and children are expected to take on responsibilities in the future. Nations with undeveloped cultures only pay attention to the present, while countries with developed cultures focus on the future. The so-called savings and so on are based on this idea, to restrain the present, sacrifice the present, and prepare for the future. The ancients said, "It takes one year to grow grain, ten years to grow trees, and a hundred years to cultivate people." Farmers sacrifice their spirits in one year and hope for a harvest at the end of the year. Tree planters sacrifice ten years of time and hope for the harvest of trees growing in ten years. The same is true for cultivating people. Children are responsible for the future of the country, so adults should sacrifice their spirits for the education and upbringing of children. For example, when a ship encounters danger at sea, women and children must be rescued first, and adults are willing to stay behind. Although this has the meaning of helping the weak, it also emphasizes the importance of children. When I was in Austria, Austria lacked milk, so the milk was allocated, and children were given it first, and the rest was given to adults. When we look at the progress of the world, the responsibilities of future people will be greater than those of present people. In other words, future people should be better than present people in terms of ability. In other words, the education and upbringing given to today's children should be more important than those given to children in the past. Only in this way can future people bear this heavy responsibility. The content of benevolent childhood can be divided into two: one is education, and the other is upbringing. Education without upbringing is futile, so upbringing is more important than education. We should have appropriate adjustments for all the clothing, food, and housing of children, and hygiene should be especially emphasized. In childhood, because of close contact with the family environment, parents should be perfect role models for their children. The ancients said, "Confucius's family members did not know how to scold, and Zengzi's family members did not revile." In the families of Confucius and Zengzi, every word and deed was in line with morality. When we organize benevolent childhood undertakings, we should remind those who are responsible for raising children to pay close attention to this. We must do our best to help them. Even if we cannot help directly, we should provide assistance in their work indirectly, so that great achievements can be made.

Mr. Chu's Speech: Chu Minyi spoke, briefly stating the importance of the benevolent childhood undertaking, which everyone should do their best to promote. People should not only enjoy themselves in this world, but should also think about where they came from, so they should respect their ancestors and love their descendants. Our people have always had the saying "There are three unfilial acts, and having no descendants is the greatest," and "Having many children and grandchildren is the greatest happiness." Therefore, the Chinese nation has reached four hundred million or even four hundred and fifty million to this day. Now, countries all over the world are paying close attention to the encouragement of population reproduction. For example, if a family has too many children, the government will bear part of the education expenses of those children, so the population of various countries is expanding rapidly. Although our country's population is still large, the quality of the population has been ignored, so we have the title of "Sick Man of East Asia." In the future, if we want to strengthen the race and strengthen the country, we must pay attention to the quality of the population, that is, to give children full education and upbringing. I believe that attention to hygiene and the promotion of physical education should be strengthened, etc. Representatives of the Municipal Party Headquarters Mao Yun and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Chen Lengseng also delivered speeches (omitted due to length).

General Situation of Association Affairs: Xu Jianping reported on the general situation of the association's work in the 23rd year (1934), and small booklets in Chinese and English were distributed separately, including: 1) Holding the National Benevolent Childhood Leaders Conference, 2) Organizing Benevolent Childhood Associations in various places, 3) Handling children's cases, 4) Petitioning the Judicial Yuan to allow benevolent childhood organizations to have the right to sue on behalf of abused children, 5) Establishing the Shanghai Benevolent Childhood Clinic, 6) Assisting other organizations in their clinic work, 7) Constructing the Benevolent Childhood Tuberculosis Sanatorium, 8) The Shanghai Benevolent Childhood Nursery, 9) The Shanghai Benevolent Childhood Education Institute, 10) Promoting Children's Day and advocating Children's Day, 11) Publishing the Modern Parents Monthly, 12) Taking over the Zhabei Civilian Education Institute, 13) Petitioning the National Government to instruct secondary and higher schools across the country to pay attention to parental education, 14) Holding benevolent childhood broadcasts and speeches, 15) Publishing "Parentology" and "Parental Education Charts," and other fifteen sections.

Report on Income and Expenditure: Lin Kanghou reported on the association's income and expenditure in the 23rd year (1934). The total income was as follows: (A. Income) 1. Total: 70,758.85 yuan.

Amendment of Constitution: After Mr. Lin's report, Zhao Jinqing reported on the amendment of the constitution. The committee unanimously passed the following points regarding the proposed amendments to the constitution: 1) Regarding membership, adding group members; 2) Regarding organization, it is proposed that the president, vice president, secretary, accountant, and other standing committee members.

Work Plan: Then, Wu Weide reported on the implementation work plan for the 24th year (1935) as follows: 1) Promoting Children's Year, 2) Promoting Children's Day, 3) Enriching the content of the association's affiliated institutions, 4) Promoting the resolutions of the National Benevolent Childhood Leaders Conference, 5) Establishing Benevolent Childhood Associations in various places, 6) Investigating the status of national Benevolent Childhood undertakings, 7) Assisting in the improvement of Benevolent Childhood institutions in various places, 8) Holding an exhibition of Benevolent Childhood items (such as reading materials and toys), 9) Completing the Capital Benevolent Childhood Health and Amusement Park, 10) Establishing a model Benevolent Childhood Institute in the capital, 11) Promoting nursery undertakings, 12) Promoting fertility regulation, 13) Holding children's health and amusement competitions, 14) Holding parents' meetings, 15) Holding parental education workshops, 16) Holding benevolent childhood speeches, 17) Holding benevolent childhood broadcasts and speeches, 18) Promoting the Modern Parents Monthly, 19) Compiling the Benevolent Childhood Series, 20) Rescuing homeless children, 21) Protecting oppressed children, 22) Stopping the sale of children, 23) Establishing a complaint office for young prostitutes in Shanghai, 24) Promoting children's laws, 25) Promoting children's courts, 26) Requesting the government to allow Benevolent Childhood institutions to have the right to sue on behalf of abused children, unanimously passed.

Election of New Committee Members: The results of the election of new committee members are as follows: 1) Executive Committee: President Kong Xiangxi, Chief Vice President Luo Yunyan, Second Vice President Fei Meide, Accountant Lin Kanghou, Deputy Accountant Sun Ruihuang, Secretary Chen Heqin, Committee members Ding Shujing, Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Youyu, Zhu Lide, Du Yuesheng, Wu Weide, Li Tingan, Wei Zhihua, Mrs. Boland, Cao Yunxiang, Mrs. Zhang Xuelou, Zhao Jinqing, Mrs. Herrmann Krans, Sevis, Yan Fuqing. 2) Honorary Committee Members: Honorary President Lin Sen, Legal Counsel Xue Dubi, Committee Members Ding Guitang, Wang Yiting, Wang Shijie, Wang Sima, Wang Rutang, Wang Liao Fengxian, Kong Song Ailing, Zhu Ziqiao, Zhu Shaoyang, Zhu Jiahua, Song Ziwen, Yu Rizhang, Li Denghui, Wu Zushen, Qu Wenliu, Shen Honglie, Wang Jingwei, Wu Jingxiong, Wu Tiecheng, Jin Bangping, Hu Wenhu, Hu Yigu, Chen Bohong, Xu Shiying, Tao Zhihang, Ma Junwu, Yan Yangchu, Huang Hanzhi, Huang Yingbai, Huang Shaoxiong, Gao Fengchi, Zhang Zhijiang, Zhang Boling, Zhang Qun, Zhang Jingjiang, Sun Ke, Yang Chongrui, Chiang Kai-shek, Chiang Song Meiling, Chu Minyi, Pan Gongzhan, Cai Jiemin, Cheng Jingyi, Yong Jianqiu, Xiong Bingsan, Lu Zuofu, Wen Lanting, Liu Ruiheng, Zhong Rongguang, Dai Chuanxian.

Fire Extinguisher Buckets Charged the Same as Bicycles 140

Ministry of Railways Instructs Railway Bureau to Comply

The Two Railways Administration received Instruction No. 157 from the Ministry of Railways, stating: According to the report from the Business Department of this Ministry, according to the letter No. 2187 from the Military Vehicle Department of the said road, it is reported that the area of ​​a fire extinguisher bucket is smaller than that of a rickshaw, and the two small wheels installed below are similar to bicycles, and the area is also similar. However, there are no clear regulations in the passenger car transportation rules on how to charge transportation fees, so it is often difficult to follow when this item is transported by passenger car. It should be requested that the Ministry approve the matter. Based on this, the report is true. If the above item is transported by passenger car, how should the transportation fee be charged? Please inquire. The Ministry has replied that the fire extinguisher bucket is said to be similar to a bicycle, and the area is also similar. It can be handled in accordance with two-wheeled bicycles, with a charge of 2 cents per kilometer per item, with a minimum of 50 cents. In addition to separate orders, the bureau is hereby ordered to comply. This order has been forwarded by the bureau to the Vehicle Affairs Department for compliance.

Li Zhenfu Accuses of Assault 141

Rescheduled for Further Hearing on February 1st

Li Zhenfu, a Cantonese man who once served as the manager of the Shanghai Bank's Moganshan branch, had previously developed a romantic relationship with Huang Peixian, a woman from the same hometown, out of friendship. Li was unmarried, and Huang was unwed, both being in the prime of their sexually mature years. A lonely man and a lonely woman, once they came into contact, were like magnets drawn to iron, inseparable. It seemed easy to achieve a happy marriage. Unexpectedly, the sea of love is turbulent, with its movements unpredictable. The deep affection suddenly turned into profound resentment. As a result, the pursuit of a good match was unfulfilled, and lawsuits arose repeatedly. In the autumn, although Li offended Huang, he did not diminish his ardent admiration for Huang, even though she treated him like a stranger. He could truly be described as having a singular passion and being rich in unrequited love. They both belonged to the modern stream, and their daily lives, actions, and etiquette were all required to cater to the trends of the times. December 25th was Christmas, and Li specially prepared flower baskets and candies, personally driving his motorcycle on that afternoon at 4 PM to send them to his beloved Huang Peixian, who resided in apartment number 3 in Lane 3, Jing'an Temple Road. Upon arriving at Huang's room number 5, he found the door tightly closed, so he placed the gifts on the ground and stood to knock. Huang heard the sound inside, knowing it was Li. Initially, she offered him the cold shoulder, then she cursed and scolded him from inside the room, and finally, she suddenly flung the door open, raised her delicate hand, and slapped Li's cheek, kicked the baskets with her natural foot. Li felt humiliated by receiving such treatment while presenting gifts, which was rare in his life. He immediately ordered his driver to call the police to reason with her, but both sides continued to revile each other in Cantonese. The officer tried his best to mediate. Soon after, the Jing'an Temple Police Station also received a report and dispatched Western Officer Number 15 to rush to the scene, advising Li to go downstairs first. Huang was still filled with anger, picking up candies and throwing them at Li from afar. Afterward, Li went to the Jing'an Temple Police Station to report the circumstances of being provoked and assaulted, then returned to consult a doctor, who said that his arms and other parts were injured by the beating. Consequently, he hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to file a criminal self-accusation against Huang. Yesterday afternoon, the First Special District Local Court held a hearing before Judge Yinghua. The defendant, Huang Peixian, claimed to be ill and did not attend. Her lawyer appeared in court and requested a postponement. Li Zhenfu then recounted in detail the experience of being assaulted while delivering gifts, saying that although the defendant was a woman, she had practiced sports in school and was therefore very strong and powerful. A slap on the cheek was of no consequence, but his arm was injured by the beating, although he did not initially notice it, but only realized it after consulting a doctor, who said it was an internal injury. Next, Chinese Officer Number 2117 reported the circumstances of the conflict between the two parties that he had witnessed. Judge Xiang then granted the defendant's request, ordering the hearing to be rescheduled for February 1st in the afternoon.

Creditors of the China Industrial Bank Held a General Meeting Yesterday 142

Lu Xihou Failed to Raise Sufficient Funds, Creditors Rose Up to Reproach Him

The creditors' group of the China Industrial Bank held a general meeting at the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday at 2 PM. More than 500 people attended. Yin Shouguang, Luo Jiaheng, and Qian Zunmin served as the presidium. After the formalities, lawyer Dong Yu first reported on the progress of the negotiations, followed by lawyer Wu Linkun, representing Lu Xihou, who stood up to state that his client, Lu Xihou, had been granted bail by the First Special District Court less than two weeks ago. Before the bail was granted, he had agreed with the creditors to first repay half of the debt. However, since being bailed out, the time has been very short, and he has been running around everywhere, intending to borrow cash from various parties. Unexpectedly, he has been rebuffed everywhere, and even some organizations that were expected to be able to help have recently gone bankrupt themselves, so everything has come to naught. Now, he has tried his best to raise 40,000 yuan in cash and is specifically proposing two conditions to the creditors: 1. Creditors with claims of 500 yuan or less (amounting to approximately 40,000 yuan in total) will be repaid 20% first. Creditors with claims of more than 500 yuan (amounting to approximately 200,000 yuan in total) should preferably agree to a temporary postponement. If absolutely necessary, he proposes to repay 10% first. 2. Lu Xihou has borrowed several land deeds from various parties and is willing to hand them over to the creditors, who can then seek mortgage loans from banks to distribute the funds. If the above two conditions are agreed upon, they can be implemented accordingly. If the creditors object, Lu Xihou is willing to return to prison to await punishment, thereby repaying the creditors, etc. A creditor then stood up and said that before Lu Xihou was granted bail, his lawyer had stated that Lu Xihou had raised cash from various parties, and if he were granted bail, he could repay the creditors 50% first. He even said that the funds had been deposited, and once Lu was released and signed the documents, the repayment could be made accordingly. Unexpectedly, Lu Xihou has now gone back on his word. We are not willing to be deceived and have decided to resolve the matter legally with Lu. At this time, all the creditors applauded in agreement, and the order gradually became chaotic. During the commotion, Lu Xihou suddenly made some inappropriate remarks on stage, which aroused the public anger of the creditors, who rose up to argue with him. Lu Xihou's younger brother then came forward to mediate. The creditors, due to the similarity in their clothes and appearance, mistook him for Lu himself and surrounded him. After he explained, they dispersed. Lu Xihou, in the midst of the commotion, had changed into someone else's clothes and secretly left the meeting place. Thus, the two sides have reached extreme positions. The creditors insist on first repaying 50%, while Lu insists on 20%. The creditors' representatives, Wu Peng and others, then resigned from their positions and left the meeting in protest, making the situation even more deadlocked. Subsequently, Lu's wife went on stage to express her apologies to the crowd. The creditors resolved to make a demand to Lu: 50% repayment for claims under 500 yuan and 20% repayment for claims over 500 yuan, to be paid before the final settlement deadline, with the remaining debt to be repaid after the final settlement. Lu Xihou is required to respond in the newspaper within two days. The meeting adjourned due to the late hour.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Decides to Operate Public Buses in Pudong 143

Since the Shanghai-South Public Bus of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities started operating, its business has been quite prosperous. In addition to adding routes in the Shanghai-South district, it is also planning to set up new routes in Pudong to facilitate transportation. According to the person in charge of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities,

Shanghai-South Buses: The ring road route and the Longhua-West Gate route operated by the bureau in Shanghai-South have been quite successful. However, due to the recent soaring gasoline prices and the low fares set by the bureau, there are concerns that the revenue may not be able to offset the expenses. If gasoline prices rise further, the increased expenses will inevitably require alternative solutions. The bureau originally planned to switch to using charcoal, but the three ring road routes are short, and there are more than ten stops, so the horsepower may not be sufficient.

New Pudong Route: The bureau will open a new public bus route in Pudong in March this year. This route is actually very necessary, so the bureau will strive to make the operation of buses on this route a reality. However, due to the high gasoline prices, charcoal will be used instead. Since the route is longer and has fewer stops, switching to charcoal should not cause concerns about insufficient horsepower. Therefore, the bureau will conduct preliminary tests. If it is successful, it will consider reforming other routes as well.

Taifeng Canned Food Company Owes More Than 600,000 144

Debts Owed by Others Are Insufficient to Offset the Debt

Creditors Jointly Sue the Court

The Taifeng Canned Food Company on Nanjing Road has been in business for decades, and its business has always been prosperous. In recent years, due to the impact of the economic downturn and the decline of all industries, it has also felt the strain on its working capital. Consequently, on December 20th of the lunar year, it announced the temporary suspension of business and entrusted accountants Xu Yongzuo and lawyers Zhang Zhengxue and Zha Renwei to handle the liquidation affairs. Therefore, the creditors of the company initially believed that their debts would be secured and adopted a wait-and-see attitude. However, after more than a month, the company has announced no definite measures, and the general creditors have become highly suspicious, fearing that it will use the name of liquidation to imitate the bad habit of賴債 (defaulting on debts). Therefore, currently, 46 creditors in the banking and money industries, including Shanghai Bank and Tongqing Money Shop, have hired lawyers Sun Yuan and Xu Zuyan, based on the current Regulations on the Liquidation of Merchants' Debts, to file a petition with the First Special District Local Court, requesting that the Taifeng Company be declared bankrupt and that its movable and immovable properties be provisionally attached to protect their claims. It is reported that the amount owed by Taifeng to these banks and shops is only over 150,000 yuan, while the total amount owed to others is as high as more than 600,000 yuan. The assets owed by others to Taifeng, including the company's Xiaoshadu Road factory base and buildings, the Nanjing Road storefront and business goods, various stocks purchased by the company, various guarantee deposits paid, and the property of a certain match factory that has also suspended operations, are only worth 300,000 to 400,000 yuan. The difference is quite large, so the banks and shops have sought the protection of the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tao Dejun of the First Special Court held a hearing. Lawyers Sun and Xu, representing the petitioning banks and shops, appeared in court and stated the reasons for their request, asking that the company be declared bankrupt, that all account books be seized, and that auditors be appointed to conduct liquidation. Before the declaration of bankruptcy, they requested that all its properties and goods be provisionally attached. After reviewing the case, Judge Tao ordered the petitioners to file a separate statement regarding the provisional attachment and await verification. As for the request to declare bankruptcy, he also directed them to wait for further investigation and verification.

Foreign Firm Comprador Accused of Enticement and Abandonment 145

Xu Qimei Was Deceived During the Shanghai War

Shen Zhijing's Marriage Agreement Was Unfounded

Xu Qimei, a 26-year-old woman from Suzhou residing at No. 1, Yongyu Lane, Baylor Road, French Concession, has recently hired lawyer Ping Heng to file a criminal complaint in the First Special Court against Shen Zhijing, a foreign firm comprador from the same hometown residing at No. 32, Yongqing Lane, Xin Dagulu, accusing him of using deception to make her mistakenly believe that they had a marital relationship, enticing and abandoning her, and attaching a civil lawsuit, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi presided over the hearing in the Criminal Court No. 8. The defendant, Shen Zhijing, did not appear. According to the plaintiff, Xu Qimei, during the January 28th Incident, she met the defendant in Shanghai. He took care of her attentively and persuaded her to move to Suzhou to avoid the disaster. Moreover, the defendant expressed that his home was still empty and that he wished to form a lifelong alliance with her. As a lonely bird in troubled times, she could not help but feel grateful for his comfort and care. The defendant then made solemn promises, saying that after the war subsided, they would return to Shanghai to hold a wedding ceremony and would never be careless or deceitful. Because she was burdened with debt at the time, she did not have time for private plans. The defendant also offered to repay her debts and was willing to write an IOU, further specifying her status as his wife. Seeing his enthusiasm, she agreed to live with him first. Between husband and wife, their affection surpassed that of painted eyebrows. Later, as the situation stabilized, they moved back to Shanghai. She asked the defendant to fulfill his previous agreement and hold a wedding ceremony. However, the defendant claimed to be economically distressed, using excuses to delay. Once he was a little better off, he would make up for the marriage contract. If she did not believe him, he would write an IOU stating that if either party changed their mind midway, they would be liable for compensation of 5,000 yuan. Seeing his gentle words and sincere feelings, she could not bear to push him too hard. Recently, she heard that the municipal government had group weddings, and the wedding ceremony was very economical. She then ordered the defendant to prepare for the wedding. Unexpectedly, the defendant pretended to agree but secretly stole the previously written note and left, never to return. On December 26th, she discovered that the defendant resided at No. 32, Yongqing Lane, Dagulu, and went there. She met the defendant, but unexpectedly, the defendant already had a wife and children. His wife was even pregnant and awaiting childbirth, so she aggressively drove her away. A dream of spring, only now did she wake up. Upon investigation, the defendant's actions actually violated Article 244 of the Criminal Law and should be severely punished. Moreover, he should be ordered to pay 8,000 yuan in living expenses, etc. Judge Wu reviewed the statement and ordered that the case be rescheduled for the afternoon of the 30th, waiting for the defendant to be summoned to court for further questioning.

Unemployed Servant Extorts Manager 146

Sentenced to Two Months Imprisonment

Xia Xinquan, a man from Ningbo, 49 years old, used to be a servant at the office of Mr. Pagmen, a Western director of the Zheng Guanghe Foreign Firm at No. 44, Fuzhou Road. In 1930, Pagmen dismissed Xia because Xia was suffering from mental illness. Xia believed that his dismissal was caused by the slander of the Chinese General Manager, Lin Chengchuan. Therefore, he often went to the foreign firm to make trouble for Lin, demanding that he be paid a monthly salary of 45 yuan. Lin, unable to bear his harassment, paid him 150 yuan on August 11, 1931. At that time, Xia's friend wrote a receipt on his behalf and guaranteed that he would no longer make trouble in the future. Unexpectedly, not long after, Xia relapsed and made trouble at Zheng Guanghe again. Lin reported him to the police, who detained him and sent him to court, which sentenced him to eight months of detention in a settlement. Recently, Xia went to Zheng Guanghe to make trouble again, and on the 21st of the month, he demanded that Lin pay him 200 yuan in living expenses and 3,000 yuan in wages for the five years he had been dismissed, to be delivered by the morning of the 25th. Otherwise, he would die with him. Lin, fearing danger, reported the matter to the General Police Station, and the captain ordered Chinese detectives Che Xuehui and Wu Chunrong to wait at the foreign firm on the morning of the 25th. At 11:15 AM, Xia came as expected and said that 3,000 yuan was not enough, he wanted 6,000 yuan to settle the matter. The detectives arrested him and took him back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Court No. 1 of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the case, prosecuting him for attempted extortion by intimidation under Article 370, Section 3 of the Criminal Law. Then, Lin Chengchuan submitted a petition detailing the events. The defendant was questioned and confessed that his business was dismissed due to the plaintiff's slander, so he demanded to maintain his livelihood or be introduced to a job. The plaintiff agreed to introduce him to a job, so he often went to inquire and did not make trouble. He admitted to demanding 3,000 yuan, etc. Judge Qian Hongye asked if he had suffered from mental illness. He replied that he had recovered. Judge Qian then announced the verdict, sentencing Xia to two months imprisonment for attempted extortion by intimidation as a warning.

Neighbors Report to Police for Arrest

Prize Savings to End Soon 152

The Ministry of Finance Has Set Ending Measures

To Be Implemented After Approval by the Executive Yuan

According to the New Sound Agency, after the promulgation and implementation of the Savings Bank Law, Article 14 states that "Prize savings should be prohibited. Prize savings that have been handled before the implementation of this law should immediately stop collecting savings deposits, and the ending measures should be drafted by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval." The Ministry of Finance has drafted the measures for ending the prize savings that have been handled before the implementation of this law and submitted them to the Executive Yuan. After the approval, they will be ordered to comply. The institutions that handle prize savings include: 1. The 万国储蓄会 (International Savings Society), a French company, was founded in 1912 and has a large scope. Its headquarters are in Shanghai, and its branches are spread across Guangzhou, Chongqing, Hankou, Beiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other ports. 2. The 中法储蓄会 (Sino-French Savings Society) was founded in August 1918. Its headquarters are in Beiping, and its branches are located in Shanghai, Hangzhou, Shantou, Tianjin, Nanjing, Fuzhou, Hankou, Guangzhou, Xiamen, Anqing, and Changsha. In addition, there is also the China Industrial Bank, which had already been ordered by the Ministry to stop collecting savings and handle the ending.

Secret Plot to Blow Up Shun'an Steamer Trial Begins 153

Ship Owner Ouyang Tai and Zheng Akang Both Granted Bail

Further Investigation of the Case and Summoning of Witnesses Are Required for Retrial

The Shun'an steamer of the Shun'an Steamer Company, which travels to and from Xinghua, Fujian, etc., departed from Shanghai on September 13th of last year, loaded with goods and set sail for Fujian. When it arrived at Sanduwo, Fujian, the ship owner Ouyang Tai reported to the customs there that Chen Youbai, the manager of the company, secretly instructed to blow up the steamer in order to claim insurance money. Because he could not bear the innocent sacrifice of all lives on board, he reported this matter, etc. After receiving the report, the customs detained the ship and cargo and sent Ouyang Tai to the Minhou Local Court for detention. Zheng Zhongwu, the chairman of the Shun'an Company, also learned of the previous situation and was greatly shocked. He immediately reported to the police station, and on the night of September 24th, Chen Youbai was arrested inside the Beifang Steamer Company on Fadama Road and sent to the Second Special District Court. Due to the issue of jurisdiction, Chen Youbai was transferred to the Nanshi Local Court. Prosecutor Zhao Chuanjia questioned him, detained him, and sent the police to the Minhou Local Court in Fujian to transfer Ouyang Tai to Shanghai. After several interrogations and investigations, the case was clarified, and a prosecution was filed in the Criminal Court. Chen Youbai was ordered to provide a 3,000 yuan surety to be released on bail awaiting instructions, and Ouyang Tai was returned to detention. The details have been reported previously. At 9:30 AM yesterday, Judge Chen Jingyi specially opened the 13th Court for a continued hearing. First, Zheng Zhongwu's younger brother, Zheng Akang, 19 years old, from Xinghua, Fujian, currently a student, testified. Question: Why did you return to Fujian on September 13th of last year? Answer: Because my father died, I took the Shun'an steamer back to my hometown to handle the funeral. Question: Did your brother Zhongwu instruct you to go back? Answer: No. Question: What happened when the steamer left the port? Answer: In the middle of the journey, I was lonely on the ship, so I chatted with the ship owner Ouyang Tai. He said, "If the steamer unfortunately encounters danger and breaks and sinks, are you afraid?" I replied at the time, "I haven't practiced swimming, of course I'm afraid." Question: Was there anything else? Answer: On the second day (i.e., the morning of the 14th), after I got up, I walked around by myself and went to the ship owner's room. I saw many crew members talking in the room. When they saw me coming, most of them were silent. Seeing the opportunity, I withdrew and asked the old captain if there was a meeting. He replied that they were planning to blow up the steamer. Question: Since you knew about this major change, why did you change to another ship after the ship docked at Sanduwo? Answer: Because I was in a hurry to handle my father's funeral. Question: What is your relationship with Chen Youbai? Answer: None. After the interrogator finished, he ordered Ouyang Tai, who was in custody, to be brought to the case. He asked, "You said last time that Zheng Akang prevented you from telegraphing to Shanghai, destroyed the telegraph machine, and forced you to blow up the ship. Now, according to Zheng Akang's testimony, this is not the case. What is the situation?" Answer: "Zheng Akang pressured me, and he convened a meeting of the crew on the ship, requiring that the ship must be blown up. He also publicly promised that after the matter was completed, he would pay each person a year's salary." Question: "The motive for blowing up the ship was discussed by Chen Youbai and you. Why did Chen Youbai order Zheng Akang to board the ship to supervise? Moreover, Zheng Akang is Zheng Zhongwu's brother. According to this situation, it does not conform to the facts and reason." Answer: "Zheng Akang relied on the power of his brother Zheng Zhongwu, who is the chairman of the board, so he came to pressure me to blow up the ship. Because I was unwilling to do something that would lose my conscience, when the ship docked at Sanduwo, I reported the situation to the customs." They harbored resentment and framed me. I request the court to investigate clearly. Finally, the manager of the Hehai Insurance Company gave a statement. The judge said that further investigation and summoning of witnesses were necessary in this case. A continued hearing will be held again. Chen Youbai will still be released on his original bail, and Ouyang Tai will be released on a 5,000 yuan surety. Zheng Akang will also be released on a reliable surety pending instructions.

Establishment of the Society for the Study of Chinese and Western Medicine 154

The Society for the Study of Chinese and Western Medicine was initiated by thirty people from the medical community, including Song Daren, Chu Minyi, and Ding Fubao. The inaugural meeting was held yesterday (the 26th) at 2:30 PM in the auditorium of the New Asia Hotel on North Sichuan Road. Over a hundred people attended, including Song Daren, Ding Fubao, Guo Qiyuan, Jiang Huiming, Shen Jingfan, Fan Tianqing, Mao Yun representing the Municipal Party Department, Nie Haifan representing the Education Bureau, Jiang Shouchun from Tongji University, and others. Song Daren was publicly elected as chairman, and Jiang Huiming as recorder. The order of proceedings was as follows: ㈠ Formal opening ceremony; ㈡ Opening address by the chairman, briefly stating that there is inherently no division between Chinese and Western medicine, but the inclusion of both terms in the society's name reflects temporal and spatial considerations. He felt that China has a history of thousands of years, and the knowledge of medicine discovered through human instinct deserves study. However, this study must be conducted using scientific methods to clarify the essence of Chinese culture; ㈢ Report on the preparatory work by Shen Jingfan, a member of the preparatory committee; ㈣ Review of the society's constitution; ㈤ Election of Guo Qiyuan, Song Daren, Fan Tianqing, Shen Jingfan, Ding Fubao, Jiang Huiming, Liu Guoxiang, Tang Jinghan, Zhao Jiru, and others as nine directors, who were sworn into office; ㈥ Guidance from representatives of party and government organs; ㈦ Speeches by guests; ㈧ Photography; ㈨ Banquet; ⑽ Adjournment. It is noted that the Society for the Study of Chinese and Western Medicine is an academic organization dedicated to introducing new medical knowledge, researching ancient Chinese herbal remedies and proven formulas, and organizing Chinese medical literature. It is a pioneering endeavor in China and is destined to make significant contributions to the academic community. The society's address is No. 65 Yongfeng Lane, North Sichuan Road, this city.

Discussion on Improving Ambulance Sirens 156

The sirens used by the Shanghai Municipal Council Fire Brigade's ambulances have been considered disruptive by some. The Police Committee recently reported that it has instructed the Fire Brigade Chief to pay attention to this matter. It is claimed that this type of siren is used in the United States and Canada and is effective in ensuring the rapid passage of ambulances. Other types of sirens are easily confused. Currently, tests are being conducted to add a reflector to direct the siren sound forward to allow pedestrians to give way. Committee members stated that the siren's design inevitably disturbs patients in the vehicle, and quietness should be prioritized over speed. The Fire Brigade Chief has taken this into account and instructed drivers to be mindful.

Publication of the Fourth Issue of the Anhui Series 160

The complete fourth issue of the Anhui Series is a compilation of the posthumous works of Ling Tingkan, collected by the Anhui Series Compilation and Printing Office, and is collectively titled "Mr. Ling Cizhong's Posthumous Works." It includes 13 volumes of "Explanations of Ritual Classics," 6 volumes of "Origins of Yanyue Music," 1 volume of "Corrections of Flute Temperament Errors," 2 volumes of "Chronological Biography of Yuan Yishan," 14 volumes of "Xiaolitang Poetry Collection," 36 volumes of "Literary Collection," 2 volumes of "Plum Blossom Flute Score," and 2 volumes of "Appendix: Chronological Biography of Mr. Ling," totaling 78 volumes, bound into 26 large books, all exquisitely printed on domestic Lianshi paper. Ling Tingkan, courtesy name Cizhong, alternate name Zhongzi, was a native of She County and a Jinshi graduate in the Qianlong Gengxu year. He served as a professor at the Ningguo Prefectural School. In his youth, he was friends with Wang Zhong, Ruan Yuan, Jiao Xun, Jiang Fan, and others. When Huang Wenyang proofread Ci and Qu music, Mr. Ling assisted him. He also studied under Weng Fanggang, delving into the study of classics and history, and developing the ideas of Jiang Yong, Dai Zhen, and Jin Cheng. He was skilled in the interpretation of rites, seeking examples and analyzing words. His explanations were clear, and he sought truth through corroborating evidence, correcting old theories. He can be considered a reliable source for the study of ancient Chinese culture and social history. As for acoustics, philology, the Nine Chapters, and the Eight Lines, he reached their extremes. He was particularly knowledgeable about musical temperament, distinguishing between palace tones and northern and southern tunes, and wrote "Origins of Yanyue Music." The discussions in his literary collection also largely focused on this. He was truly a master of music, temperament, Ci and Qu music of the Qing Dynasty. In poetry, he did not distinguish between the Tang and Song schools, but his talent and knowledge were abundant, and his style was vigorous and lofty, closely resembling Yishan. His Ci music also did not adhere to any single school, but he was strict with musical temperament. If a single word was not in harmony, he would seek to correct it. His prose was skilled in parallelism, attaining the purity of the Han and Wei dynasties and the beauty of the Six Dynasties, surpassing Hu Zhiwei and Kong Guangxuan. He immersed himself in historical studies and was familiar with anecdotes, as seen in his collection. Jiang Fan praised his profound historical knowledge, saying that only Qian Zhuting, Shao Eryun, Li Xiaochen, and Wang Rongfu could be compared to him. The Xiaolitang Collection is extremely rare and sought after by scholars. Now that it has been printed by the Anhui Series Compilation and Printing Office, its popularity can be foreseen.

Pig Boat and Wooden Boat Collide in Storm 163

Fifteen Crew Members Lost at Sea

Qin Ziyi, a pig merchant from Jiangbei, recently purchased over 700 pigs in the Lusi area and hired Zhang Yuanhe's boat to transport them to Shanghai for sale through commission agencies. As the Lunar New Year approached, the demand for pigs in Shanghai was very high. On the 21st of this month, Qin handed the pigs over to Zhang to load onto the boat and urged Zhang to rush to Shanghai for early sale. Qin entrusted his 60-year-old father to escort the shipment. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, while sailing in the waters outside Sanjia, Chongming East Sea, the wind became very strong, and waves crashed against the boat. Qin's father, seeing this, feared danger and urged Zhang to take shelter in port. He ordered the helmsman to quickly steer towards the Chongming coast for berthing. While turning the helm, a wave crashed against the boat, and the main mast in the middle of Zhang's boat was broken by the wind, causing a loss of steering ability. The boat drifted with the wind. The crew shouted for help, but the sea was vast, and no ships came to their rescue. Later, the boat was washed by waves to the Chuansha waters. At that time, the Ningbo sand boat Fang Anyu, fully loaded with timber, was speeding by. Due to the darkness and night, they did not notice each other. When Zhang's boat crashed straight ahead, it was close to Fang's boat. They shouted for help upon seeing each other. Fang's boat heard the sound and was about to avoid it, but the two boats had already collided. Zhang's boat capsized instantly, and all 18 people on board fell into the water. The bow of Fang's boat was also damaged, and three crew members working on the deck were knocked off. They immediately stopped the boat to rescue them, but due to the darkness, strong winds, and high waves, rescue was difficult. They rescued four of Zhang's boat's crew and two of their own crew. The whereabouts of the rest were unknown. Yesterday, Fang's boat sailed to Wusong and anchored, giving money to the rescued crew of Zhang's boat to send them to Shanghai. However, Qin, upon receiving the news and learning that his father had not returned, cried loudly. He was persuaded to stop by friends and immediately hired a boat to go to the scene of the accident to search for bodies. It is said that Fang's boat needs repairs before it can sail again.

Lawsuit over Purchase of American Cotton Futures 168

Losses Due to Continuous Drop in Cotton Prices and Failure to Add Margin

Defendant Claims Plaintiff's Short Selling Borders on Gambling

Gu Cheng Lian, a native of Nanxun, successively placed orders with the American trading firm Meisheng Foreign Firm for 1,000 bales of American cotton futures and 25,000 baskets of American wheat futures between August and September of last year. Three contracts were drawn up, specifying the prices. The contracts stipulated that if the prices fell below the agreed-upon purchase price within the agreed-upon period, Gu would have to pay a margin equal to the difference in the purchase price. Otherwise, the seller would settle the accounts at any time based on the market price of American cotton and wheat, and any losses would be borne by the buyer. After the contracts were established, Gu paid a margin of 7,200 yuan. Unexpectedly, cotton and wheat prices began to fall, and Meisheng requested an increase in the margin, but Gu ignored the request. The foreign firm then abruptly closed all accounts on November 17th, before the goods were due, claiming a total loss of 14,928 yuan and 83 cents and demanding compensation from Gu. Unable to resolve the dispute, they filed a lawsuit for damages in the First Special District District Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong opened the court to summon the parties for questioning. The plaintiff's representative lawyers, Fei Si, Lu Congzu, stated the plaintiff's case, roughly stating that the plaintiff is a member of the New York Cotton Exchange and the Chicago Board of Trade, as well as a member of the Shanghai Stock Exchange. The defendant signed two contracts with the plaintiff on August 29th and September 4th of last year to purchase American cotton, one for 600 bales at a price of 13.38 cents per pound and one for 400 bales at a price of

13.22 cents per pound. The delivery dates were set for December and March. Subsequently, on September 8th, another contract was signed for the purchase of 25,000 baskets of American wheat, priced at $1.07 and 5/8 per basket, with December as the delivery date. It was agreed that the plaintiff would purchase the goods on Gu's behalf from the New York and Chicago exchanges. The contract specified that the defendant should deposit a down payment, known as the margin, upon the delivery of the goods. It further stipulated that if the price of the goods fell to a certain level, the margin would have to be increased. Subsequently, the prices of the goods fell steadily. "The plaintiff repeatedly notified the defendant to pay the margin, and the defendant initially paid 7,200 yuan on October 4th. However, this amount was

significantly different from the amount requested by the plaintiff. A letter was sent to the defendant on November 13th, requesting that an additional 19,000 yuan be paid before 3:00 PM on the same day. Otherwise, the cotton and wheat would have to be resold, and any losses would be borne by the defendant. However, the defendant continued to ignore the request, and the two goods were completely resold on November 15th, resulting in a loss of over 14,000 yuan, which should be compensated according to the contract. These are all established facts, which the defendant should not deny. The reason that the defendant relies on is that this transaction is purely short selling, similar to gambling, which is a far-fetched argument." The defendant's lawyer, Yang Linzhi, then replied, stating that there was no dispute over the facts of the case, except that the bill presented by the plaintiff only listed

the purchase price but not the sale price, so the difference could not be recognized. However, this point was not the defendant's main defense. What the defendant emphasized was that all three contracts contained a gambling nature and were essentially a form of short selling. For example, 1) the contract stated that the cotton and wheat were purchased from the American exchange and were subject to American law, which was clearly different from a normal purchase contract. 2) The rise and fall of the price of the goods was based on the market price of the American exchange. 3) Despite the long-term order, the contract did not specify the period for shipment and arrival, or the quality of the goods. 4) What the buyer paid was not a down payment but a margin. 5) If the price of the goods fell,

an additional margin would have to be added. 6) If the additional margin was not paid, the account would be settled according to the market price. 7) The amount of the loss would also be based on the rise and fall of the market price. 8) The calculation of profits and losses was based on the price in U.S. dollars. 9) The contract contained the phrase "the intention to actually deliver the goods." If the goods were actually delivered upon expiration, why would this footnote be necessary? It was even more evident that it was a cover-up. In addition, two of the three contracts were due in December, while one was due as late as March of this year. However, the plaintiff's settlement was in November, far from the due date. If the defendant asked for the goods upon expiration, how would the plaintiff respond? Therefore, even if the plaintiff wanted to settle the account, it should have been done after the due date. Now the loss being pursued, even if it is not

short selling, is difficult to acknowledge, let alone the fact that it is indeed a gambling act of short selling. This kind of illegal transaction violates our country's mandatory regulations. Since the plaintiff is neither an exchange nor a broker, how can it operate the business of an exchange? Articles 16 and 40 of our country's Exchange Law are very clear. It should be declared that the three contracts in dispute in this case are invalid, etc." The plaintiff's lawyer immediately refuted the defendant's reasons for defense, stating that the defendant's accusation of violating mandatory regulations was a misunderstanding by the defendant, and stated that transactions of the same nature between Chinese and foreign businesses are happening in this city every day, and do not necessarily involve the Exchange Law. The defendant is now using the excuse of short selling to avoid liability for damages because of losses. However, trade always has profits and losses. If a loss is said to be gambling, it is tantamount to deceiving oneself and others. Judge Shen said that this case was quite complicated, and the plaintiff should submit a list of the sale prices of the goods, and then adjourned the hearing for further questioning.

Yang Qingtian's International Spy War, Zhang Zhongshi's American Renaissance Prospects, Yun Dan's American Cultural Decline, Xu Xuehan's Characteristics of China's Financial Panic, Science and Technology aspects, including Er Dan's Airplane Knowledge Q&A, Ming Peng's Weight Reduction Movement in Engineering, De Yuan's Ten Most Needed Inventions, Zhang Wenhui's Electrical Advertising Technique, Shui Jing's Several Simple Physics Experiments, are all major issues that meet the actual needs of the Chinese public's life. The materials are all very new and have an extraordinarily strong interest. This issue also includes two pages of comics, which is a unique creation for semi-monthly publications. The illustrations within the text are also exquisite and precious works. Therefore, although the publication has only been issued for two issues, it has already won the support of the general public because its content is both rich and noble, its interest is very strong, and its mass-market price is far beyond what other publications can achieve. Preliminary Discussion on Amending the Current Trademark Law Xu Chao 179

Introduction, After the National Government promulgated the Trademark Law in May of the 19th year of the Republic of China, the public was confused. The industrial and commercial circles, due to their own vital interests and the special circumstances of our country's society, had to conduct an in-depth review. In November of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the Judicial Yuan explained in a court order that the text used in the trademark in Article 1, Paragraph 2 of the current Trademark Law does not include pronunciation. At that time, public opinion was in an uproar. Those who successively expressed their opinions, such as Chen Xuyuan, Hu Xiyuan, Pan Yang'an, Li Wenjie, Qin Yanzhao, etc., all believed that the defects of the current Trademark Law were even more blatant. In June of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Member Representatives Congress, I, in my capacity as an attending representative, proposed to the Congress to organize a Trademark Law Research Committee, sincerely because the current Trademark Law has been implemented for more than two years, and it is not very suitable for the current situation of industry and commerce. It is urgent to gather leaders from the industrial and commercial circles to contribute opinions to the legislators with the views of the majority. In December of the same year, Director He of the Trademark Bureau, based on his experience in handling cases, published an article entitled "My Humble Opinion on Amending the Current Trademark Law," explaining the shortcomings with righteous words and solemn expressions. We then knew that the legislative authorities did have the determination to amend the current Trademark Law. The Trademark Bureau authorities have already received instructions from the Industrial Department of the Executive Yuan to draft an amendment to the Trademark Law and submit it to the ministry for review. Then, based on our own interests, it is even more urgent to list our opinions. Therefore, we will conduct a separate review as follows: (1) Pronunciation Issues, The text of a trademark was originally registered to highlight the products manufactured by oneself, to develop them, and to hope to obtain the protection of exclusive rights. The so-called "distinctive" is nothing more than to make it easier for buyers to identify them and avoid confusion. If it is really as explained by the Judicial Yuan, then "Ajinomoto" and "Ajijin", "Fish Head" and "Jade Hand" can be registered separately. What is the meaning of the Trademark Law protecting the exclusive right to a trademark? According to the legislative intent, is it like this? However, our country has a vast territory and a large population. Across a mountain or a river, dialects are different. Let alone Beijing and Guangdong, Shanghai and Hankou, commercial ports, and industrial and commercial gatherings, disputes involving trademarks including pronunciation are still difficult to avoid. In my opinion, after amending Paragraph 2 of Article 1 of the current Trademark Law, add a paragraph, "The text used in the trademark includes pronunciation, but it is based on the national pronunciation of each country." (2) Classification Issues, National legislation should first suit national conditions. Our country's industry is backward and has been miserably invaded and oppressed by capitalists for more than a year. The Trademark Law is a law to protect industry, how should it take into account the national economy and have the spirit of encouragement? The current Trademark Law's strict classification is contrary to the principle of protecting industry. Industry is divided into heavy and light industries. The Trademark Bureau is not a tax revenue agency. What is the point of detailed classification? For example, Article 37, Paragraph 1 of the Implementation Rules, in addition to the categories of chemicals, medicines, and western medicines, lists resins, glues, mineral springs, salts, and chemical products, which are no less than thousands of kinds. If they are listed in this way, can they be complete? What is the difference between dyes and pigments in the second item? What is the difference between paint, oil, ink, and coatings? What is the difference between stone or its imitation in Item 12 and stone and artificial stone? How can Item 15 distinguish between glass and its products and glass materials? According to Item 29, linen yarn is classified as one category, and rayon yarn is also classified as one category. Then, cotton yarn and cotton thread in Item 27 and wool yarn and wool thread in Item 28 can be merged. Logically speaking, the capital of heavy industry is larger, and complicated classification is still acceptable. Light industry or even handicrafts have small capital, and detailed classification is overwhelming. How should it be summarized and merged? The responsibility lies with the legislators. Let us try to be aware of the immaturity of domestic industry and the decline of the national economy. If we can expand exclusive rights to similar commodities without being limited to the same commodity, then there will be more opportunities to promote our country's industrial future. (3) Issues of Priority of Use, Our country's Trademark Law adopts the principle of first use. Since its legislation, it has been in effect for many years and still feels suitable for national conditions. However, in the past, our country's merchants had a weaker concept of registration. According to the latest survey, since the establishment of the Trademark Bureau, approximately 20,000 trademark registrations have been made, and Chinese only account for a quarter. The weakness of the concept is self-evident. According to Article 3 of the current Trademark Law, when two or more people apply for registration of the same or similar trademarks for the same commodity, the actual first user shall be allowed to register. Also, according to Article 4 of the same law, when a trademark that has been continuously used in good faith for more than ten years is submitted for registration in accordance with this law, it is not subject to the restrictions of Article 2, Article 6, and Item 3. The good intentions of the latter article are self-evident. However, our countrymen's emphasis on registration should be a fact in recent years. It is difficult to make preferential treatment universal. The history of our country's industry is less than 50 years, while looking around at the developed machinery of various countries, it has reached its peak. Now, with its long history in its own country, it is competing with our country for a day's length. Our harm is endless. Moreover, our countrymen's thinking is not necessarily behind others. The accidental coincidence of trademarks cannot be said to be a rare fact. A fair solution would be to add the seven words "within the Republic of China" to the phrase "actual first user" in the original text of Article 3. (4) Conclusion, There are many people who argue that the current Trademark Law should be amended. In addition to the above three points, the Trademark Bureau's issuance of appraisal certificates is not legally based. If merchants change or add additional notes to registered trademarks to use them for insinuation, the Trademark Bureau may impose a revocation penalty. However, if the Trademark Bureau itself changes or adds additional notes to approved trademarks to insinuate, the Trademark Bureau cannot take action to prohibit them. The urgency of adding clauses to these two points is self-evident. In particular, I have even more to say. According to current practice, when applying for registration of a trademark for a drug, a chemical verification certificate from the Central Health Administration must be attached. If the same trademark is used for hundreds of drugs, it will be necessary to wait until all hundreds of drugs have been verified and certified before the registration can be submitted. The delay in time is secondary. The chemical verification fee for each drug is 25 yuan. Hundreds of drugs require no less than tens of thousands of dollars. A small pharmaceutical merchant will use all of his funds for chemical verification and it will not be enough. How can he register a trademark? Chemical verification of drugs is a way to ban drugs, while trademark registration is to protect the exclusive rights of merchants. How can they be discussed together? For the sake of the future of the national industry and commerce, it is hoped that the administrative authorities will not require chemical verification as a condition for drug registration in order to facilitate the process. Then the future of industry and commerce will be fortunate. In summary, this letter is lengthy and I dare not say that the review is thorough. I am casting a brick to attract jade, and I really hope that there will be virtuous people in the country.

The Ministry of Education Begins Casting Phonetic Type Molds 182

Determined After Surveying Commercial Casting

And Decided on the Principles of Compiling Simplified Characters

(Nanking, 26th) The Ministry of Education convened a meeting on the morning of the 26th to discuss the casting of phonetic type molds and the compilation of a "Simplified Character List." As a result of the discussion, whether the type molds should be cast by the Ministry itself or commercially will be determined after Li Jinxi and Wang Yi go to Shanghai for investigation and submit their findings to the Ministry for approval. The principles of compiling the simplified character list, such as easy to write, easy to recognize, and simple strokes, have been decided upon, totaling five items. Wang and Li are scheduled to go to Shanghai on the afternoon of the 27th.
