Chiang Meng-lin and Liu Chan-en Report on Attending the East Asia Higher Education Conference 185

Report on the Conference and Express Their Thoughts

Chiang Meng-lin and Liu Chan-en reported on their attendance at the East Asia Higher Education Conference, stating: "We respectfully report that the University of the Philippines and the Higher Education Association of the Philippines initiated the East Asia Higher Education Conference to exchange views and strengthen ties, and invited our country to participate. Meng-lin and Chan-en were dispatched by the Ministry to attend the conference. We departed from Shanghai on December 12th of the 23rd year and arrived in Hong Kong. Dr. Chen Jung-chieh, the representative of Lingnan University, boarded the ship and accompanied us. The conference was held from December 18th to 21st for four consecutive days in Manila. In addition to the representatives from our country, there were two representatives from Japan and over a hundred representatives from the Philippines. There were no formal resolutions passed during the conference. The discussions, such as the purpose of universities, curriculum teaching, etc., were mostly related to higher education in the Philippines. However, one group specifically studied international education, emphasizing that the friendship between China and the Philippines is already profound and should be further strengthened. It was hoped that China and the Philippines would exchange faculty and students more frequently in the future to implement cultural exchange. During the general assembly, Meng-lin delivered a speech on 'Higher Education in China,' Chan-en delivered a speech on 'New Trends in Education in China,' and Chen Jung-chieh delivered a speech on 'Education and Humanity.' After the conference, we were invited by Philippine leaders and our overseas Chinese compatriots to visit Iloilo, Baguio, and other places, and were warmly welcomed and entertained by all sectors. We gave over twenty speeches. We left the Philippines and returned to China on January 2nd of this year. We respectfully submit the following brief report on our thoughts on this trip. As for the educational situation, the Philippines has placed great emphasis on education since being governed by Americans for over thirty years. There is one national university on the island, with over six thousand students, six or seven private universities with over ten thousand students, one hundred and twenty middle schools with five thousand eight hundred students, and one thousand five hundred and fifty-five elementary schools with one million one hundred and twenty-one thousand and twenty-eight students. There are one thousand five hundred and forty-one middle school teachers and twenty-four thousand and seventy-six elementary school teachers. With a population of thirteen million, there is one elementary school teacher for every five hundred and thirty-nine residents, and one middle school teacher for every eight thousand five hundred and sixty-five residents. The current system is seven years of elementary school, four years of middle school, and four years of university. Its teaching methods are quite adapted to the needs of individual students and society, with particular emphasis on compulsory education. Every village has at least one school, and the facilities and buildings are in accordance with government regulations and are completely uniform. Two-thirds of school-age children have entered school, so its education is quite widespread. As for its funding, the central government allocates 40% to education, the provinces allocate 40% to 60% to education, and the local governments supplement it with one-third of the total education funding from the central and provincial governments. Because its education funding is abundant, its educational facilities can be actively developed, resulting in today's achievements. (2) As for the government, commerce, and people's lives, the Philippines' politics emphasizes a centralized system. Through years of effort, the United States has approved its full independence after ten years. A constitutional conference is currently being held to prepare for the organization of a new government. Due to the clarity of its politics and the meticulousness of its finances, its commerce is also very developed. The main trades on the island are sugar and coconut oil. A total of 720,000 people in the country are engaged in the sugar industry, with an annual output of 483,025,069 Philippine pesos. 1,147,000 people are engaged in the coconut oil industry, with an annual output of 200,000,000 Philippine pesos. In terms of foreign trade, the surplus in 1929 was 623,214,234 Philippine pesos. Although the world economy was sluggish in 1933, the surplus was still able to maintain 349,466,331 Philippine pesos, so its economic foundation is still solid. The country's income increases annually. In 1918, it was 4,371,338,000 Philippine pesos. In 1926, it was 6,035,152,000 Philippine pesos. In 1933, it was 6,676,876,000 Philippine pesos. As for the people's lives, due to the unique natural advantages and abundant resources, food and fruit are everywhere. With a little effort, they can be well-fed and clothed. Moreover, clothing and housing are simple, so the problem of livelihood is not difficult to solve. Everyone lives and works in peace and contentment, and there is little fear of hunger and cold. (3) The situation of overseas Chinese. There are approximately 100,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines, mostly from Fukien Province, followed by Kwangtung Province. Their history is long, dating back to before the arrival of the Spanish in the Philippines during the Ming Dynasty. They are engaged in commerce, such as food and groceries, and occupy a dominant position locally. The trade with the motherland exports 1,600,000 Philippine pesos and imports 10,000,000 Philippine pesos. In recent years, more enlightened overseas Chinese have paid more attention to the education of their children, and are keen to cultivate specialized commercial talents and improve their commercial knowledge in order to maintain the superior commercial position of overseas Chinese in the Philippines for 300-400 years. However, due to the impact of the world's economic downturn, they are inevitably somewhat financially constrained. It is therefore necessary to guide them according to the situation and strive for unity. The above are rough sketches. In short, the Philippines is a newly emerging country with vigor and vitality, and its future is limitless. The relationship between China and the Philippines is profound and their friendship is strong. In the future, we should strive to be friendly and support each other, thereby establishing a foundation for peace in the Far East and ensuring the lives of more than 100,000 overseas Chinese living there. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Education, Chiang Meng-lin, President of National Peking University, Liu Chan-en, President of Private Shanghai University."

Chen Lifu and Others' Opinions on the Ten Professors' Manifesto 186

Since the Ten Professors' Manifesto was published, many academic leaders and party and government authorities in China have expressed their support. Yesterday, Chen Lifu, a member of the Central Committee, and Luo Tingguang, Dean of the Hupeh Public Education College, Li Denghui, President of Fudan University, and Zheng Zhenduo, Professor of Tsinghua University, also expressed their opinions. They are recorded separately below.

Chen Lifu's Opinion. Chen Lifu, a member of the Central Committee, paid exceptional attention to the Ten Principles. Recently, Chen wrote to a friend, stating, "The construction of a Chinese-based culture has been the proposition he has continued to strive for in the past year. If there is an opportunity in the future, he will strongly promote it to become a new Chinese cultural movement." It is also heard that Chen is currently drafting a lengthy article expressing his views on the construction of a Chinese-based culture.

Luo Tingguang's Opinion. Luo Tingguang, Dean of the Hupeh Public Education College, passed through Shanghai today on his way to Europe to further investigate education. He expressed his support for the Ten Professors' Manifesto, stating, "Cultural construction is extremely important. What I pay most attention to during this overseas investigation is the cultural construction situation in European countries, especially the so-called cultural elements of the United Kingdom, as well as the national characteristics and causes of national revival in continental countries. If I gain any insights in the future, I will contribute them as much as possible for reference."

Li Denghui's Opinion. Li Denghui, President of Fudan University, specifically expressed his opinion on this issue, stating: "To engage sincerely in cultural construction, it is necessary to examine the general trend of the world. The trend of world culture today can be said to be moving towards harmony and mixture, that is, cultures of various nations and countries, as a result of mutual contact, influence each other, modify each other, and supplement each other, gradually producing a new culture with a global nature. The most concrete example is architecture. The architecture of the West in ancient times was already a mixture of various architectures of Greece, Rome, Egypt, and the emerging Nordic peoples. Recently, Chinese and Indian architecture has been harmonized with Western architecture, becoming the most magnificent structure that no single original architecture can match. Just as architecture is like this, all cultures are also like this. When we build a new Chinese culture, we should not pick up the leftovers of other countries, nor should we stick to our own established methods. We must identify the advantages of Western culture and adopt them, and identify the advantages of our old culture and preserve them. When the two sides are brought together and then smelted in one furnace, a brilliant new culture can be produced. Now we are standing at a crossroads. We do not know what to do with the things of others and our own. At one time, we blindly worshiped the West, and at another time, we turned around and excessively exaggerated ourselves, and even abandoned our own essence and picked up the dross of others. These are all very dangerous. Fortunately, in recent years, the Chinese people's ability to discern seems to be improving day by day. I very much hope that the Ten Professors' Manifesto can arouse everyone to conduct more detailed research, analysis, investigation, and comparison, and ultimately be able to select, eliminate, and create a new culture that runs through China and the West. Furthermore, speaking of China's current urgent needs, although everyone attaches great importance to material construction, there is indeed a need to quickly find ways to relieve the people's livelihoods. I also very much agree with this, but I think that spiritual construction is especially important. If material construction is to succeed, it must be presided over by a full spirit. What the Chinese people lack most is enthusiasm. Because without enthusiasm, it is difficult to unite and sacrifice, and the sins of selfishness, cowardice, and corruption are also prone to occur. These are all great enemies of material construction. If these great enemies are not eliminated, then material construction is also very likely to become an opportunity for private enrichment, and most people will still not be able to enjoy happiness. Therefore, promoting inherent morality and the New Life Movement can both be said to be important plans for spiritual construction. However, I personally feel that the power of religion should also be fully utilized to inspire the enthusiasm of the Chinese people."

Zheng Zhenduo's Opinion. Zheng Zhenduo, Professor of Tsinghua University, took the opportunity of his visit to Shanghai to express his support for the Ten Professors' Manifesto, stating, "I think that while cultural issues are indeed important, how the Chinese nation itself can survive is an even bigger issue. If Japan's claws are forever gripping China, China will never have the possibility of revival. The problem now is how to enable China to escape Japan's claws, so the most urgent problem is not the problem of culture, but the problem of survival. We certainly know that we can survive in a bad environment, but how to survive is always a big problem. (Omission) In China's old culture, a way out can never be found. For example, national medicine and national health movements are just acts in the prelude to national subjugation. The survival of the Chinese nation must be entrusted to a new culture and a new organization. How to organize the masses and how to make the masses have a conscious fighting spirit for survival is today's urgent task, while restoring the old culture is a dead end."

The Municipal Education Association Actively Promotes Social Education Undertakings 188

Publishing Citizen Life Aimed at Workers and Shop Assistants

The First People's School Continues to Operate with Huang Chao-hsiung as Principal

Establishing Public Inquiry and Writing Services at the North and South Stations

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association held its fifth board meeting at 2 p.m. yesterday. Those present included Tao Pai-chuan, Huang Chao-hsiung, Weng Chih-lung, Chen Pai, Chen Chi-cheng, and Chang Tsai-po. The chairman was Huang Chao-hsiung, and the recorder was Li Kuang-teng. Matters discussed: (1) Director Tao Pai-chuan proposed that the association plans to publish a Citizen Life weekly magazine. Is it appropriate to request a review? The resolution is as follows: 1. The purpose is to use written education to help the working masses, increase their knowledge, and improve their lives, so as to cultivate them into sound citizens. 2. The format is 16-size four pages, about 6,000 words per issue. 3. The content is divided into columns such as talks, current news, common sense, and literature and art. The text should be as popular as possible and use more illustrations. 4. This publication is aimed at workers and shop assistants. 5. Set up one editor-in-chief and one assistant, to be concurrently held by the association's general secretary and staff member. 6. The initial printing cost is 5,000 copies per issue, with a printing cost of 10 yuan and miscellaneous expenses of 2 yuan, for a total of 60 yuan per month. 7. It is planned to ask the General Labor Union for assistance in publishing. 8. The first issue is scheduled to be published on February 16, and thereafter it will be published every Saturday. (2) How should the People's School continue to operate? The resolution is as follows: 1. The original First School will continue to operate. 2. The principal will be concurrently held by Huang Chao-hsiung, the executive member of the association. 3. The teachers will receive a monthly subsidy of 15 yuan from the association. 4. The school's electricity, miscellaneous expenses, paper, and teacher supplies will be subsidized by a total of 10 yuan. 5. The school's expenses will be allocated from the association's regular expenses. 6. The textbooks used by the students will be purchased and allocated by the association. 7. Day school students shall not be admitted. (3) Director Tao Pai-chuan proposed that it is planned to establish public inquiry and writing service centers at the North Railway Station or South Railway Station. Is it appropriate to request a review? The resolution is as follows: 1. After the location is selected, a small square wooden pavilion will be built (like a police guard booth) for office use. 2. Hire one staff member with a monthly salary tentatively set at 20 yuan and find someone with aspirations to fill the position. 3. The rules for the office will be drafted by the Promotion Section. (4) Director Tao Pai-chuan proposed that it is planned to establish a public reading room in Chapei to also handle public inquiry and writing matters. Is it appropriate to request a review? The resolution is as follows: 1. The name will be the Shanghai Municipal Education Association Public Reading Room. 2. The location is planned to be in the Hengfeng Road or Tatung Road area of Chapei. 3. Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Environment and Influence 202

— Zhang Muliang

We must always avoid all kinds of bad environments, so that we will not be subject to all kinds of bad influences. But avoiding all kinds of bad environments is not an easy thing. We heard Mozi say: "Dyed in blue, it is blue; dyed in yellow, it is yellow." Isn't his intention the same as "Accustomed to good, it is good; accustomed to evil, it is evil"? This proves that the goodness or badness of our environment lies in how we do things on weekdays.

If we are in a dark and filthy environment, over time, we will inevitably become degenerate. In other words, if we are in a bright and noble environment, over time, we will naturally be influenced and subtly assimilated. Now, I can use an example to prove this:

During the Warring States period, Mencius was once in a bad environment in his childhood. When his mother lived next to the cemetery, he liked to do things like building tombs. Later, when he moved next to the market, he liked to do things like selling goods. This was because Mencius was in a bad environment and was thus negatively influenced. Therefore, Mencius' mother became very worried and decided to move next to the school palace. Mencius then spent his days setting up ritual vessels and practicing etiquette, gradually getting on the right track. This was because Mencius was in a good environment and was thus positively influenced. In short, the magic of the environment greatly affects people's tendencies.

Dear children! No matter what, you must get out of the dark and filthy environment and go into the bright and noble environment, so that you will not be negatively influenced.

Lunar and Solar Calendars 203

— Bing Yu

Since Julius Caesar formulated the calendar in 46 BC, the day of the winter solstice, when the sun returns, has been the beginning of the year, which is January 1, used worldwide today. The Julian calendar takes the month of the winter solstice as January, but people often confuse it with the ancient winter solstice, New Year, and the anniversary of Christ's birth (December 25). As for the old calendar used in our country, it originated in the Xia Dynasty and is also called the Xia calendar. Because in the agricultural era, agriculture was the most important thing, the year's harvest was over, and spring and winter were divided according to the solar terms. If you look at it according to the current Gregorian calendar, it is indeed not suitable for the relationship with agricultural affairs. Therefore, most rural areas in Japan still use the lunar calendar. Although urban agencies follow the Gregorian calendar, it is only regarded as a memorial festival, which commemorates the significance of the founding of the country. In other coastal areas, the rise and fall of tides often coincide with the new and full moon of the lunar calendar, so it is more convenient to use the lunar calendar. However, the dates of the lunar calendar are easy to calculate incorrectly. Even the calculation method of the lunar age under the decimal point is different. Moreover, it only counts the days according to the waxing and waning of the moon, from new moon to new moon, from full moon to full moon, using a purely lunar calendar completely, and without considering the operation of the sun, it is inevitable that there will be differences in the seasons. Therefore, India and Japan used the lunisolar calendar to avoid seasonal errors. The method of determining the seasons in the lunar calendar is based on the waxing and waning of the moon, determining the new and full moon, with 30 days for a large month and 29 days for a small month. The winter solstice is in November, the vernal equinox is in February, the summer solstice is in May, and the autumnal equinox is in August. An intercalary month is placed in a month that does not contain the central solar term. Japan used this method to compile the calendar in the past. After the fifth year of Meiji, the Gregorian calendar was adopted. However, more than 60 years have passed, and the people in the rural areas of the country still stick to the old rules and celebrate the New Year according to the lunar calendar. This is because half of it is constrained by customs, but it is also because the season and agriculture are related and cannot be helped.

Plants and Animals 205

— Zhen

Children! Do you know that all objects in the natural world can be divided into two major categories: living organisms and non-living organisms. Humans, horses, peaches, and plums are living organisms. Mountains, iron, stone, and soil are non-living organisms.

Living organisms can be further divided into plants and animals. Humans and plums, dogs and pines, who are animals and who are plants? There are very obvious differences:

1. Cell Structure: A cell is the smallest unit that makes up the body of a living organism. If the cell membrane wrapped outside the cell is made of fiber, it is a plant. Otherwise, it is an animal.

2. Method of Nutrition: Plants have green chlorophyll and rely on sunlight. The function of extracting nutrients from water and carbonic acid gas is that of a plant. Otherwise, it is an animal. In short, plants absorb inorganic matter. Animals absorb organic matter.

3. Ability to Move: Plants absorb inorganic matter, which is everywhere, so they do not need to move their bodies. Animals absorb organic matter, so they must search for it, so they have to move.

4. Ability to Feel: Plants do not have nerves, so there is no significant response when you touch them. Animal nerves are very sensitive. If you hit a dog, it will definitely run away quickly.

There are more than 233,000 species of plants. They can be divided into two major categories:

1. Phanerogams (flowering): like plums and peaches.

2. Cryptogams (non-flowering): like bacteria.

Animals can be divided into ten categories:

1. Vertebrates: humans, etc.

2. Arthropods: shrimp, etc.

3. Mollusks: clams, etc.

4. Echinoderms: sea cucumbers, etc.

5. Annelids: earthworms, etc.

6. Nematodes: roundworms, etc.

7. Platyhelminthes: tapeworms, etc.

8. Coelenterates: hydras, etc.

9. Sponges: sponges, etc.

10. Protozoa: small animals under the microscope

Shadowing Game 210

— Qian Chuo Hengjiu

Children! When you are at home or at school, you must have many good friends, right? I think you must not want to leave your good friends, but what method can make them stay with you forever? There is one! Please see the shadowing game below!

First, we use thumbtacks to nail a piece of black waxed paper to a flat wall (with the black side facing inward). Place a seat near the wall and call your friend to sit on it. Place a lamp on the table next to the seat so that the shadow of your friend's head falls exactly on the paper. Then use a pencil to outline the contour of the shadow, cut it out, and paste it on white paper (with the black side facing outward). Isn't that a photograph of your good friend? Can't he live with you forever?

There are four points to pay attention to in this game: 1) Your friend's shadow must show the side shape, because if it is the front shape, it will be difficult to recognize who it is. 2) When you outline the contour for your friend, please ask your friend not to move, otherwise the drawing will be spoiled. 3) The lamp on the table and the light should allow him to stay still. 4) It is best to do this game at night, because the shadow may not be clear during the day.

One day, a woodcutter frantically called for help in a trap. After being heard by pedestrians, they immediately summoned several people to rescue him, but his leg had been injured by the medicine arrow. Fortunately, the injury was not serious, and the hunters each took out secret medicines to heal him. After bandaging the wound, they asked the woodcutter how he had fallen into the trap by mistake. Wasn't a warning posted near the mountain?

The woodcutter said: "I only saw many red posters, but I didn't know that you had made a trap to trap tigers?"

The hunter asked in surprise: "How? You saw the red posters but didn't know there was a trap? Don't you know how to read?"

"Yes! I am illiterate, so I was injured today!" the woodcutter said with great regret.

Dear friends! After reading the news above, do you feel the pain of illiterate people? There are many people like the woodcutter in China! I hope you study hard at school! Be serious! If you encounter elderly people who have dropped out of school, quickly persuade them to go to a nearby community school to learn to read!

Scary Ants 211

— Little Franklin

Children! When you read this topic, you may be surprised. What's so scary about ants? But, children, please don't rush, let me tell you about it.

In Africa, there is a kind of ant that is different from the ants we usually see. This kind of ant is three inches long and very strong. Their residence looks like a pagoda, twice as tall as a person, and is made entirely of mud very carefully. Whenever they come out to look for food, there are always thousands or tens of thousands of them, like a disciplined army. If they encounter large animals (such as lions, tigers, etc.) on the way, they will also rush up together, climb on the animal's body and bite it until the animal dies, and then divide it and transport it to the pagoda residence. Therefore, people in Africa are very afraid of these ants!

Dear children, you see, as long as many small ants have the power of unity, they are not afraid of anything. China has such a large population and such a large area, why is it not as good as even small Japan? Children! What is China lacking?

How Snow is Formed 213

— Yang Xiying

Little friends! We all know that when the weather gets cold, it will snow. But do you know how snow is actually formed? I'm afraid very few of you little friends know the answer to this question. Now I will write the answer simply below:

When the weather is cold, the water vapor originally in the atmosphere encounters cold, and the temperature continuously decreases, dropping to below zero degrees Celsius. The water vapor slowly condenses into small, solid, hexagonal crystalline flakes, which fall from the sky to the ground. We call this thing "snow." Its shapes are all different. Although it can be seen with the naked eye, it is very blurry. If we take a microscope to observe it carefully, we can see many different shapes, which are extraordinarily beautiful. This kind of natural beauty can truly amaze us. Its color is colorless and transparent. Looking from all aspects of the crystal, there are reflected light rays, so after it snows, the outside is particularly bright. This is the reason why.

The Heavenly God is about to send down snow, little friends! Let's all observe it!

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (Part 4) 214

— Xin Qing

I didn't know how long I had slept, but when I woke up, the ship was gone. I could see it sailing away, its sails full, far in the distance. I knew that no matter how hard I shouted, the sailors wouldn't be able to hear me. I thought about my sorrowful situation and cried. For a long time, I didn't know what to do.

I was so sorrowful that I was almost going crazy. I thought to myself that if I had put aside the thought of greed for gold and not made this return voyage, I wouldn't have ended up in this situation. Of course, this kind of thinking was too late. I told myself that what I should do was to find a way to get myself out of this sorrowful situation.

Immediately, I saw a tree. In a little while, I was sitting high in the middle of the tree branches. From my hiding place, I could see a beautiful view. On one side, there was nothing to see but the sea and the sky.

When I turned my eyes to look at the land, I saw what I thought was a very large white ball in a place far away from me. Because it was too far away, I couldn't tell what it was. So I climbed down from the tree and ran forward to see what it was.

Before long, I had approached this strange thing and could put my hand on it. It felt very smooth. I walked around it several times, but I couldn't figure out what it was. This big white ball was more than forty and a half yards in circumference and also extremely high.

Although I walked around it several times as I said above, I still couldn't think of a way to get inside. I thought, "Maybe if I climb to the top, I can find a way in." But the thing was so high and so smooth. I couldn't climb up at all.

I was standing there when the sky suddenly became as dark as night. The reason for this was a huge bird. Its wings were so large that they blocked the sunlight.

Then I knew that this bird must be a roc, an Arabian giant bird, because I had heard stories about these giant birds before. What I thought was a big white ball was the egg of this giant bird. It had flown down and was sitting on the egg, incubating it!

Once I understood its plan, I went up and got close to the egg. When I sat down, I was close to one of the bird's legs. This leg must have been as thick as a tree trunk. Immediately, I tied myself to that leg with a piece of cloth I had with me. I hoped that when it flew away the next day, it would take me back with it.

Finally, the night was over. At dawn, the roc flew away with me. We rose higher and higher, and finally the land disappeared.

Finance 215

The Gold Standard Unit Continues to Fall Sharply, Selling Pressure in the Gold Market Intensifies

A Rise and Fall of Two and a Half Yuan in Half a Day

Resulting in a Decline of Three Yuan and One Jiao

The gold market yesterday was triggered by the Central Bank's Customs Gold Unit exchange rate, which suddenly fell by 1.3%, stimulating selling pressure and causing a drop. The foreign exchange market was also affected by the money market conditions, which were loose in the near term but tight in the long term. However, because buyers maintained support at lower prices, the situation stabilized after the initial decline. Trading in the market was quiet, with both buyers and sellers mostly taking a wait-and-see approach, resulting in an extremely calm market situation in the morning, with only a rise and fall of 2.5 yuan. It was observed that early in the morning, overseas gold and silver markets were flat in both England and the United States, the forward silver price in Montreux slightly contracted, the exchange rate also contracted, and the London spot gold price slightly rose by half a penny. However, the French franc remained weak, and over-the-counter preparatory trading was mediocre, opening at around 62 yuan. Later, when the Central Bank's exchange rate was announced, the British pound rose by 1.25, the US dollar rose by 1.875, and the Customs Gold Unit fell by 1.3%, the standard gold price retreated to 973.4 yuan, stimulating selling pressure, which immediately retreated into the 60-yuan range. After opening, the situation remained relatively stable. However, due to the banks' appetite becoming constricted and the money market tightening, the process of recent foreign exchange drafts became unusually tight and fell. Although buyers came to maintain support, because it was known in advance that HSBC's exchange rate would be 1.25 higher for the British pound and 1.875 higher for the US dollar, retail investor sentiment was downward. In addition, Sassoon & Co. also came to aggressively sell shillings, ultimately making it difficult to maintain support and causing a temporary decline. However, due to buyers' activity at lower prices and the continued difficulty in settling forward exchange drafts, the situation gradually rebounded as short positions were covered. The announcement of the silver equalization tax remained unchanged, still levied at 6%, calculated at 1 shilling, 5 pence, and 78125. Subsequently, the demand side became more active, and the price once became firm. Banks took advantage of the high price to sell, which further fueled selling pressure. Short positions slightly increased their bets, and the price became weak again. Thereafter, trading became sporadic. Although short positions were covered, there was still a supply of gold, so the price fluctuated around 8 yuan for a very long time. Later, retail investors pushed up the price, and short positions closed out some of their positions, causing another rise. However, the rise was only temporary, and the supply of gold at high prices was again abundant, causing the price to rise and then fall again. The final state was even more stagnant, with no special changes. The swap spread had risen to more than 10 yuan, and buyers were extremely distressed. The market situation for the morning is recorded below:

The opening price in the morning was 989.5 yuan, a decrease of 1.4 yuan compared to the previous closing price. Hengyu Qianchang Xiangjin's contracts once rose to 9 yuan and 8 jiao, but because Tongfu Fuxing Yong sold contracts, they struggled, hovering around 9 yuan and 5 jiao. Citibank sold February US dollars at 0.0625 and spot US dollars at 0.06875. Hengchang Yong Hengyu Tongtaichang Dadecheng Fuxing Yong and others hastily sold, retreating to 8 yuan and 5 jiao. Dadecheng and Yuan Maoyong bought contracts at low prices. However, because Ruixing Dachang Xiang Hengyu Yuli retail investors all sold, knowing in advance that HSBC's exchange rate would be 1.25 higher for the British pound and 1.875 higher for the US dollar, the price retreated to 8 yuan. Hengyu Tianfeng Tongyu Run Yongli Yongde Shenkang bought contracts at low prices, gradually rising to 9 yuan and 1 jiao. Dachang Xiang Fuyu Shenkang Dingkang Dingtai Zhaofengchang and others hastily sold, retreating to 8 yuan. However, because Xiangfeng Qingfa Yongda Fayong Yuan Yiyuanchang Yong and others limited their purchases, they struggled. Retail investors pressed prices very hard. Hengyu Fuxing Yong Fuyu Jinlong and others sold. Sassoon aggressively sold shillings non-stop, so the price fell to 7 yuan and 3 jiao. Retail investors and Hengyu bought contracts at low prices. At this time, because Dingkang Fuxing Yong and others were still selling, there was still some struggle. Afterwards, Hengyu Zhaofengchang Dadecheng Houchang Yong Dingchang and others all bought, gradually rising. The silver equalization tax announcement remained unchanged. At this time, the price once rose to 9 yuan. The Dalian gang and Yuan Maoyong sold at high prices, retreating to 8 yuan and 1 jiao. Mitsui bought spot US dollars at 0.08125, but forward US dollars were still difficult to buy. Hengyu Changda came to buy, rising to 9 yuan and 2 jiao. HSBC sold March US dollars at 0.0875. Although Shenkang and Dadecheng Hengyu sold, with retail investors maintaining support, the market price was held at around 8 yuan. Later, because retail investors raised prices, Richang Qianchang Xiang Dafayong Changdashengda and others jointly bought, making trading even quieter. The price once rebounded to 9 yuan and 1 jiao. Hengyu Tiancheng Xiang Yuxin Xiang and others hastily sold, retreating to 7 yuan and 6 jiao. Zhaofengchang and Dadecheng slightly bought at low prices, rising to 8 yuan and 1 jiao. After fluctuating, the closing price at noon was 957.8 yuan. It was observed that the highest price of the day was 959.8 yuan, and the lowest price was 957.3 yuan, a rise and fall of only 2.5 yuan. As a result, the price decreased by 3.1 yuan compared to the previous closing.

The closing price was announced with the Central Bank's standard gold price retreating to 973.4 yuan. According to the closing price, it was pressed down by about 15 yuan, a decrease of about 4 yuan compared to the previous closing. The registered price for February was 951 yuan, and for March, it was 958 yuan. The supplemental water in the morning was 941 yuan. Tianjin goods were priced 1 yuan higher according to the forward price, but there was also a lack of transactions. The main reason was that after the decline in the standard gold price, the merchant groups lacked the appetite to sell, and the swap spread was even higher. Fuchang paid 9 yuan and 8 jiao to Fu'an for 49 contracts, 10 yuan for 28 contracts to Jiatai, 10 yuan for 21 contracts to Dada, and 10 yuan for 14 contracts to Yuan Maoyong. All were paid by Fu'an. Trading in the market was slow. In summary, Yifeng Yong Qingfa Yong Dingchang Yongde Tianfeng Yicheng Dafayong Yuqing Yong Juchang and others were on the buying side. Money Market Conditions: Foreign Exchange Market Tightens in the Long Term, Loosens in the Short Term 216

Banks and Sassoon Selling

Resulting in Firming of Both British Pound and US Dollar

According to foreign dispatches yesterday, the London big market was flat in both the near and far terms, the New York silver price did not move, the Montreux forward silver price slightly decreased, the London spot gold price increased by half a penny, the British pound against the US dollar contracted by 0.0075, the British pound against the French franc increased by 6 pounds, the US dollar against the British pound decreased by 0.0075, and the US dollar against the French franc contracted by 0.0125. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the asking price for the near term: the British pound at 1 shilling, 5 pence and a half, and the US dollar at 35 and a half yuan. Compared with the previous closing, the British pound loosened by 0.000625, while the US dollar was flat. The Central Bank's exchange rate announcement was 1.25 higher for the British pound and 1.875 higher for the US dollar, and the Customs Gold Unit decreased by 0.013. The sentiment of Chinese merchants turned fearful. After opening, banks had a selling appetite again, and the process became loose. The HSBC exchange rate announcement was 1.25 higher for the British pound and 1.875 higher for the US dollar. Thereafter, Sassoon came to aggressively sell shillings, and the situation became even looser. However, the far term was tight, so Chinese merchants and the Dalian gang still had a buying appetite. The silver equalization tax announcement did not move. Thereafter, it presented a phenomenon of being loose in the near term and tight in the long term. The overall trend was mediocre. Although banks took advantage of the high price to sell, maintainers were still abundant. There were no special changes thereafter. Extending to the noon closing, the asking price for the near term was: the British pound at 1 shilling, 5 pence and 0.0005625, and the US dollar at 35 yuan and 0.06875. Compared with the previous closing, the British pound loosened by 0.00125, and the US dollar firmed by 0.01875. With the settlement period approaching and tight money market conditions, the foreign exchange market again presented a phenomenon of being loose in the near term and tight in the long term. New York Stock Market Stagnant but Firm 220

Xinfeng Foreign Company reported that yesterday (25th) the New York stock market was extremely sluggish but still firm. This was because the United Corporation's preferred stock and other public utility stocks were quite outstanding and brought the market up. However, the public utility enterprises themselves had no concrete developments. It was only because the buyers believed that the current unstable situation of the industry would soon be eliminated. Brokers paid close attention to this situation. Several people said that if the public utility stocks could truly rebound, it would be quite beneficial to the overall stock market. However, the rest believed that there were still many hidden reefs in the future of public utility enterprises. Although electricity consumption reached the highest record in four years, the profits of the companies were reduced instead. Therefore, they were mostly skeptical about the possibility of a rebound. After the stock market closed, General Motors Company announced that the company's profits last year totaled 85,591,000 yuan, that is, a profit of 1.91 yuan per share. The bond market tended to rise, especially public utility bonds. The stocks on the small exchange had mixed ups and downs, with no significant differences. Zheng Biao Quietly Listless. At the opening of the forward flower market, all contract months showed signs of weakness. Yesterday, at the opening of the US cotton market, due to the end of the January contract and selling by spot traders, the market was flat and weak, with each month falling by six to eight points. US Cotton Awaits Development of Gold Bar Case 226

A telegram from New York on the 25th reports on the cotton market for the week: At the beginning of the week, the Supreme Court failed to make a ruling on the gold bar case, causing disappointment among cotton sellers. However, their supply was absorbed by domestic and foreign traders, so the market was firmer afterwards. This was due to frost damage in the Indian cotton region and private estimates of a reduction in the Indian cotton harvest. Ordinary transactions were extremely quiet, and traders were waiting for the enactment of the gold bar case. Legislative discussions are underway regarding changes to or extensions of the cotton mortgage deadline. Generally, people are waiting for an indication from the authorities regarding the next season's cotton production mortgage. It is reported that Mr. Mills, Chairman of the Senate Agriculture Committee, will convene a meeting of New York Cotton Exchange brokers in mid-February to change futures contracts and operating rules. The low average temperatures in the South are sufficient to reduce insect damage. However, people in the industry have preconceived notions due to the uncertain situation in Washington. Regarding the beginning of the cotton production situation, they are paying close attention. The attached US cotton weekend statistics are as follows (unit: thousands of bales):

Grains

Factories Continue to Order Foreign Wheat Saying Flour Market Afternoon Dumping Arises Suddenly 227

Yesterday, in the flour market, after the opening in the morning, the prices of various months showed a trend of first stabilizing and then falling. According to foreign wheat quotes, Chicago rose by 2.0 angle and Canada rose by about 4.0 fen. When prices were quoted, this month, since there was only one day of trading, both internal and external buyers and sellers were liquidating step by step, so the market atmosphere fluctuated and there was not much change. Transactions for far-term months were still smooth, with outsiders buying in and floating shorts covering positions, so the market atmosphere remained stable. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, the market turned weak again. Many holders of the current month were liquidating, and prices gradually loosened. In the far term, it was reported that factories continued to order a ship of foreign wheat at a price of 4 yuan, 7 jiao, and 3 fen, or 7 jiao. However, whether the transaction was concluded has not yet been determined. Nevertheless, the market sentiment has weakened as a result, and with a surge of dumping, prices fell by more than 1 fen. Observing the situation, with the continued conclusion of foreign wheat transactions, the market may show a declining trend during the opening of the Spring Festival. As a result, the current month fell by 1 fen and 7.5 li, February fell by 2 fen and 2.5 li, March fell by 1.5 fen, April and May fell by 1 fen and 2.5 li, and June fell by 1 fen and 2.5 li.

Overseas wheat, winter wheat areas are experiencing severe cold weather with thin snow cover, causing some buying. However, the situation in Canada remains the main factor hindering the market.

Foreign Ke Xian Rice Prices Increase Step by Step 228

Yesterday, the foreign rice market showed a very strong trend. Foreign quotations have not fallen, and hoarders are particularly firm in their intentions. Therefore, futures prices were called up by 3-5 fen before transactions occurred. The domestic market for spot foreign rice is already weak, but cargo owners are also unwilling to lightly release their holdings with the market. Therefore, the entire market only opened one lot of 500 bales of Saigon rice, and the market situation remained unchanged. Futures opened 1,600 tons of Saigon rice to be loaded for road transport in February and March, and 50 tons of Siamese broken rice for road transport, all handled by this street. The arrival and inventory of Ke Xian rice were both low. Yesterday, 664 bales of Xiang rice were handled by inland areas such as Nanjing, and the price continued to rise by 2-3 fen. Although the inventory of foreign rice is sufficient, they are all unwilling to sell. Arrivals are also continuous. Yesterday, another 18,000 bales of Siamese rice arrived at the port.

River Rice Arrival Turns Active Suddenly Hogshead Price Plunges 2-3 Jiao 229

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the sources from various gangs suddenly turned active again, with a total of more than 60 numbers (more than 10,000 shi of goods). As the final closing period approaches, the sales market is particularly sluggish. Therefore, the appetite of this street is stagnant, and very few goods are being transacted. Although there are also inquiries, they are extremely harsh on the issue of eating the market, and the customer's share is only from the Qingdao gang, slightly handling 7-800 bales. As a result, a trend of frequent declines has emerged. In addition to the sharp decline of 2-3 jiao in the price of various thick japonica rice, other late rice varieties are also difficult to recover, and have seen declines of 1-2 jiao. Fortunately, the limited supply of Du Jian rice has been able to hold its ground, with no great honor or disgrace. Yin Bian Yuan, due to oversupply, has fallen by more than one jiao.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, the inner rivers from various ports downstream of the river were still not open, so there were only twelve number one arrivals. Various buyers in the market bought japonica rice. Bian Yuan continued to melt, and Yang Du was stagnant. Early indica rice was active. Market price White japonica rice was slightly tight. Bian Yuan was firm, and Yang Du showed a sluggish trend, similar to early thin rice. The remaining goods were settled.

Furthermore, the rice merchants' associations in the North and South markets have jointly decided that due to the approach of the end of the old lunar year, all accounts will be closed. Therefore, they have specifically decided to close on the 28th of the Gregorian calendar.

Soybean Outlets Are Only Sporadic 230

Yesterday, the soybean market slightly softened, but in this closing period, it should not affect the overall situation. Statistics show that there were very few transactions. It is estimated that factories handled 600 bales of Guide soybeans at a price of 3 yuan and 8 jiao, a decrease of 5 fen compared to the previous market price. This street purchased 200 bales of Hankou Zha soybeans at a price of 3 yuan and 8 jiao, and 100 bales of Shashi soybeans at a price of 3 yuan and 6 jiao. Domestic inquiries for Dangshan soybeans totaled 200 bales at a price of more than 3 yuan and 8 jiao. The market price has been slightly adjusted by 1-2 fen.

With Year-End Closing Approaching, Sugar Market Is Quiet 231

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was flat and weak, and trading remained low. The guild's pricing of spot 24 coarse sugar was generally called at 18 yuan and 5 fen, but no transaction was made. Some cargo from this store was slightly sold out at a price of 18 yuan and 1 jiao. Dutch red and Taikoo sugar were not transacted. The original price of cotton white from this factory had a slight transaction. The plate number had the Chao gang opening a price of 10 yuan and 1 jiao to 10 yuan for Huanggang green, and 9 yuan and 8 jiao for the second grade, and 9 yuan and 6 jiao for Longgang green. The rest was not continued.

North-South Goods, Fungus Suddenly Rises 3-4 Yuan 232

The current Han market for fungus is gradually rising. The handling price for, for example, Yan fungus has already reached 90 yuan, and Xing'an fungus also requires 88 yuan. The price of Sichuan fungus here has been over 102 yuan. Although sales are not strong at the time of this major closing, the upward trend is still strong. For example, the market price of the Ding Sheng Hao Airlines brand small package fungus is sold to 100 yuan, high-grade fungus is 94-95 yuan, and Yichang fungus is 85-86 yuan, an increase of 3-4 yuan compared to the previous price.
