Women's Corner

Eulogy for a Chaste Widow 251

— Zi

At the end of last year, there was the "Chaste Widow Banquet" in Da Luo Village, Guangdong. At the beginning of this year, there was the expulsion of a "Remarried Woman" in Qingdao City. The Qingdao newspaper reported on the 22nd... Because Wei Wenxiu, the concubine of the late President Li, married the merchant Wang Kuixuan in Qingdao, which tarnished the reputation of the Li family... Expulsion from the country... The feudal atmosphere permeates the north and the south, truly "how magnificent!"

If Qingdao is said to be clean and cannot keep remarried women, Wei Wenxiu, although remarried, is still a clean and upright Chinese citizen. Because a widow's remarriage is already legally recognized in the Republic of China, and in the past, Wei was President Li's concubine. In law, the existence of concubines is no longer explicitly recognized, and this time marrying Mr. Wang is instead legitimate and justified. Qingdao is a small place, harboring many non-Chinese who openly rob and secretly plot against us, yet it cannot keep a weak woman who has been bullied? In a letter to a friend, Wei said: "Now that President Li's bones are not yet cold, and his descendants cannot tolerate me, if I do not seek my own support, how can I survive?"

The world crisis is becoming more urgent day by day. Some countries are working together to build internally and strengthen national defense externally. Some countries are manufacturing poison gas, germ bombs, death rays... preparing for a mass slaughter. In addition to uniting and resisting for a long time, we China are adding the promotion of women's chastity. In the future, we can raise a large number of martyrs and chaste women... One cry will make the enemy retreat, and another cry will bring world peace. We wish feudalism victory! May the goddess of chastity be victorious!

Hair 252

— Chen Yan

Hair on a person's body is inherently the least useful thing, but China has an ancient saying: "Our body, hair, and skin are received from our parents, and we dare not damage them." Therefore, although after the Xinhai Revolution, the whole country was ordered to cut off pigtails (only men, not women), there were indeed many pedantic people who considered dragging a tail to be fulfilling their filial piety. However, the cleanliness and convenience after cutting it off, as well as the world trend, finally overcame the ancient saying. Now, if a man still drags a pigtail and walks around the streets, everyone will laugh at him as a moldy antique.

The most original meaning of cutting hair is temporarily impossible to trace, but it must have been for cleanliness and convenience. Now, among men in various countries around the world, apart from Indians who still like to pile it on top of their heads like cow dung, there are probably very few who keep this troublesome thing. However, women are an exception.

The popularity of women cutting their hair has only been in recent years. During the European War, European women, because they participated in various jobs, felt the trouble and burden of combing hair into buns and braids, and naturally cut it off. It became a global trend for a time, and soon spread to China. At that time, the warlords were arresting revolutionary parties, and at one point, women with short hair were all considered to be revolutionary parties, and a large search was carried out. Fortunately, the revolution was soon successful (?). Women cutting or keeping their hair became a personal freedom!

Recently, Chairman Chiang issued an order prohibiting soldiers from marrying women without hair buns. After this order is implemented, women with short hair have indeed lost the qualification to marry soldiers, but as long as she does not let her hair down or perm it, she is still a law-abiding female citizen.

However, it is said that several female leaders in Shanghai have stated that as a result of cutting their hair for several years, in terms of economics, time, and other aspects, there has been no benefit compared to when they had hair buns. From now on, they will no longer cut their hair and will restore hair buns. According to the person in charge of the female student organizations in various schools in Shanghai, the female students have organized the Hair-Growing Alliance (excerpted from the Zhonghua Daily on the 23rd of this month).

Whether this news is true is unknown. As a rule, cutting hair can save gold hairpins and silver hair ornaments, which is economical; it is not necessary to spend every morning tidying up long black hair, which saves time; it is also easier to wash and more hygienic; men cut their hair, women also cut their hair, which is equal. Therefore, since the Northern Expedition in 1927, women everywhere, with the exception of a very small number, have cut their hair. If it is said that perming hair is uneconomical, and letting hair down is unsightly, one can simply not perm or let it down - in fact, it is the idlers who are uneconomical. If she does not perm her hair, she will have other new developments. As for beauty, there is no fixed standard - so, what is the purpose of restoring hair buns and the Hair-Growing Alliance? Is it because there are many Chinese male soldiers, so if they don't do this, "they are afraid they will have difficulty finding a mate"?

Cursing and Love 253

— Guan Lu

There is a very common way to curse people in China, which is to start by saying "His mother's" something something: "His mother's" is just the most common and easy way to curse people, and naturally there are many similar ways to curse, and according to the different dialects in the north and south, the words used are also different, but we can summarize them into a system: that is, one of the most common ways to curse people in China is to use "sex" as the object.

This habit of using "sex" as the object of cursing is probably not only limited to China. It has also existed in foreign countries. Russian novels can be found in many dialogues (of course, other countries are rare), but this way of cursing is most popular, applied most skillfully, and most universally. When two couples, two brothers, or even two fathers and sons break out in cursing each other, they will generally choose one or several of "His mother's," "Dog X's," "Screw your..." etc., as the most satisfying, thorough, and refreshing and liberating expressions! In short, as long as sex is used as the object and weapon of cursing, mothers, sisters; six relatives, nine clans; ancestors, eight generations, can all be dragged in to insult the other party.

Why is this custom so prevalent in China? Naturally, this consciousness of cursing people with "sexual" relations is the consciousness of despising women; the stronger the feudal forces, the more intense the consciousness of despising women.

Originally, in the feudal system, everything of women was in a subordinate position. In the relationship between men and women, women were also absolutely subordinate and passive. The feudal system blocked all freedom for women, and even in natural physiological sexual life, women were not free. Men could freely look for wives, but if a woman took the initiative to find a man, this would be considered a "great shame" and "a violation of morality." A man could marry several times in his life and approach several women, but a woman had to be faithful to one man to the end, and had to have the virtue of chastity. If a woman had a relationship with more than two men, this was a disgrace, a loss of status, a loss. In short, a woman, apart from that one marriage specified by her parents, should avoid male-female relationships and should adopt an absolutely passive attitude. Otherwise, she is a promiscuous woman.

Feudal society has such a golden rule for male-female relationships, engraved in the classics for women. Then, if a man intends to insult a woman, he can insult her through "sex"; slander and defamation can also be developed from "sex." Therefore, when cursing, if the other party is a woman, she can be directly insulted; if the other party is a man, one can start with his mother, sisters, nine relatives, six relatives! The yin side!

This custom of cursing can be said to come on the one hand from certain social concepts of men and women, and at the same time, this custom can express a certain male perspective in society. Of course, the remnants of a habit cannot be immediately eradicated even after the entire consciousness of that society has changed. However, this habit of cursing is not a remnant in the general habits of China today, but is very prevalent and very "popular."

Now it can be said that the historical concepts of Chinese feudal society towards women, attached to this artistic form of cursing, are built on a very solid "Twenty-Four Bridges," and have been gently carried over from the era of feudal monarchs to the present.

Let's look at the relationship between men and women in Chinese society today, starting from the starting point of "sex," and see what attitude society today holds towards women. Then we will know that this cursing that uses "sex" as the object is by no means an accidental matter. At the same time, from this point, we are very intimately linked to the most realistic and most concerned so-called problems of "marriage" and "love."

People with a slightly more progressive mindset understand that "marriage" should be autonomous and "love" should be free. However, in the process from starting love to reaching marriage, in terms of art and technology, it should generally be initiated by men. It is free for a man to want to talk to a woman about love, and it is also free for a man to propose to a woman; but if a woman takes the initiative to talk to a man about love and expresses her love for him first, this is very unskillful and unartistic. The other party will probably despise her, reject her, and she will encounter failure as a result. Even if this woman is not rejected by the other party, it seems to others that this woman is also not very "decent"! Also: If a man attacks a woman and is rejected, he can still perform for others; but if a woman expresses her love for a man and is spurned, this is truly a "great shame" for the woman!

Based on the above many facts, although today's society is not like feudal times, which used explicit canons to stipulate women under the "Three Obediences" and does not regard women as those who should "follow one man to the end" and be servants of their husbands; but under the slogans of "autonomous marriage" and "free love," what have women gained? The "sexual" relationship is secret and passive for women, and is only an obligation without rights. In the freedom of love, women only have the freedom to be acted upon, not the freedom to act. A woman who has gone through a divorce even causes others to feel the need to consider when dating her, which of course proves the health of feudal consciousness in Chinese society today!

My intention, of course, is not to prepare to do this kind of women's work: to unite and mobilize many young women to attack and surround men, and to open a large love training institute. My intention is: as long as it is not "parents' orders" and "matchmakers' words," marriage is based on mutual willingness, and love is also based on mutual willingness, not one-sided willingness. In the relationship between men and women, there should be no division between initiative and passivity, no stipulations of master and servant, and the subordinate status of women must be abolished.

The custom of cursing "His mother's" and the old male-female relationship that sacrifices women are a fire snake, locked by an iron chain; if you feel that the phrase "His mother's" sounds unpleasant, then naturally you also cannot stand this old male-female relationship. In short, the art of cursing "His mother's" brings some danger to women's love!

△···············△

"A Social Person's" Self-Description 254

— By She Ying

My personal involvement in society began during the 1911 Revolution. The social activities I participated in can be broadly divided into two categories: engaging in journalism and participating in the women's movement. My time teaching in schools was relatively short, only three to five years in total.

Period in Journalism

I recall that during the 1911 Revolution, women enthusiastically participated. At that time, women's organizations sprang up like mushrooms after rain, petitioning for the Northern Expedition and assisting with military expenses. As a young and passionate reporter, I eagerly wanted to see the revolution succeed immediately, so I bravely joined the activities. At that time, the aspirations of most women were entirely focused on striving for the revolution and seeking welfare for the country and the nation, unlike the subsequent women's movement that fought for equality. At the time, my father and Mr. Yu Youren, Mr. Song [blank], and other gentlemen used the Minli Pao as a revolutionary organ for creating an atmosphere and propagating ideas. I was assigned to edit the supplement, which was the beginning of my life as a journalist. Afterwards, I almost entirely pursued a career as a journalist, with the longest period being spent at the Zhonghua Xinbao. Initially, I edited the literary supplement, and later I was in charge of the "Women and Family" section for about seven or eight years.

Overview of Participation in the Women's Movement

Since the 1911 Revolution, the first organization I joined was the Shenzhou Women's Relief Society. I was responsible for editing the Shenzhou Women's Gazette monthly magazine. In the first year of the Republic, five groups merged and reorganized the Nationalist Party, holding their first inaugural meeting at Zhang Garden on Jing'an Temple Road in Shanghai. I served as a recorder at the time. There were four recorders on that day, two men and two women. One was a reporter from the Minquan Pao, Mr. [blank]. Another was Xu Xue'er, a reporter from the Minli Pao. One was Yang Jiwei from Wujiang. And the last was myself. Twenty years have passed. Mr. [blank] now holds an important position in the party and the nation. Mr. Xu has passed away. Mr. Yang is often ill. As for myself, I remain the same as before. Each of us has a different situation, which shows the changes in human affairs. During the May Fourth Movement, I participated in the patriotic movement in Shanghai. In the autumn of the eleventh year of the Republic [1922], I initiated the Shanghai Women's Rights Movement League with comrades, in response to the Beijing Women's Rights Association. In the spring of the fourteenth year of the Republic [1925], I united with comrades in the women's movement in Shanghai and Hangzhou to organize the Chinese Women's Association, and I also edited a special publication. Because the international status was important, there had to be a liaison organization between countries, so at the beginning of its establishment, it joined the International Women's Association to communicate the voice of the women's movement to the world and to win international sympathy. In the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], when the revolutionary army first arrived in Shanghai, it was organized by the Propaganda Department of the Eastern Front Political Department to create the Shanghai Women's Movement Committee. At the same time, it published the Women's Movement Ten-Day Publication to promote women's awareness of the revolution and the women's movement. In the summer and autumn, in order to concentrate the strength and will of the women's movement, I organized the Shanghai Women's Organizations Unity Association with my colleagues. As for those who merely participated and contributed nothing to society, there were the Women's Association, the Chinese Women's Suffrage Association, and the movement to promote domestic goods by women, as well as certain women's organizations, etc. Since they have no special achievements, they are not worth mentioning. In the spring of the eighteenth year of the Republic [1929], in view of the disunity of the women's movement and the need for a propaganda organ to act as its mouthpiece, I co-founded the Women's Resonance Society with my colleagues and published Women's Resonance. Initially, it was a bi-monthly publication, and in the twenty-first year of the Republic [1932], it was changed to a monthly publication. Fortunately, due to the efforts of my colleagues, it has had a six-year history, which is fortunate indeed. The recently joined Nantung Women's Cultural Promotion Association is also for the promotion of the women's cultural movement. In short, my life in the past twenty years has been within the scope of this kind of society and association life. Indeed, journalism and social movements are interconnected. Newspapers have the authority to create public opinion and transform society. For example, the ease with which the 1911 Revolution overthrew the political system and transformed it into a republic was due to the power of public opinion. At that time, the people's thinking was instilled by newspapers, which were full of nationalistic ideas. People yearned for the Han Chinese, so when someone raised an arm and shouted, the wind rose and the clouds surged, and the response was overwhelming! When women first sought liberation, they were oppressed everywhere. Although newspapers claimed to be a sharp weapon for promoting society, they often failed to abandon old habits and truly embrace the concept of equality between men and women. They did not pay much attention to news about the women's movement. Having one more person involved meant occupying one more position. Not only could propaganda be more convenient, but also opinions could be corrected more. At the very least, it could reduce some of the careless tone, ridicule, and advisory tone.

Thoughts on Social Life

In summarizing my experience in social work, I feel that the most interesting and enduring achievement has been the Women's Resonance Society. From the experience of this society, I realize that engaging in social movements cannot solely rely on nominal unity and solidarity to be considered a sound organization or to increase some kind of strength. If a large number of people do not make efforts or cannot resolve their differences and cooperate, they often end up fighting for power and profit or shirking responsibility, leading to inaction and stagnation. Resonance, on the other hand, was initiated by three or four like-minded comrades who were able to treat the society's affairs as their own, treating each other with sincerity. There was no competition for rights or evasion of responsibility, so it has been able to have a six-year history. Otherwise, in terms of women's organizations, there are many organizations with abundant finances and numerous talents. Why do they rise and fall quickly and cannot last long? The importance of sincerity is not great? I would like to say to comrades in social movements that if they can treat each other with sincerity, there is almost nothing that cannot be done in the world. My personal thoughts are roughly like this, and I will conclude my self-description with the above hope.

A Visit to the Childhood Education and Care Institute 255

— [blank]

The Childhood Education and Care Institute on Tangshan Road in this city is run by the China Childhood Relief Association and has been established for five years. Recently, I visited the institute to understand its current situation.

Ms. Liu Jinfang, the director, is about thirty-five or thirty-six years old and has a kind and approachable manner. Her answers can be summarized as follows: The institute's organization is divided into four departments: general affairs, education, training, and hygiene. It has one director, six teachers and staff, and three male and female nannies and workers.

The annual expenses are about 10,000 yuan, which is entirely raised by the sponsoring organization.

There are currently more than 90 children in the institute, with boys accounting for slightly more than half. They come from various sources, mostly sent by the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Local Court, the Relief Society, and other institutions. Some are adopted or sent back to their hometowns, so there is an average of about fifteen children entering and leaving each month.

In terms of education, the institute has an attached primary school, with a curriculum similar to that of ordinary schools. Due to "economic," "talent," and "location" limitations, it currently uses a combined grade system, divided into six grades and three classes. The teaching method for the middle and upper grades is self-study and guidance, while the lower grades use the design education method. As for extracurricular practice, girls mainly focus on sewing, shoemaking, knitting socks, and housekeeping, while boys mainly focus on developing farms, cleaning, and cooperatives.

According to regulations, children can stay in the institute until they are twelve years old, but if there are children with higher intelligence, the institute can make special arrangements to extend their stay until they are sixteen years old so that they can continue to complete six years of schooling. When underage children reach a certain age, they are either adopted or introduced by the institute to factories and shops as apprentices. When necessary, the institute will find a match for adult female children. The method is not to accept betrothal gifts, but the suitor must prepare 100 yuan to be used for the girl's dowry. The qualifications of the suitor are as follows: (1) unmarried, (2) of good character and conduct, (3) has a proper occupation and has received considerable education, and (4) has two introducers.

The institute has a contact method for children after they leave the institute. Those who want to adopt children from the institute must accept the institute's guidance at any time and cannot refuse when the institute sends someone to visit. The children's daily performance must also be reported to the institute at the end of each semester for evaluation. The training is roughly the same as in ordinary schools. However, the children here cannot leave the institute at will, so there are no opportunities to go out except for mountain teachers accompanying them on visits.

The conversation ended here. At this time, a man in a blue cloth long gown walked in. Introduced by Director Chen, he was Mr. Li, a teacher at the institute. Therefore, I seized the opportunity to ask Mr. Li to accompany me on a tour of the rooms, and this request was immediately agreed to without hesitation.

The classrooms were on the second floor, a total of three. Each classroom was in session. The students were wearing neat blue bamboo cloth uniforms and listening attentively and happily. Because I couldn't bear to disturb their attention, I only stood in each classroom for a moment before walking out. In the classroom of the upper grades, there was a slogan: "Work hard, and we will have a way out." At that time, I was truly touched. Indeed, in this era, what else can a poor boy do besides work hard?

The boys' dormitory was located along the window. The word "cleanliness" was very appropriate. Small iron beds were arranged in rows, with white sheets and blue cotton quilts neatly spread on the beds. The girls' dormitory was on the third floor. Because Mr. Li was not accustomed to using the key, he did not go in, but only stood on a high stool and looked from afar. The scene was similar to the boys' dormitory.

In addition, we also visited the municipal columns and wall newspapers run by the students, as well as the Citizens' Bank! Mentioning the Citizens' Bank, some people may wonder, "Where do the orphans get the money?" In fact, it is not entirely the case. According to Mr. Li's explanation, the institute encourages the work interest of older students. After doing productive work, each person can get wages. These wages are deposited in this small bank, and will be returned to the children when they leave the institute.

The institute's medical equipment is generally sufficient. However, the lighting in the examination room is really too dim.

Walking back to the office, Director Chen was organizing the children's registers. The spirit of this director is worthy of admiration. I couldn't help but feel happy for the orphans for a moment. Although strictly speaking, the establishment of this kind of education and care institute is just a superficial relief work of reformism, orphans are pitiful after all. Since the government is unable to take care of them, then it is better than nothing.

Finally, in order to provide a reference for scholars of sociology, I repeatedly asked about the detailed reasons for the children's admission to the institute. Director Chen gave me a recent statistical table. From March of the nineteenth year of the Republic [1930] to September of the twenty-third year of the Republic [1934], the origins of the children admitted during this period were: 153 disaster children, 50 extremely poor children, 9 children sold, 20 abused children, 15 abducted children, 35 lost children, and 20 abandoned children.

Readers, from these numbers, the symptoms of Chinese society are already imaginable. What are your thoughts?

Women and Literature (Continued) 256

— Qian Zijin

To write about the pitiable nature of parasitic life, to awaken women's self-awareness of their own independent personality. In Ibsen's play "A Doll's House" (Nora), the female protagonist Nora discovers that her husband's usual tenderness, sweetness, and love are all hypocritical, all feigned. Once something happens that damages his reputation, he reveals his true self, scolding his wife for dragging him down. However, after the matter is resolved, he pretends to be magnanimous and forgiving. Thus, Nora completely "understands" and realizes that she has been living with a stranger, bearing him three children. She decides to leave from now on, intending to educate herself and become a "person." Nora says, "In short, I am a person."

In order to demand an independent life and to become a person, Nora resolutely abandons everything from the past: her husband and children, and leaves home. This implies that women's independent personality, being a true "person" of oneself, is more important than anything else.

"After Nora's Declaration of Independence was issued, it did indeed cause a great stir and sparked enormous waves in the minds of the society at the time. Gosse once said: 'This work elucidates the inner nature of humanity. The people who watched the play all vied to imitate the tone of the characters in the play. ... In fact, everyone who saw this play was talking about it and debating it at home, and the family's peace was even disrupted because of it.'"

Since Nora was born, some women have awakened from their dreams, raised their heads from underground, and reached out from the darkness. With their bare hands, they broke out of the haunted tower and went to find their own paths.

(III)

But what happened to Nora after she left home? That is, what happens to women after they awaken? The women after that are the new type of economically independent women trained by Nora's spirit in Shaw's "Mrs. Warren's Profession" (published in 1893), namely, Vivie.

If women want to liberate themselves from the dependent and parasitic life of slaves and demand an independent personality, then they must first have economic independence. Vivie is Nora after she left home, from the family to the society. She represents a new type of woman who uses her own abilities to earn social rewards and live an independent life. Vivie has become a person of the world, a person of society, not a slave or plaything of a family or husband.

Vivie rejects money, status, Duchess Croft, and everything from the old era that Mrs. Warren gave her. She opposes and rejects them. She received higher education at Cambridge University and is proficient in mathematics. She calculates accounts for a female lawyer. After working six hours a day, she takes a walk for exercise. She relies entirely on her own brain and hands to live, without depending on others at all.

Vivie rejects the wealthy Duke Croft, whom Mrs. Warren wants her to flirt with, and mocks the "childish dreams of love" of ordinary frivolous young men. She shouts to her mother, "Everyone has the freedom to choose their profession. The most unfortunate child in the world, although he cannot choose to be the Queen of England or the President of Oxford, can, according to his own preferences, choose to collect rags or sell flowers."

A woman who creates her own life and is self-reliant in this way is the typical new woman after Ibsen. It is also Nora's proper return after leaving home. With a new ideal of life and a firm determination, she struggles with society and opposes old-fashioned people like Mrs. Warren. Kicking aside the barriers built by men with prejudice and selfishness, they enter offices, desks, factories, shops, laboratories, experimental rooms, schools, and government offices, which have always been forbidden to women.

In Hauptmann's novel "The Weavers" (Die Weber), the female protagonist Marie is also a representative of new women. Poverty and distress have strengthened her determination to fight for life. She knocks on the door of a factory and becomes the most hardworking female worker among a large group of workers. The thorns of life have wounded her hands and feet, but she does not feel pain. Fate has thrown all kinds of ridicule, but her iron face does not show a trace of tremor or terror. She boasts of a strength that she possesses: the strength to live alone without relying on others at all.

In Nagrodzka's novel "The Wrath of Dionysus," the female protagonist Tanya is a female artist from a wealthy family. She falls in love with Stark, a young man who is enthusiastic about science. They go through legal procedures to live together. But she and her husband each have their own world, each doing their own work. Sometimes Tanya is caught in a conflict between "love" and "work." But she always uses her enthusiasm for work to extinguish the flames of love. She does her artistic work first. During the passionate love affair, her diary is also filled with words of ardent love for work: "Today I did work. This is fanatical work, and from morning on, I felt that I couldn't put down the work for a moment."

Kollontai's "Red Love" (Red Passion) features Vasilisa, a revolutionary and a model modern woman. She loves her work deeply and passionately, especially the work of organizing public housing. Although she also falls in love, she never forgets her work, even when love is disillusioned or even during passionate love. In her work, she is not at all constrained by love. What is most noteworthy is the calm attitude she takes after losing love. Because there is an endless amount of work piled up in front of her, waiting for her to do it.

Here, it shows that the "love" that was especially valued in the old days is no longer the only content of women's lives, and that "love" is a secondary matter for women as well as men. "Love" is sacred. At this time, it is treated coldly by women and not regarded as their treasure. Instead, "career" is their primary concern!

There are also Phanla, the female protagonist in Potemkin's novel "In the Mist," Maiya, the female protagonist in Helge Krog's novel "The Sound Barrier," Yuxiefu, the female protagonist in Yrjö Hirn's novel "Work," and Dana, the female protagonist in Gorky's novel "The Diary of a Vagabond," who are all typical new women.

After Ibsen, there are already tens of millions of working women earning their own living, and tens of millions of women are immersed in their own careers.

(IV)

From the Book of Songs, the Yuefu ballads, "The Romance of the Western Chamber," "Dream of the Red Chamber," the Bible, and the novels of Turgenev, Chekhov, Zola, Maupassant, and Tolstoy, we have seen many enslaved women who are passive, devoted, elegant, gentle, delicate, and pitiable. But after Nora, the rebellious revolutionary rebel of the Ibsen era, there emerged awakened women such as Vivie, Marie, Tanya, and Vasilisa. What will the women of the future be like? There are still few great writers who have come out to inspire, to raise beacons, and to sound alarm bells, but we can easily imagine by speculating on the present. The women of the future will definitely be progressive and developed in both quality and quantity. They will be more advanced than Vivie, Marie, Tanya, and Vasilisa, and the number of new women will increase even more. The new women will not be a group formed by a special minority, but the entire female population. In the future, Vivie, Tanya, Marie, etc., will no longer be new types, but a universal and inevitable phenomenon. Every remote and backward area, every corner of the world, will be filled with awakened and more advanced Vivie, Marie, Tanya, and Vasilisa.

Moreover, they will not have the kind of anarchic, greedy, and multifaceted demands that were present during the era of women's revolution. They will strive to develop their own excellent instincts. Because true human culture requires both men and women to develop their inherent excellent instincts as much as possible. Therefore, I believe that the women of the future, under absolutely equal treatment with men, will not only be doing ordinary general work, but also developing their excellent instincts and doing some special work. This work is needed by society and cannot be done by men, or cannot be done well.

Sisters, work hard! There is light ahead! (The End)

Shenbao Amateur Weekly

The Arts

On Guanyin Plays and Their Sound Effects 257

— Chen Dabe

Since the birth of the Guanyin Play on the twenty-second Double Tenth Festival of the Republic of China, it has had a history of fifteen months of broadcasting. There are reportedly as many as thirty-nine drama troupes on various broadcasting stations in Shanghai. As the ancients said, "The predecessors plant trees, and the successors enjoy the shade." I am the first person to plant trees, so of course I like to see many pursuers of wireless radio drama art come to my tree to enjoy the shade. But, unfortunately, although the number of shade-enjoyers is increasing day by day, there are still few who are truly interested in pursuing wireless radio drama art. This is already enough to make me feel bad. What is especially unbearable is that I often hear the people sitting in the shade ridiculing and squeezing each other because the shade is not enough, and even the tree planter is being squeezed out of the shade! Don't you think that's pitiful?

"Guanyin Play" is another name for "Wireless Radio Drama" (Radiodrama). Although wireless radio drama is popular in European and American countries, it is still in its infancy. According to many art critics, this little sister's future is limitless. When she grows up, she may be able to do great things that her sisters cannot imagine. Unlike her sister, the drama, which is limited by space and time, she can spread her artistic seeds to the whole world, or even the whole universe, on any radio station and in any season. Only this little sister can achieve the artification of all mankind?

I gave wireless radio drama the nickname "Guanyin Play" simply to make it easier for people to notice and remember. There is no Chinese person who has not heard the words "Guanyin." But what exactly do the words "Guanyin" mean? I'm afraid many great monks can't answer it fluently and straightforwardly. Since I was a child, I have been extraordinarily interested in the words "Guanyin." Several years ago, after I discovered the wireless radio drama of the British Broadcasting Drama Society, I felt that "sound" could be "viewed" only in wireless radio drama.

However, because our plays are called "Guanyin Plays," many Christians and other religious believers still do not dare to listen to them because they fear being accused of apostasy! There is also a joke that wandering monks often see the signboard of our "Shanghai Guanyin Drama Society" and mistakenly believe that we are Buddhists, so they come to us to solicit donations for the repair of dilapidated temples.

Radio drama scripts are more difficult to write than stage plays. Although many speculative books have been published in Europe and America, it is not easy to find many that are practical. The most difficult point is that radio drama cannot use costumes, scenery, lighting, makeup, etc. to reveal part of the environment and personality of the characters in the play. Moreover, because the audience never sees the characters in the play, there cannot be as many characters in each scene as in a stage play. If there are too many, it will be difficult to distinguish them. Moreover, the appearance and disappearance of each actor must be naturally revealed in the dialogue of the characters in the play. The location, season, climate, etc. of the characters in the play that are helpful to the progress of the plot are best revealed in the dialogue in the most artistic way. In addition to dialogue, only sound effects can increase the density of the plot. A pure radio drama script does not need a third-person narrative. Shakespeare's plays are a good model for radio drama because the interrelationships between time, place, and people are all revealed in the dialogue. But it is not the best model because, although Shakespeare's plays have no scenery, they still rely on vision, while radio drama is almost performed for the blind, just as pantomime and silent films are performed for the deaf.

I hear that several vaudeville-ized drama troupes in Shanghai still use the siren to open and close the curtain like in a vaudeville play. This excessively stimulating high-pitched sound is most unsuitable for radio. Since there is no curtain to close, and since it is not limited by space, the characters in the play can walk slowly from the garden into the bedroom in a play with a continuous beginning and end. Why bother blowing the siren twice and adding so many appendix-like reports?

Although our sound effects methods have been painstakingly searched for by several comrades, we have never dared to keep them secret. A machine gun is an iron rod knocking on the edge of a table. A rifle is a rattan whip whipping a wooden board. A cannon and a bomb are the low frequencies of a full-armed piano. The sound of an airplane is a roll of old newspaper lightly touching the two wings of an electric fan. The rest is mostly just a little bit of ventriloquism.

There is also the sound of rain. We tie grains of dry soybeans with short lines to a banana leaf fan. Gently waving it creates various sounds of rain of different sizes. There is a joke about this. Our sound effects technician often stores this treasure in various radio stations. When it comes time to use it, the soybeans have all entered the bellies of the mice. After this, we plan to use beads instead.

Industry Surveys

Second-Hand Clothing Business 258

— Xu Xiao

Speaking from the perspective of the overall commerce and social economy, the business of second-hand clothing stores does indeed occupy a very important position. If there were no pawnshops in the market, then the economy of the lower-class citizens in this area would inevitably be greatly affected; however, if there were only pawnshops and no second-hand clothing industry, then many of the pawnshops' overdue pledges would have no outlet. Therefore, the second-hand clothing industry and pawnshops, for the economic prosperity of a market, are mutually causal and complementary, occupying a very important position in the overall commerce. However, the second-hand clothing industry is, after all, a kind of deformed commerce; the clothes sold there are always old, even if some of the clothes are actually not old, the second-hand clothing store itself still has to say they are old. This is, it is precisely using a business method that is the opposite of others.

In the Shilu area of Shanghai, there are no fewer than thirty such second-hand clothing stores. In addition, there are more than a dozen "brokerage houses" also located in this area. People who like to wear cheap clothes, there is no one who does not know Shilu, which is like the headquarters of the second-hand clothing industry, and at the same time, it can be said to be a warehouse for a part of the pawnshops' pledges. Therefore, if pawnshops do not have the second-hand clothing industry, their pledges cannot be promoted; but if second-hand clothing stores do not have pawnshops, they will lack a source of goods. However, in their principle of mutual utilization, it is still the second-hand clothing industry that suffers; because the clothes received by the second-hand clothing stores have to go through a "brokerage house" in the middle.

Their transaction form is that the pawnshops first pack the expired clothes into bags and put them together: regardless of whether there are long gowns or cheongsams inside, and regardless of whether the clothes inside are new or old; big, small, modern, old-fashioned, leather, silk, cloth, all kinds of strange clothes, countless such packages. If the "brokerage houses" want to buy, they can open them at will; but at most, they cannot exceed thirty packages, which is a rule they mutually abide by. After the goods are inspected, the estimated costs of these goods are all added up, and finally, a discount of 30% or 25%, 27% is applied, depending on the case. After the "brokerage houses" buy these many clothes, they classify them one by one; at this time, it all depends on the "appraiser's" eyesight to evaluate a very appropriate price for these many clothes.

Speaking of the job of this kind of "appraiser," it is indeed not an easy job to do; other things cannot be said to be brilliant, but when a package of clothes is sent to him, he can immediately determine which company's products the clothes are, whether they are foreign goods or domestic goods; the newness of the clothes, the value of the price, are all determined by him in the blink of an eye.

Each "brokerage house" has two such "appraiser" talents, and large-scale ones also use four people; the "brokerage house's" treatment of such employees is always more favorable than that of general employees. From morning to night, if they don't want to come to the brokerage house to eat, they rarely have time to stay in the house; most of their time is spent chatting, either sitting in that silk shop or sitting in that fur shop; while chatting with the people there, they secretly keep an eye on the prices of the goods there, and sometimes they also run to various clothing factories to visit. People who hold this position not only have to have that talent, but also have to be familiar with all aspects of the business community in Shanghai; otherwise, you will only have a "black lacquer gatehouse," and you won't be able to move a step.

The pricing of various clothes by the "brokerage houses" is all executed by the "appraiser"; he divides the various clothes into different sizes, and each hundred taels of silver is discounted by 30% and then resold to the second-hand clothing merchants.

The second-hand clothing stores also hire specialized purchasing staff, and their vision is not inferior to the "appraiser" of the "brokerage house" however, their

Assorted Fragments 259

I think, if someone were to propose that men marry women, then 200 million women might not completely agree. If it were put to a vote according to the precedent of a majority passing, then it might not be possible to pass this proposal.

The Yang Zhu school advocates "Enjoy the present life, why worry about after death?" and "What glory is there for posthumous fame to withered bones?" These words are most suitable as a portrayal for the young masters and ladies of Shanghai.

In the second issue of the Literary Quarterly, there is a "Chiyoko" with a very strong island country flavor. In the article, Yoshida says; "I have seen through it long ago, even if the whole of China is destroyed, we are still us. Those officers and politicians are still the ones taking concubines with bound feet." This remark is quite enough to be a wake-up call for the people of a militaristic country who are being deceived!

Chinese people age before their time and especially like to act old. It's better to die丨······"

Page 21

targets are different. The clothes they welcome are mostly old-fashioned, long, Chinese-style clothes; Western suits are of course also needed, but they are not very welcome, because this kind of customer is not easy to come by. As for women's cheongsams, they make them even more headache. This kind of clothes is even more difficult to sell than Western suits.

In the current situation of this social and economic downturn, many people who wear Western suits are mostly limited by economic circumstances, so they make do with what they have. Therefore, a relatively decent Western suit does not worry about not having a customer. But women's cheongsams are a bit different; because the tailoring of this kind of clothes is mostly made according to the body's fatness and thinness, just like men's Western suits, but it is even more difficult to change than Western suits. Moreover, general fashionable women simply do not want to wear other people's "old goods"; women in the countryside, they may not have learned to wear cheongsams yet, and even if there are exceptional customers from the countryside who come to buy them, they often fail because of the size of the body being mismatched, and it is rare for one out of ten transactions to be successful. Therefore, when second-hand clothing stores see that they have bought women's cheongsams, they always add the value of this piece of clothing to other clothes; if this women's cheongsam is fortunately sold, it is "extra income", otherwise, they will not lose money.

The transactions between second-hand clothing stores and "brokerage houses" are sometimes that they take the goods and pay the money at the same time. If this second-hand clothing store has a considerable history, or is usually more capable of handling large volumes, then it can take the goods first and settle the accounts again at the end of the month; however, usually, they pay 30% first, and the rest is mostly paid in installments.

These second-hand clothing stores buy the goods and then sell them again, and the profit they get in this transaction is at most 20%; however, sometimes when new goods are sold, it is also easy to make a profit on both the principal and the interest. They generally mark the prices on the clothes with a kind of code that indicates the amount of silver; each tael of silver is equivalent to about six jiao in foreign currency. For example, if a piece of clothing is marked as ten taels, it is actually less than six yuan, but they always sell it for around six yuan.

The worst time for the second-hand clothing business is in the spring and summer seasons; in these two seasons, no matter how much the boss and the employees shout, there will still be no customers. This kind of situation will continue until after September, when the business will gradually prosper; and when the north wind howls in winter, the customers will walk in like bamboo shoots after a rain, and one will be replaced by another. Especially the clothes sold at this time are mostly very profitable; because winter clothes are mostly fur goods, and even the general working class will at least buy a cotton robe. This period can be said to be the golden age of the second-hand clothing industry; the second-hand clothing store's own business increases, and the employees' fortune also comes along at the same time.

In the second-hand clothing industry, employees are mostly hired on a commission basis; it is generally stipulated that they receive three cents per yuan, and some may even receive more than this. But in general, it will not be much; however, in addition to receiving a commission of three cents per yuan, appraisers can also earn an extra cent for each piece of clothing sold. Generally, an appraiser's monthly income averages between twenty and thirty yuan, and at most will not exceed forty yuan; another hope is the year-end bonus. The method of distributing this bonus varies from store to store, with some offering 10% or 20%, but others offering no bonus at all, all depending on the boss's personal will.

The apprentices in second-hand clothing stores not only cannot receive one or two yuan per month from the store for miscellaneous expenses such as haircuts, baths, and laundry, like apprentices in ordinary stores; but the cost of food and lodging during the three-year apprenticeship period must instead be repaid to the boss, which, in the general business situation, cannot be considered a kind of deformed state, right?

Small Monograph

The Problem of Japanese Goods Dumping 260

— Kesheng

Since the global economic panic occurred in 1929, the torrent of recession has been sweeping through the prosperity of the world's imperialist countries with the greatest force. This situation was first manifested in foreign trade. We see:

1931 1933

British exports £454.4 million £416 million imports £860.1 million £678 million

US exports 2.424 billion yuan 1.674 billion yuan imports 2.091 billion yuan 1.448 billion yuan

French exports 30.42 billion francs 18.43 billion francs imports 42.19 billion francs 28.42 billion francs

German exports 9.59 billion marks 4.87 billion marks imports 6.72 billion marks 4.2 billion marks

These are the major countries of the world. From the above table, it can be seen that the figures for their foreign trade in 1933 were greatly reduced compared to those in 1931, which means that their foreign trade is in a state of increasing decline.

However, in the situation of the increasing decline of foreign trade in various countries around the world, Japan has become an exception: In 1933, Japan's total trade volume was 3.74 billion yen, of which exports accounted for 1.83 billion yuan and imports accounted for 1.91 billion yuan. Compared with 1932, exports and imports increased by 33% in total; compared with 1931, exports increased by 60% and imports also increased by 55%. By the first half of 1934, Japan's exports reached 1.03 billion yen and imports reached 1.158 billion yuan. Compared with the same period in 1933, its exports increased by 20% and imports also increased by 14%.

In the torrent of global recession, Japan's foreign trade alone can rise, of course, because Japanese goods enter and exit the world market, that is, because of the dumping of Japanese goods. In fact, all the important markets in the world are filled with the footprints of Japanese goods. In Asia, such as China, India, Dutch India, the Straits Settlements, and Siam; in Europe, such as England, France, and the Netherlands; in Africa, such as Egypt, South Africa, and East Africa; in Oceania, such as Australia; in the Americas, such as the countries of Central and South America, all have become the main markets for the dumping of Japanese goods. Major countries in the world such as England, the United States, France, and Italy have been greatly threatened by the dumping of Japanese goods. During the Anglo-Japanese cotton industry conference in February last year, the British representative publicly said: "The current activities of Japanese goods in the world market threaten the industrial organizations of various countries. If this situation continues like this, then, as a result, Japan may become the common enemy of the world." From this, one can imagine a glimpse.

We know that the Americas have always been the main market for England and the United States. Taking South and Central America alone, the great powers have invested as much as 15 or 16 billion gold yuan here, accounting for 50% of the funds they have invested in the entire colony; but among them, England and the United States have each invested 6 billion gold yuan, accounting for more than two-thirds of the total. From this, one can know how strong the economic power of England and the United States is here. However, in recent years, the dumping of Japanese goods in the Americas, especially in Central and South America, has shown an astonishing degree of development. Please see the table below丨丨

1931 1932 1933

North America Amount (thousands of yuan) 438,865 453,965 499,156 Percentage 38.3 32.2 26.8

Central America Amount (thousands of yuan) 3,301 5,130 16,175 Percentage 0.3 0.4 0.9

South America Amount (thousands of yuan) 10,225 13,133 30,379 Percentage 0.9 0.9 1.6

Total amount including other continents (thousands of yuan) 1,146,981 1,409,991 1,861,045 Percentage 100.0 100.0 100.0

It's no wonder that England wants to say "Japan is a common enemy of the world"!

The dumping of Japanese goods is like "mercury leaking to the ground," and there is no place it cannot enter. The major countries in the world are increasingly threatened by it. The reason why it can be like this, needless to say, is because the value of Japanese goods is low. "Just take the Japanese goods in the European market, for example, light bulbs are two and a half cents each, men's socks are four and a half cents per pair, gold nib fountain pens are seven and a half cents per pen, nine-piece coffee sets are forty-nine cents per set, bicycles are four yuan and fifty-six cents each, and the price of rayon in Marseille is lower than the yarn price in Lyon, and cotton fabrics can reduce the cost by 40% to 70% compared to European factory products." The selling price in other places is also lower than the local market price. Therefore, it can dump its products all over the world.

Why is the selling price of Japanese goods so low? According to the Japanese themselves, it is: 1. The yen is low and the foreign exchange market has fallen; 2. Technological progress and industrial rationalization; 3. Low labor wages and increased production efficiency; 4. Convenient sea transportation; 5. The increasingly close economic relationship between Japan and "Manchukuo" stimulates the development of Japanese industry; ...... (See page 99 of the December issue of the Japanese "Diplomatic Times"). These are indeed important reasons why Japanese goods are so cheap. However, due to space limitations, we cannot discuss these reasons in detail one by one. Now, let's quote a paragraph of Mr. Xu Dixin's explanation of this issue below for reference 丨丨

"Vigorously implementing dumping is premised on currency inflation, wage reduction, and strengthening the exploitation of labor. ...... In the past three years, the yen has depreciated by about 60%, but the selling price has only increased by about 18%, while the cost of living (Tokyo) index has increased from 136 in 1931 to 148 in 1932. As for currency wages, the index in 1931 was 91.3, and it fell to 85.1 in June 1932. Wages have decreased by 6%, while the cost of living has increased by 9%. The real wages of Japanese workers have decreased by 15% in two years. The income of workers has been greatly reduced, but the labor of workers has been deeply squeezed out. According to the statistics of Mitsubishi Bank, the general industrial production index in Japan was 100.7 in 1931, but it increased to 137.6 in October 1933. In three years, it increased by 37%. This 37% production index is the blood and sweat that Japanese workers have spent under the conditions of reducing wages and strengthening labor." (See page 35 of Volume 31, Issue 18 of "Eastern Magazine")

The most important reason for the recent rise of Japanese industry, the low value of Japanese goods, and the ability of Japanese goods to dump their products everywhere and threaten the world market is that Japan exploits its domestic workers to make the cost of its various goods cheap.

The major countries in the world have been threatened by the dumping of Japanese goods, so of course they have to find ways to deal with it. Therefore, England first prompted India to greatly increase the import tax on Japanese cotton, restricting the import of its cotton textiles; at the same time, it also raised its own tariffs to resist the dumping of Japanese goods. The United States has also implemented raising tariffs and restricting the import of Japanese goods since it implemented the Agricultural Relief and Industrial Recovery Act in 1933. Dutch East Indies also conducted a boycott of Japanese goods at the same time as England. ...... In this way, the entry and exit of Japanese goods in the world market is like "a rat crossing the street", and people are shouting "Beat! Beat!" everywhere! If Japanese goods continue to desperately dump their products on the world market, we believe that other countries will continue to find ways to deal with it.

However, England and the United States can use methods such as raising tariffs and restricting imports to resist the dumping of Japanese goods, but only general weak nations, especially semi-colonial countries, cannot use extremely effective methods to deal with it. Therefore, when Japanese goods run into walls everywhere, they desperately attack places with weaker resistance. Our country has always been Japan's most important market, and under the dumping of its goods, of course, it is the first to be looted. In this situation, what countermeasures should we take? This is what we hope people across the country will pay special attention to.

Commonsense

The Card Method of Literary Research 261

— Yijun

"Card method" is the best method of collecting research data. Anyone who studies can get a lot of convenience from this method. Literary people can also get a lot of help from this method to collect writing materials. Now I want to give a brief introduction to this method and its application in literary research.

First of all, I have to explain the "card" itself. The form of "card" is usually a rectangular thick paper about four inches long and three inches wide, but there are also some that are larger or smaller than this. The paper is not limited to that kind, Daolin paper, twill paper... are all available, as long as it meets the conditions that it is suitable for writing on both sides and is easy to collect and not easy to damage. It is best to have different colors of paper, which is needed for material classification; for example, in terms of literature, valuable materials read from literary books and newspapers may be recorded on yellow paper, writing materials may be recorded on blue paper, and miscellaneous feelings, essays, experiences, questions, etc. may be recorded on light red paper, and so on. This is still a rough classification, and there are also more detailed classifications. For example, in the creation aspect, if you want to collect materials for a novel, you want to record it with one color, and for the materials for another novel, you may use another color of paper to record it. In short, there can be many kinds of paper colors, and the purpose is entirely for easy search, examination, and classification. After doing this work for a long time, a lot of materials of the same kind will accumulate, and you will know a lot about this matter. When you write, you will not feel the pain of lack of materials, and the content of your article will not be empty and without anything.

The recording method is like this: For example, you want to write a novel (or a thesis, essay, miscellaneous feeling... all are OK). Suppose the name of your novel is "Passion". You must first write these two words in the upper left corner of the card. On the next line, you may write down your inspiration, the materials you have obtained, your theme (such as the contradiction and conflict between revolutionary passion and love passion, etc.), your temporary most satisfactory words and sentences, your flow of thoughts... These various materials may not be coherent, even if the words and sentences are not coherent due to haste, it does not matter, because this is not originally for others to see. You should always write down the materials you get today, and even tomorrow, the day after tomorrow, next month, next year, three or five years, seven or eight years later, if your great work is still not written, you still have to continue to write down those necessary materials at any time. It is not uncommon for the number of cards to accumulate to hundreds or even thousands for a book. Naturally, ordinary random feelings, essays, etc., only need one or two or at most three or five.

In fact, this is the best way to preserve memory. In today's society, people and events are complicated, and our little inspiration and little materials are easily lost unnoticed. If we have the habit of recording them with card paper, we can save these things at any time, and we can take them endlessly and use them inexhaustibly in the future.

Obviously, it is much more convenient and easier to take notes with card paper than with a "notebook". The biggest drawback of notebooks is that they are inconvenient to open, inconvenient to classify, and too troublesome to search and examine. However, note card paper can be used at any time, and the above-mentioned shortcomings can be avoided.

The preparation of this card paper is also extremely easy. Because the area is not large, an ordinary piece of Daolin paper can

Impression of Master of Sinology, Mr. Hu Puan 262

— Sang Ying

Whenever Mr. Hu Puan is mentioned, the four words "Master of Sinology" immediately come to mind. Indeed, among the people of our time, regarding sinology, those with truly profound attainments, Mr. Hu Puan, I fear, is the last glimmer of a dying tradition!

He once served as the Commissioner of Civil Affairs in Jiangsu Province. Navigating the officialdom seemed not to be his forte. During his tenure, it was heard that he very much wanted to develop the aspirations of a scholar, but alas, amidst a world of universal intoxication, he alone was sober. His efforts yielded little result. After resigning, he remained with sleeves empty of riches, living in seclusion in Shanghai. From then on, he no longer set foot in the political vortex, only making a living by running newspapers and teaching at various universities.

My acquaintance with Mr. Hu was in the Arts program at ×× College.

Before meeting Mr. Hu, I always imagined him to be a gentle and refined scholar. But when Mr. Hu walked into the classroom that day, carrying a briefcase under his arm, I realized that my conjecture was completely wrong, and even absurd and laughable. Mr. Hu was entirely a "Northern type" of large man, with a robust physique, a purplish-brown complexion, a long, grizzled beard on his mouth, spectacles with wide tortoiseshell frames on his nose, wearing a melon-shaped cap, and dressed in a loose-fitting gray cloth gown.

丨丨 Mr. ×, look how hale and hearty the old gentleman is!

丨丨 Yes, and I've heard that he is punctual for every class he teaches in any school, without the habit of professors these days wasting time.

I remember that the class that day started at seven in the morning. Isn't that the time when those young masters and mistresses are usually still "sleeping soundly in seclusion"?

Walking up to the podium, he sat securely in the teacher's chair, took off his wide-rimmed glasses from the bridge of his nose, and started calling the roll. His two large eyeballs shot towards the faces of the students whose names were called. His voice was loud and resonant, immediately revealing that he was not someone who grew up in the water and soil of the South. Moreover, his pronunciation was mixed with many Hui dialect sounds.

He lectured on "Xunzi's Theories."

丨丨 "Human nature is evil; that which is good is artificial!"

When he said this famous quote from Xunzi, he took off the melon-shaped cap from his head, placed it on the podium, and his spirit became increasingly energetic. He even stood up from the teacher's chair and gave an "impassioned exposition" for fifteen minutes, then sat back down in the teacher's chair and chanted from his self-edited lecture notes.

His lecture notes were elegant in language, sonorous, and easy to recite, truly excellent classical prose. Those few pages of lecture notes are still hidden in my book trunk to this day.

For the entire hour, from the beginning to the end of class, I always remember that the old gentleman's face was constantly tense, without even a hint of a smile. At that time, I thought of the demeanor of an ancient ascetic monk. Once, I don't know what he was lecturing on, the old gentleman exceptionally used male-female love as an analogy, but coming from the mouth of Mr. Hu, who didn't tell jokes, it always felt a little out of place, I felt at the time.

It has been a long time since I last saw Mr. Hu. Unexpectedly, on Saturday afternoon of the previous week, when I was walking at the intersection of Connaught Road and Jiaozhou Road, I met an elderly man of tall stature coming towards me. He was walking with his head held high and with a wide stride. Upon closer inspection, it turned out to be Mr. Hu. That day, the north wind was biting cold. Mr. Hu was wearing a loose-fitting overcoat, and because the buttons were not fastened, the coat was opened by the force of the wind. It seemed that there was also a young lady accompanying him. She was probably his daughter!

He might not be able to call out my name, but he certainly could still recognize me. After greeting each other, we did not talk much on the roadside and then nodded in farewell.

My relationship with Mr. Hu is very shallow, but his noble spirit, revealed everywhere in his words and deeds, and in his demeanor, left a very deep impression on me.

Mr. Hu Puan is from Jing County, Anhui Province, and currently resides at No. 9, Kangle Lane, Connaught Road.

Page 22

Page 23

Six or seventy cards can be cut from each sheet, and lined paper can be cut into thirty or forty cards. Each card costs only three or four cents. One dollar can cut eight or nine hundred to a thousand cards, enough for you to use for two or three years. And this kind of paper is also sold in the market, but it is relatively more expensive. This kind of card stock is usually kept by people who study in a multi-layered long wooden cabinet, inside which it is separated by hard paper by category, systematically and meticulously, without any disorder. You can find the material you need inside in less than a minute. Assuming you can't afford a cabinet (which costs at least five or six dollars), you might as well have a drawer or box specifically for these cards, the effect is the same.

Several years ago, I read an article in "The Middle School Student" by Mr. Xie Liuyi recommending this method, "To Literary Youths," which, although somewhat brief, is still quite worth considering. I might as well quote a few sentences below: "······· I advise you to use the 'card system.' Let us buy some thick paper cards and put them in a drawer; write down our daily experiences and thoughts on the cards. Anything sensed by the five senses, imagined by intuition, must be written on a card. No matter how many cards you write each day, put them in the drawer at hand. After accumulating day by day, the accumulated cards should be quite a few. On Saturday evenings, slowly sort out the cards, there is quite a lot of fun.······" Scholars, writers, university students, middle school students can certainly use card stock, and even generally uneducated people who want to study can also use card stock. Although this is not an era of studying behind closed doors, but at least one person should always have some knowledge, some ability to express themselves, so I still recommend this method that I have used to you, my wise readers.

Outlying Postal Agency

Doggerel 263

— He Sheng

Correspondence from Qianshan County, Anhui

I remember Zeng Guofan once said that "raising pigs, weaving cloth, and making oil are sideline occupations for farmers." In various parts of Anhui, especially in central, western, and northern Anhui, these three kinds of sideline occupations for farmers are indeed very commonly distributed. There are very few farmers in any place who do not raise pigs or weave cloth; naturally, there are also quite a few places where making oil is a sideline occupation. Just like in our small place 丨丨 Qianshan County, Anhui 丨丨, farm families who make oil as a sideline occupation are "everywhere."

Making oil is a more troublesome and laborious matter than raising pigs or weaving cloth. To make oil, one must first have a work machine 丨丨 "oil mill." In the inland rural areas, it is naturally out of the question to use any "machines"; oil-making equipment is nothing more than some hand-made "oil vats" and "oil baskets," etc. The labor used is nothing more than the blood and sweat painstakingly accumulated by farmers. The composition of an "oil mill" generally consists of the following: a house specially built for the purpose of "making oil," a clumsy "oil vat," the "oil channel" underneath the "oil vat," and "oil baskets" for receiving the oil, etc. A special feature of this house is that there must be a thick wooden beam on its roof ridge, to which must be tied an extremely sturdy hemp rope, with a heavy wooden weight of several hundred or even a thousand pounds suspended from the lower end of the rope. As for the purpose of this thing, I will leave it for later. The structure of the "oil vat" is also quite simple: a large tree that several people can embrace is cut off, the middle is hollowed out, planed smooth, and then steel plates are inlaid around it, and countless small holes must be left in the ones inlaid on the bottom surface so that the oil can leak out. On both sides of the "oil vat," wooden boards or iron plates must be inlaid that are a few points higher than the "oil vat" in order to "add wedges" when pressing the oil. In order to squeeze the "oil cake" in the "oil vat," a heavy wooden board or heavy iron plate on top of the "oil vat" is necessary. Also, this kind of "oil vat" is usually nailed together with iron stakes, so it is very strong.

The process of "making oil" is roughly like this: first, we must have "oil cakes." "Oil cakes" have various differences in quality: there are "sesame cakes," "rapeseed cakes," "cottonseed cakes," etc. From these various "oil cakes," we can extract "sesame oil," "rapeseed oil," "cotton oil," and various other kinds of "oil." The composition of "oil cakes" also requires a bit of work. First, the constituent materials of the "oil cake": sesame seeds, rapeseed, cottonseed, etc., must be dried, and then put into a specially made "mill" 丨丨 this "mill" is usually pulled by oxen, and its capacity is quite large, capable of grinding more than ten dan per day 丨丨 to be ground. After grinding, it must be put into a pot and stir-fried until cooked over a fire. After stir-frying, it must be mixed with a considerable amount of water to make it sticky and wet, and finally it must be "stamped into cakes." "Stamping into cakes" is a procedure in which the stir-fried and sticky raw materials mentioned above are placed in molds of a certain size and form, and stamped into "oil cakes" with the feet. The person who "stamps cakes" is a specially trained "oil worker."

After we have the "oil cakes," we should place them neatly in the "oil vat," arranged so well that there is not a single gap left in the "oil vat." It is also necessary for them to be placed flat. After placing them flat, we use that heavy wooden board (or iron plate) to press on top of them, adding "wedges." The "oil cake" is subjected to pressure, and the "oil" naturally flows out from the small holes at the bottom into the "oil channel." If not much oil comes out, and it is necessary to add more "wedges," then the "wedges" that are pointed at one end and clumsy at the other (i.e., the "inclined plane" in physics) must be driven in. These "wedges" are usually not very small, and the method of driving them in is extremely special. Didn't I say above that a thick and heavy wooden beam must be suspended from the rough and heavy roof beam of the "oil mill" with hemp ropes? This is necessary for driving in the wedges. The method is that there is a person in front who holds the heavy wood like a helmsman on a ship, aiming it at the "wedge" to be driven in. Behind them, there are four or five or six or seven people, each holding one side of the heavy wood, using all their strength to hit the wooden wedge. Like this, hitting it again and again, with increased pressure, the oil in the "vat" flows out again and again. If the oil flows out less again, add more wedges again and hit it again, and so on, until all the oil has been squeezed out.

The "oil channel" that receives the oil is constructed with a special inclination, for the sake of facilitating the "downward flow" of the oil. The end of the "oil channel" is tightly connected to an "oil basket," and the oil drips into the basket in an endless stream. When the basket is full of oil, take it away and replace it with another empty one to receive the oil. The full ones can be taken to the market to sell, or to exchange for some necessary things. Farmers who make oil mostly have dealings with oil, salt, and sundries stores in market towns.

Since "making oil" is a "sideline occupation for farmers," this work is naturally inevitably suspended temporarily during the busy farming season. Usually during the rice transplanting and grass cutting in the third, fourth, and fifth months of the lunar calendar, and during the harvest in the seventh and eighth months, farmers mostly have no time to make oil. From drying the "oil seeds," grinding them, stir-frying them until cooked, "stamping cakes," all the way to "squeezing oil," it takes up quite a lot of the farmers' time from beginning to end. Just from "stamping cakes" to "squeezing oil," it takes them about three days of work. Therefore, the best time for making oil is the several idle months of the tenth, eleventh, twelfth, first, and second months of the lunar calendar. Now it is the twelfth month of the lunar calendar, no wonder that in the rural areas here, the noise in the "oil mills" is resounding in many places.

Speaking of this kind of noise, I'm afraid anyone who hears it will feel impatient. The sound of heavy wood hitting the wedges, the sound of the oil workers "heaving ho," combined together, form a noisy symphony. What is most annoying is that it is not only like this during the day, but also at night. If you live near an "oil mill," you don't want to get a good night's sleep. Originally, making oil requires quite a few people. Naturally, the manpower of one farm family is not enough, and it is necessary to "exchange labor" with other families. "Night labor" is of course even more sought after. Like this, working day and night in shifts, it is not difficult to imagine the hard work of the farmers.

In addition to the farmers themselves and "exchanging labor," hired "long-term workers" and a kind of specially trained "oil workers" are also often involved in this work. The duty of "long-term workers" is to cultivate the land, but making oil is an extra job for them. They make oil for the landlord, but do not get any reward. In terms of annual salary, their total annual income is only more than thirty yuan. These people can be considered the most miserable. The "oil workers" who are experts in "stamping cakes" are mostly hired temporarily. In addition to supplying food, they can still get about two jiao of silver dollars per day.

Some farmers do not have their own oil mills and want to ask people to make oil for them, so there is also a kind of so-called "inviting labor." Inviting the people in the oil mill to make oil for you, you only need to pay one to one and a half yuan of labor costs for each dan of oil seeds. Usually, making oil cannot be less than two dan, seven dou, and five sheng of oil seeds, so you must pay about three or four yuan of labor costs for making oil once.

Finally, there is one more strange thing that must be mentioned, that is, the purpose of farmers making oil is not to get "oil," but to get "fertilizer." The "rapeseed cake," "cottonseed cake," and "sesame cake" after the oil has been squeezed out are the main goals of their hard work. This is truly their life that determines their likes and needs. Farmers rely on fertilizer to eat. It is not a big problem if they don't have "oil" to eat. And this point just illustrates the low standard of living of the general farmers.
